Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
12 min
Conditions of Hajj Obligation in the Hanafi School
Definition and conditions for Hajj obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the eight conditions for Hajj obligation and explain why the Hanafi school considers the obligation immediate (fawr).

Core Idea
Hajj is fard immediately once conditions are met; delaying it is sinful.

Hajj is one of the five pillars, but its obligation depends on specific conditions defined by the Hanafi school. This lesson from Nur al-Idah clarifies the definition of Hajj, lists the eight conditions of obligation, and settles the question of whether the obligation is immediate or can be delayed.

Guided Path
1
Define Hajj and its ruling
Identify the act: visiting the Ka'bah and Arafah with specific actions (ihram, tawaf, wuquf) during specified months. State the ruling: fard 'ayn once in a lifetime.
The definition sets the scope; the ruling is from Quran 3:97.
2
List the eight conditions of obligation
Recall the eight conditions: Islam, sanity, puberty, freedom, time (Hajj season), ability (physical health), ability (provisions), and ability (mount). The text mentions 'provisions and mount' as one condition but includes them as part of overall ability.
The matn says 'eight conditions' but lists only seven items; the eighth is often considered 'physical ability' (health) or 'safety of route'.
3
Analyze the fawr vs tarakhi debate
Understand the dispute: is the obligation immediate (fawr) or permissive (tarakhi)? The relied-upon view is fawr. Delaying without excuse is sinful, but if performed later, it is ada' not qada'.
The text states 'على الفور في الأصح' indicating the most correct view.
4
Examine the condition of Islam
A disbeliever is not obligated. If a disbeliever possesses ability and then converts after losing wealth, no Hajj is due. But if a Muslim had ability and later became poor, the obligation remains as a debt.
This is based on the principle that Islam is a condition for obligation, not for validity.
5
Understand the ability condition
Ability (qudra) is relative to one's usual standard of living. A person accustomed to meat is not considered capable if only bread and cheese are available. The provision must suffice for the journey and for dependents.
The text says 'يفيد أنه يعتبر في حق كل إنسان ما يصح به بدنه'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج
٢٤١
فرضية الحج وشرائطه
كتاب الحج
هو زيارة بقاع مخصوصة بفعل مخصوص في أشهره وهي شوال وذو القعدة وعشر أراد بها الكعبة وعرفة
ذي الحجة فرض مرة على الفور في الأصح ، وشروط فرضيته ثمانية على الأصح:
الإسلام، والعقل والبلوغ والحرية والوقت والقدرة على الزاد ولو بمكة بنفقة وسط.
وصلية
الحج: اعلم أنه ينبغي لمريد الحج والغزو أن يستأذن أبويه، فإن خرج بدون إذن مع الاحتياج إليه للخدمة أثم، وقيل: يكره والأجداد والجدات كالأبوين عند فقدهما. وللأب . منعه إذا كان صبيح الوجه حتى يلتحي وإن استغنى عن خدمته، كذا يستفاد من "النوازل". وفي "الفتاوى": الغلام إذا كان صبيح الوجه لا يخرجه الأب من بيته وإن كان بالغا، كما لا يخرج بنته؛ لأن البنت يشتهيها الرجال فقط، والأمرد إن كان صبيح الوجه يشتهيه الرجال والنساء معا، فالفتنة فيه من الجانبين. وينبغي أن يستأذن رب الدين والكفيل ويستخير في هل يشتري أو يكتري، وهل يسافر برا أو بحرا، وهل يرافق فلانا أو فلانا؛ لأن الاستخارة في الواجب والمكروه والحرام لا محل لها، ويبدأ من التوبة مراعيا شروطها من رد المظالم إلى أهلها عند الإمكان، وقضاء ما قصر فيه من العبادات، والندم على
تفريطه والعزم على أن لا يعود، والاستحلال من ذوي الخصومات والمعاملات [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٢٦] بفعل مخصوص بأن يكون محرما بنية الحج سابقا وطائفا في زمن من ابتداء طلوع فجر النحر، ويمتد إلى آخر العمر واقفا في زمن من زوال يوم عرفة إلى طلوع فجر النحر. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۷۲۷] في أشهره إلخ: فائدة التوقيت بها أنه لو فعل شيئا من أفعال الحج خارجها لا يجزئه، وأنه يكره الإحرام قبلها وإن أمن على نفسه من المحظور لشبهه بالركن، وإطلاقها يفيد التحريم [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٢٧] على الفور: اعلم أن وقت الحج في اصطلاح الأصوليين يسمى مشكلا؛ لأن فيه جهة المعيارية والظرفية، فمن قال بالفور، لا يقول بأن من أخره عن العام الأول يكون فعله قضاء ومن قال بالتراخي، لا يقول بأن من أخره لا يأثم أصلا كما إذا أخر الصلاة عن الوقت الأول، بل جهة المعيارية راجحة عند القائل بالفور، حتى أن من أخر يفسق وتردّ شهادته، لكن إذا حج بالأخرة كان أداء لا قضاء وجهة الظرفية راجحة عند القائل بخلافه، حتى إذا أداه بعد العام الأول لا يأثم بالتأخير، لكن لو مات و لم يحج أثم عنده أيضا. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٢٧] الإسلام فلا يجب على الكافر حتى لو ملك ما به الاستطاعة ثم أسلم بعد ما افتقر لا يجب عليه شيء بتلك الاستطاعة، بخلاف ما لو ملكه مسلما فلم يحج حتى افتقر حيث يتقرر وجوبه دينا في ذمته. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٢٧] والقدرة على الزاد وأطلق في الزاد فأفاد أنه يعتبر في حق كل إنسان ما يصح به بدنه، والناس متفاوتون في ذلك.
[البحر الرائق: ٤٨٨/٢] فالمعتاد للحم ونحوه إذا قدر على خبز وجبن لا يعد قادرا. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٢٧]
Book of Hajj. 241. The Obligation of Hajj and Its Conditions. Book of Hajj: It is visiting specific places with specific actions in its months, which are Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the ten of Dhu al-Hijjah. He meant by them the Ka'bah and Arafah. It is fard once, immediately (ala al-fawr) according to the most correct view. And the conditions of its obligation are eight according to the most correct: Islam, sanity, puberty, freedom, time, and ability regarding provisions and mount, even if in Makkah, with moderate expenses. And an additional condition (from the matn?): It is recommended for the one intending Hajj or military expedition to seek permission from his parents. If he goes out without permission while they need his service, he sins; it is said it is disliked. And grandparents are like parents when they are absent. The father may prevent him if he is handsome-faced until he grows a beard, even if he is not needed for service. Thus it is understood from al-Nawazil. In al-Fatawa: The youth, if he is handsome-faced, the father should not let him out of his house even if he is an adult, just as he does not let out his daughter, because the girl is desired only by men, while the beardless youth, if handsome, is desired by both men and women, so the temptation is from both sides. And he should seek permission from the creditor and the guarantor, and perform istikharah regarding whether to buy or rent, whether to travel by land or sea, and whether to accompany so-and-so or so-and-so, because istikharah has no place in what is obligatory, disliked, or forbidden. And he should begin with repentance, observing its conditions: returning wrongs to their owners when possible, making up for what he neglected of worship, regretting his negligence, resolving not to return, and seeking absolution from those he has disputes and dealings with. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 726] With specific actions: by being in ihram with the intention of Hajj before, and performing tawaf in a period starting from the dawn of the day of sacrifice (Yawm al-Nahr) and extending to the end of one's life, and standing (wuquf) in a period from the decline of the sun on the day of Arafah to the dawn of the day of sacrifice. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 727] In its months etc.: The benefit of specifying them is that if one does any of the actions of Hajj outside them, it does not suffice, and it is disliked to enter ihram before them even if one feels safe from prohibitions because it resembles a pillar. And the absolute meaning indicates prohibition. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 727] On immediacy (fawr): Know that the time of Hajj according to the terminology of the usuliyyun is called problematic (mushkil), because it includes aspects of being criterion (mi'yariyya) and container (zarfiyya). One who says it is immediate does not say that if one delays it past the first year, his action becomes qada', and one who says it is permissive does not say that if one delays, he does not sin at all, as if he delayed prayer beyond the first time. Rather, the aspect of criterion is predominant for the proponent of immediacy, such that the one who delays becomes a sinner and his testimony is rejected. But if he performs Hajj later, it is ada', not qada'. The aspect of container is predominant for the opposite view, such that if he performs it after the first year, he does not sin for the delay, but if he dies without having performed Hajj, he sins in that view as well. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 727] Islam: It is not obligatory on the disbeliever. Even if he owns the means of ability and then embraces Islam after becoming poor, nothing is required of him due to that ability. Contrast: If he owned it as a Muslim and did not perform Hajj until he became poor, its obligation is established as a debt in his liability. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 727] Ability regarding provisions: He gave it absolutely, indicating that for every person what is considered is what suffices his body, and people differ in that. [Bahr al-Raiq: 488/2] One accustomed to meat and the like, if he can only afford bread and cheese, is not considered capable. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 727]
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage begins the Book of Hajj (Kitab al-Hajj) in Nur al-Idah. It defines Hajj as the visitation of specific places (the Ka'bah and Arafah) with specific actions during its months: Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah. The passage states that Hajj is fard (obligatory) once in a lifetime, and the obligation is immediate (ala al-fawr) according to the most correct view. It lists eight conditions for obligation: Islam, sanity, puberty, freedom, time (i.e., the Hajj season), and ability (capacity) regarding provisions and mount (riding animal), even if one is already in Makkah, with moderate expenses. The commentary then elaborates on several points. It discusses the etiquette of seeking permission from parents for Hajj (and jihad), especially if the child is needed for service. The father may prevent a handsome-faced youth from leaving due to fear of temptation. It also mentions seeking permission from creditors and guarantors, and performing istikharah for practical decisions. The importance of repentance before Hajj is emphasized. There is a detailed discussion on the definition of specific actions: ihram with intention, tawaf starting from dawn of the day of sacrifice, and wuquf at Arafah from noon to dawn. The commentary then delves into the dispute over whether the obligation is immediate (fawr) or permissive (tarakhi). The relied-upon view is that it is immediate; delaying it is sinful, though the Hajj itself performed later is considered ada' (performance in time) not qada' (makeup). Finally, the condition of Islam is clarified: a disbeliever is not obligated, and if one gains ability while a disbeliever then converts when poor, no Hajj is due. But if a Muslim had ability and then became poor, it remains a debt. For provisions, it is based on what suffices each person according to their habitual standard; a person accustomed to meat is not considered capable if only bread and cheese are available.

Key Terms
الحج (al-Hajj): Visiting specific places (Ka'bah, Arafah) with specific actions (ihram, tawaf, wuquf, etc.) in specific months.
على الفور (ala al-fawr): Immediate obligation; one must perform Hajj as soon as conditions are met, not necessarily in the first year but without unnecessary delay.
القدرة (al-qudra): Ability (istita'ah) regarding provisions and mount, judged according to the person's usual standard of living.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on a person who has the ability to perform Hajj but delays it for many years?
A) He commits no sin because Hajj is obligatory only once in a lifetime.
B) He is sinful because the obligation is immediate, and his testimony may be rejected.
C) He must perform Hajj as a make-up (qada') if he does it later.
D) The obligation is waived after the first year.

Key Takeaway
Hajj is fard 'ayn immediately upon fulfilling the eight conditions; delaying without excuse is sinful.

Seeking Parents' Permission for Hajj
Lists recommended actions before Hajj: permission from parents, istikharah, tawbah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on seeking parents' permission before Hajj and identify when it becomes obligatory.

Core Idea
Parents' consent is recommended for Hajj, but becomes mandatory if they need your service.

Before setting out for Hajj, a Muslim should consider the rights of his parents. This passage clarifies that seeking their permission is generally recommended, but if they are in need of his care, leaving without permission becomes sinful. It also addresses the unique case of a beardless youth, where the father may prevent him even if not needed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
State that seeking permission from parents is recommended (sunnah) before Hajj or jihad.
2
Recognize the exception
If parents need the child's service, leaving without permission becomes sinful (wajib level).
The word 'أثم' indicates sinfulness.
3
Understand the grandparents' status
Grandparents take the same ruling as parents in their absence.
4
Analyze the beardless youth case
The father may prevent a beardless son (even adult) from going out due to risk of fitnah, and the same applies to daughters.
The risk is higher for beardless youths as they attract both men and women.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصلية الحج: اعلم أنه ينبغي لمريد الحج والغزو أن يستأذن أبويه، فإن خرج بدون إذن مع الاحتياج إليه للخدمة أثم، وقيل: يكره والأجداد والجدات كالأبوين عند فقدهما. وللأب . منعه إذا كان صبيح الوجه حتى يلتحي وإن استغنى عن خدمته، كذا يستفاد من "النوازل". وفي "الفتاوى": الغلام إذا كان صبيح الوجه لا يخرجه الأب من بيته وإن كان بالغا، كما لا يخرج بنته؛ لأن البنت يشتهيها الرجال فقط، والأمرد إن كان صبيح الوجه يشتهيه الرجال والنساء معا، فالفتنة فيه من الجانبين. وينبغي أن يستأذن رب الدين والكفيل ويستخير في هل يشتري أو يكتري، وهل يسافر برا أو بحرا، وهل يرافق فلانا أو فلانا؛ لأن الاستخارة في الواجب والمكروه والحرام لا محل لها، ويبدأ من التوبة مراعيا شروطها من رد المظالم إلى أهلها عند الإمكان، وقضاء ما قصر فيه من العبادات، والندم على تفريطه والعزم على أن لا يعود، والاستحلال من ذوي الخصومات والمعاملات
Etiquette of Hajj: Know that the one intending Hajj or military expedition should seek permission from his parents. If he goes out without permission while he is needed for service, he sins. And it is said: it is disliked. And grandparents are like parents when they are absent. The father may prevent him if he is beardless until he grows a beard, even if he is not needed for service. ... He should seek permission from the creditor and guarantor, and seek guidance (istikharah) regarding whether to buy or rent, travel by land or sea, which companion to take, because istikharah has no place in obligatory, disliked, or prohibited actions. He begins with repentance...
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage covers the recommended actions before setting out for Hajj. The first is seeking permission from parents; if the parents need his service, leaving without permission is sinful. It also discusses the ruling for a beardless youth: the father may prevent him due to fear of fitnah, even if he is an adult. The same applies to daughters. Next, the pilgrim should seek permission from creditors and guarantors, and perform istikharah for decisions like travel route and companions. Istikharah is only for mubah (permissible) actions, not for obligatory or prohibited ones. Finally, repentance is prescribed, with conditions including returning wrongfully taken property, making up missed religious obligations, regret, and resolve not to return to sin.

Key Terms
الاستئذان (al-isti'dhan): Seeking permission from parents before embarking on Hajj or jihad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does seeking parents' permission for Hajj become sinful to omit?
A) Always, because it is fard
B) Only if the parents need the child's service
C) Only if the child is beardless
D) Never, it is merely recommended

Key Takeaway
Parents' permission for Hajj is sunnah but becomes wajib and sinful to omit when they need you.

Istikharah and Permission from Creditor for Hajj
Lists recommended actions before Hajj: seek permission from creditors, istikharah for decisions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain when istikharah is prescribed and apply the condition that it is only for permissible (mubah) actions.

Core Idea
Istikharah is only for mubah actions, not for wajib, makruh, or haram.

Before Hajj, a pilgrim should also seek permission from creditors and guarantors, and perform istikharah for decisions like travel route or companions. The passage makes clear that istikharah is only for permissible matters; it has no place in obligatory, disliked, or prohibited actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the additional permissions
The pilgrim should also seek permission from creditors (rab al-dayn) and guarantors (kafeel) before traveling.
This ensures rights are not violated.
2
Understand the scope of istikharah
Istikharah is to seek guidance from Allah when deciding between permissible options (mubah).
3
List examples from the text
Examples: whether to buy or rent, travel by land or sea, which friend to accompany.
4
Recognize the limitation
Istikharah is not prescribed for wajib (obligatory), makruh (disliked), or haram (prohibited) actions, because the decision is already clear.
Literal: 'la mahalla laha' - no place for it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصلية الحج: اعلم أنه ينبغي لمريد الحج والغزو أن يستأذن أبويه، فإن خرج بدون إذن مع الاحتياج إليه للخدمة أثم، وقيل: يكره والأجداد والجدات كالأبوين عند فقدهما. وللأب . منعه إذا كان صبيح الوجه حتى يلتحي وإن استغنى عن خدمته، كذا يستفاد من "النوازل". وفي "الفتاوى": الغلام إذا كان صبيح الوجه لا يخرجه الأب من بيته وإن كان بالغا، كما لا يخرج بنته؛ لأن البنت يشتهيها الرجال فقط، والأمرد إن كان صبيح الوجه يشتهيه الرجال والنساء معا، فالفتنة فيه من الجانبين. وينبغي أن يستأذن رب الدين والكفيل ويستخير في هل يشتري أو يكتري، وهل يسافر برا أو بحرا، وهل يرافق فلانا أو فلانا؛ لأن الاستخارة في الواجب والمكروه والحرام لا محل لها، ويبدأ من التوبة مراعيا شروطها من رد المظالم إلى أهلها عند الإمكان، وقضاء ما قصر فيه من العبادات، والندم على تفريطه والعزم على أن لا يعود، والاستحلال من ذوي الخصومات والمعاملات
Etiquette of Hajj: Know that the one intending Hajj or military expedition should seek permission from his parents. If he goes out without permission while he is needed for service, he sins. And it is said: it is disliked. And grandparents are like parents when they are absent. The father may prevent him if he is beardless until he grows a beard, even if he is not needed for service. ... He should seek permission from the creditor and guarantor, and seek guidance (istikharah) regarding whether to buy or rent, travel by land or sea, which companion to take, because istikharah has no place in obligatory, disliked, or prohibited actions. He begins with repentance...

Commentary
This passage covers the recommended actions before setting out for Hajj. The first is seeking permission from parents; if the parents need his service, leaving without permission is sinful. It also discusses the ruling for a beardless youth: the father may prevent him due to fear of fitnah, even if he is an adult. The same applies to daughters. Next, the pilgrim should seek permission from creditors and guarantors, and perform istikharah for decisions like travel route and companions. Istikharah is only for mubah (permissible) actions, not for obligatory or prohibited ones. Finally, repentance is prescribed, with conditions including returning wrongfully taken property, making up missed religious obligations, regret, and resolve not to return to sin.

Key Terms
الاستخارة (al-istikharah): Seeking divine guidance through prayer and supplication when choosing between permissible options.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a valid situation for istikharah according to the text?
A) Deciding whether to perform Hajj (fard) this year or next
B) Deciding whether to buy or rent a house for Hajj travel
C) Deciding whether to skip a fast in Ramadan
D) Deciding whether to lie to avoid harm

Key Takeaway
Perform istikharah only for permissible matters; for obligatory or prohibited acts, the ruling is already clear.

Conditions of Repentance before Hajj
Lists recommended actions before Hajj: conditions of repentance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four conditions of repentance (tawbah) as outlined in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
True repentance requires returning wrongs, making up missed acts, regret, and resolve—not just words.

Before embarking on the sacred journey of Hajj, a pilgrim must cleanse their soul through sincere repentance. This passage details the necessary conditions: restitution of wrongfully taken property, completing missed religious obligations, genuine regret, and firm resolve not to return to sin, along with seeking forgiveness from those wronged.

Guided Path
1
State the first condition: return of wrongs
Restitute (رد المظالم) any property taken unjustly back to its owners if possible.
Material restitution is essential.
2
State the second condition: make up missed acts
Complete any missed religious duties (qada) such as missed prayers or fasts.
Spiritual debts must be cleared.
3
State the third condition: regret
Feel genuine remorse (الندم) for the sins committed.
Regret is the core of repentance.
4
State the fourth condition: resolve
Have a firm intention (العزم) not to return to the sin.
Future abstinence is required.
5
Note the additional element: seeking forgiveness from those wronged
Also seek halal (forgiveness) from people involved in disputes or transactions (الاستحلال من ذوي الخصومات والمعاملات).
This complements the return of property.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصلية الحج: اعلم أنه ينبغي لمريد الحج والغزو أن يستأذن أبويه، فإن خرج بدون إذن مع الاحتياج إليه للخدمة أثم، وقيل: يكره والأجداد والجدات كالأبوين عند فقدهما. وللأب . منعه إذا كان صبيح الوجه حتى يلتحي وإن استغنى عن خدمته، كذا يستفاد من "النوازل". وفي "الفتاوى": الغلام إذا كان صبيح الوجه لا يخرجه الأب من بيته وإن كان بالغا، كما لا يخرج بنته؛ لأن البنت يشتهيها الرجال فقط، والأمرد إن كان صبيح الوجه يشتهيه الرجال والنساء معا، فالفتنة فيه من الجانبين. وينبغي أن يستأذن رب الدين والكفيل ويستخير في هل يشتري أو يكتري، وهل يسافر برا أو بحرا، وهل يرافق فلانا أو فلانا؛ لأن الاستخارة في الواجب والمكروه والحرام لا محل لها، ويبدأ من التوبة مراعيا شروطها من رد المظالم إلى أهلها عند الإمكان، وقضاء ما قصر فيه من العبادات، والندم على تفريطه والعزم على أن لا يعود، والاستحلال من ذوي الخصومات والمعاملات
Etiquette of Hajj: Know that the one intending Hajj or military expedition should seek permission from his parents. If he goes out without permission while he is needed for service, he sins. And it is said: it is disliked. And grandparents are like parents when they are absent. The father may prevent him if he is beardless until he grows a beard, even if he is not needed for service. ... He should seek permission from the creditor and guarantor, and seek guidance (istikharah) regarding whether to buy or rent, travel by land or sea, which companion to take, because istikharah has no place in obligatory, disliked, or prohibited actions. He begins with repentance...
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage covers the recommended actions before setting out for Hajj. The first is seeking permission from parents; if the parents need his service, leaving without permission is sinful. It also discusses the ruling for a beardless youth: the father may prevent him due to fear of fitnah, even if he is an adult. The same applies to daughters. Next, the pilgrim should seek permission from creditors and guarantors, and perform istikharah for decisions like travel route and companions. Istikharah is only for mubah (permissible) actions, not for obligatory or prohibited ones. Finally, repentance is prescribed, with conditions including returning wrongfully taken property, making up missed religious obligations, regret, and resolve not to return to sin.

Key Terms
التوبة (al-tawbah): Repentance with conditions: returning wrongs, making up missed acts, regret, and resolve.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Regret
B) Resolve
C) Returning wrongfully taken property
D) Making up missed prayers

Key Takeaway
Sincere repentance requires action—restoring rights, completing duties, regret, and resolve.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
8 min
Definition of Hajj and Conditions of Obligation
Defines Hajj, states fard obligation, lists eight conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of Hajj, identify its fard 'ayn obligation on the preferred view of fawr, and list the eight conditions that must be met for it to be obligatory.

Core Idea
Hajj is fard 'ayn once, immediately upon ability, with eight conditions.

This lesson opens the Book of Hajj by defining the pilgrimage and establishing its obligation. The author presents the Hanafi view that Hajj is fard 'ayn to be performed on the preferred view of fawr (immediacy). Eight conditions must be fulfilled for the obligation to become binding. The margin notes from al-Tahtawi provide detailed elaboration on each condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Read the definition: Hajj is visiting specific places (Ka'bah and Arafat) with specific actions (ihram, tawaf, wuquf) during specific months (Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, first ten of Dhu al-Hijjah).
2
State the ruling
Note that Hajj is fard 'ayn once in a lifetime, and the preferred view is fawr (immediately upon ability), not tarakhi (delay permissible).
Imam Shafi'i holds tarakhi; the Hanafi school adopts fawr.
3
List the eight conditions
Memorize the eight conditions: Islam, sanity, puberty, freedom, time (the months), ability for provisions (zad) and conveyance (rahilah for non-Makkans), and knowledge of obligation for converts in dar al-harb.
These are conditions for the obligation, not validity.
4
Understand 'ability' in detail
Ability includes sufficient provisions (zad) that meets one's personal standard of living, and a riding beast (rahilah) owned or hired, not borrowed. Surplus must be beyond family needs and debts.
The margin notes emphasize that ability is relative to one's social status.

[حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٢٦] بفعل مخصوص بأن يكون محرما بنية الحج سابقا وطائفا في زمن من ابتداء طلوع فجر النحر، ويمتد إلى آخر العمر واقفا في زمن من زوال يوم عرفة إلى طلوع فجر النحر. Book of Hajj. Fardiyyah of Hajj and its conditions. Book of Hajj: It is visiting specific places with specific actions in its months, which are Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and ten of Dhu al-Hijjah meaning the Ka'bah and Arafat. Obligatory once on the preferred view of immediacy. And conditions of its obligation are eight on the preferred view: Islam, sanity, puberty, freedom, time, and ability for provisions even if in Makkah with moderate expenses. [Margin: ...]
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage states the definition of Hajj and its obligation. The text defines Hajj lexically as visiting specific places (the Ka'bah and Arafat) with specific actions (wuquf and tawaf) during its fixed months. It is obligatory once in a lifetime on the preferred view of fawr (immediacy). The eight conditions of obligation are: Islam (so not binding on non-Muslim), sanity, puberty, freedom, time (the months of Hajj), ability for provisions (sufficient for him and his family), ability for conveyance (for those far from Makkah), and knowledge of its obligation for those who convert in dar al-harb. The hashiah elaborates on the definition, the timing, the concept of fawr, and details of ability.

Key Terms
الحج (al-Hajj): Visiting the Ka'bah and Arafat with specific actions in specific months.
الفور (al-fawr): Immediacy: the obligation must be performed as soon as possible, not delayed.
الاستطاعة (al-istita'ah): Ability to perform Hajj, including provisions (zad) and conveyance (rahilah).
الراحلة (al-rahilah): A riding beast, specifically a camel suitable for travel.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate

Conditions for Hajj Being Obligatory
Conditions for Hajj obligation and performance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two categories of conditions for Hajj (obligation vs performance) and apply the Hanafi rules regarding ability (istita'ah) including transport and surplus over essential needs.

Core Idea
Hajj is obligatory only when ability includes surplus wealth and transport — mere wealth is insufficient.

This passage from Nur al-Idah presents the Hanafi conditions that trigger the obligation of Hajj and the conditions required for performing it. Understanding these conditions is crucial for determining when Hajj becomes fard 'ayn on a Muslim. The passage distinguishes between shurut wujub (conditions of obligation) and shurut ada (conditions of performance), a key Hanafi distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sets of conditions
The text first lists conditions for the initial obligation (shurut fardiyyah): ability (istita'ah) through transport and surplus wealth, knowledge of the obligation for new Muslims, and residence in dar al-Islam. Then it lists five conditions for the obligation of performance (shurut wujub al-ada): health, no physical barrier, safe road, no iddah, and mahram for women.
The Hanafi distinction between 'wujub' and 'ada' is unique and affects when Hajj becomes incumbent.
2
Analyze the condition of ability (istita'ah)
Ability must include a specific mount (raahila) or share in a howdah, acquired by ownership or lease, not by permission or borrowing. This ability must be surplus over one's own expenses and dependents' expenses until return, and over essential items like housing, furnishings, tools, and debt.
The text stresses that the surplus is a condition; having wealth tied up in assets is not sufficient unless liquid.
3
Understand the transport requirement
For those who cannot walk without hardship, a mount (raahila) is required. The text defines raahila as a riding camel. If one cannot afford a full mount, a share in a howdah suffices. The ability must cover the entire journey; hiring only for part does not obligate.
There is a madhhab dispute about sea travel: some say it prevents obligation unless the predominant expectation is safety.
4
Apply the conditions to a scenario
Using the conditions, determine if a given person's situation makes Hajj obligatory. Check if they have surplus wealth after essential needs, a suitable transport, physical ability, safe route, and for women, a mahram and no iddah.
The mahram and iddah are conditions for performance, not obligation, so if they are missing, Hajj is still fard but deferred.

عموم
العدة
Conditions of Hajj being obligatory: And ability upon a mount specific to it, or upon one side of a howdah by ownership or hiring, not by permission or borrowing, for other than the people of Makkah and those around them if they can walk on foot and with strength without hardship, otherwise they must have the mount absolutely. And that ability must be surplus over his own expenses and the expenses of his dependents until his return, and over what is indispensable, such as the house, its furnishings, tools of craftsmen, and repayment of debt. And knowledge of the obligation of Hajj is a condition for one who accepts Islam in dar al-harb or who resides in dar al-Islam. And the conditions for the obligation of performance are five according to the correct view: health of body, removal of sensory obstacle to going for Hajj, safety of road, not being in a period of 'iddah, and accompaniment of a mahram.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah discusses the conditions that trigger the obligation of Hajj. The author first explains that one must have the means of transport, either a mount or a share in a howdah, acquired through ownership or lease, not through mere permission or borrowing. This applies to those who cannot walk easily. The ability must be in excess of essential needs like food for oneself and dependents, housing, and debt repayment. Then it mentions the condition of knowing the obligation for new Muslims or those in dar al-harb. Finally, it lists the five conditions for performing the Hajj once it is obligatory: physical health, safe road, not being in iddah, and availability of a mahram for women. The text elaborates on the meaning of mount (raahila) and dependents (ayal), and clarifies that one is not obliged to sell surplus property to fund Hajj, though it is commendable.

Key Terms
راحلة (rāhilah): A mount from camels, male or female, used as the standard means of transport for Hajj.
عيال (iyāl): Dependents whose maintenance is obligatory on the person, such as wife and children.
شق محمل (shiqq miḥmal): One side of a howdah, a share in a transport vehicle.
شرائط وجوب الأداء (sharā'iṭ wujūb al-adā'): Conditions for the obligation of performance, i.e., conditions at the time of performing Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT a condition for the obligation of Hajj (shurut fardiyyah)?
A) Health of the body
B) Ability to mount a rahila or share a howdah
C) Having surplus wealth after essential expenses
D) Having a mahram for women

Key Takeaway
Hajj is obligatory only when a person has the ability (istita'ah) that includes surplus wealth, proper transport, and meets five performance conditions; without these, the obligation is not triggered.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

The Mahram Requirement for Women's Hajj: Conditions and Rulings
Explains the mahram requirement: definition, qualities, distance, and husband's permission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid mahram, identify which individuals qualify according to the Hanafi school, and apply the ruling that a trustworthy dhimmi can serve as a mahram.

Core Idea
A woman must have a trustworthy mahram for Hajj journeys ≥ 3 days; a dhimmi father suffices.

This passage from Nur al-Idah explains that a mahram is essential for a woman's obligation to perform Hajj. The text clarifies the mahram's qualities: permanently prohibited in marriage, Muslim (or non-Magian dhimmi), trustworthy, sane, and adult. It also addresses the distance threshold and the permissibility of traveling without a mahram for shorter trips. The relied-upon Hanafi view accepts a dhimmi as mahram, prioritizing protection over religious alignment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core condition
The condition is that a woman must have a mahram for her journey to perform Hajj. The mahram is defined as someone she cannot marry permanently due to blood, fosterage, or affinity.
2
List the mahram's required qualities
The mahram must be trustworthy, sane, adult, and either Muslim or a dhimmi. Excluded are Magians who allow marriage to the woman, untrustworthy relatives, minors, and the insane.
The text prefers saying 'non-Magian' over 'Muslim' because a dhimmi suffices.
3
Determine the travel distance
The mahram is required for a journey of three days or more. For shorter distances, a woman may travel without a mahram for a genuine need.
The three-day measure is based on classical travel; modern speed does not change the condition.
4
Apply the ruling on husband's permission
For obligatory Hajj (Hajj al-Islam), the husband's consent is not required if she has a mahram. For voluntary or vowed Hajj, his permission is needed.
The husband's right does not override a religious obligation.
5
Evaluate the ikhtilaf on dhimmi mahram
The Shafi'i school requires the mahram to be Muslim, whereas the Hanafi relied-upon view allows a trustworthy dhimmi. The basis is the purpose of protection, not religious status.
This difference impacts many converts or women with non-Muslim relatives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شروط وجوب أداء الحج
وصلية
وخروج محرم ولو من رضاع أو مصاهرة، مسلم مأمون عاقل بالغ، أو زوج لامرأة في سفر، والعبرة بغلبة السلامة برّا وبحرا على المفتى ،به
وخروج محرم إلخ هو من لا يجوز له مناكحتها على التأبيد بقرابة أو رضاع أو مصاهرة، أطلقه فشمل الحر والعبد. مسلم : الأولى أن يقول: غير مجوسي كما في "التنوير"؛ لما مر أنه يكفي الذمي. (حاشية الطحطاوي بتصرف) مأمون إلخ وخرج به المجوسي الذي يعتقد إباحة نكاحها، والمسلم القريب إذا لم يكن مأمونا، والصبي الذي لم يحتلم والمجنون؛ لأن المقصود من المحرم الحفظ والصيانة لها، وهو مفقود في هؤلاء الأربعة. [البحر الرائق: ٤٩١/٢] لامرأة أطلق المرأة فشمل الشابة والعجوز؛ لإطلاق النصوص والمرأة هي البالغة؛ لأن الكلام فيمن يجب عليه الحج، فلذا قالوا في الصبية التي لم تبلغ حد الشهوة تسافر بلا محرم؛ فإن بلغتها لا تسافر إلا به البحر الرائق بتصرف: ٤٩١/٢] في سفر قيد بالسفر، وهو ثلاثة أيام بلياليها؛ لأنه يباح لها الخروج إلى ما دون ذلك لحاجة بغير محرم، وأشار بعدم اشتراط رضا الزوج إلى أنه ليس له منعها عن حجة الإسلام إذا وجدت محرما؛ لأن حقه لا يظهر في الفرائض، بخلاف حج التطوع والمنذور. البحر الرائق: ٤٩١/٢]
Conditions for the obligation of performance of Hajj: and? And [the condition of] the exit of a mahram, even from rada' or musahara, Muslim, trustworthy, sane, adult, or a husband for a woman in travel, and the consideration is the predominance of safety by land and sea according to the relied-upon [view]. 'And the exit of a mahram etc.': meaning one who cannot marry her perpetually due to kinship, rada', or musahara; he said it generally includes free and slave. 'Muslim': it is better to say 'non-Magian', as has passed that a dhimmi suffices. 'Trustworthy etc.': excludes the Magian who believes in marrying her, the Muslim relative if not trustworthy, the minor who has not dreamt, and the insane, because the purpose of the mahram is protection and guarding her, which is absent in these four. 'For a woman': he said 'woman' generally, including young and old, due to the generality of texts; and the woman is the adult, because the discussion is about those upon whom Hajj is obligatory; thus they said about a girl who has not reached the age of desire that she may travel without a mahram; if she reaches it, she may not travel except with him. 'In travel': he restricted it to travel, which is three days and nights, because she is permitted to go out for less than that for a need without a mahram, and he indicated that the husband's consent is not required [for Hajj al-Islam] because his right does not appear in obligatory acts, unlike voluntary and vowed Hajj.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of the conditions for performing Hajj, focusing on the requirement of a mahram for women. The mahram must be a person with whom marriage is permanently prohibited, due to blood, rada' (fosterage), or musahara (affinity). He must be Muslim, trustworthy, sane, and adult. The relied-upon view is that a dhimmi (non-Muslim protected subject) can also serve as mahram, though some say it should be a non-Magian. A person who is not trustworthy, such as a Magian who permits marriage with the woman, or a minor, cannot be mahram. Even a Muslim relative who is not trustworthy is excluded. A woman is required to have a mahram for a journey of three days or more; for shorter distances she may go without. For Hajj al-Islam (the obligatory Hajj), the husband's permission is not required if she has a mahram, because his right does not override the obligation of Hajj, unlike voluntary Hajj.

Key Terms
محرم (maḥram): A person permanently forbidden to marry the woman, who can accompany her for protection.
رضاع (raḍā'): Fosterage that creates permanent marriage prohibition.
مصاهرة (muṣāharah): Affinity, marriage relationship creating prohibition.
عاقل بالغ (ʿāqil bāligh): Sane and adult, required for a mahram to be responsible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) A Muslim cousin who is untrustworthy
B) A 13-year-old son
C) A Christian brother who is trustworthy
D) An insane uncle

Key Takeaway
A woman's Hajj obligation requires a mahram who is trustworthy, sane, adult, and either Muslim or a dhimmi; for obligatory Hajj, the husband's permission is not needed.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Pillars and Obligations of Hajj
Defines pillars and obligations of Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two pillars and two obligatory acts of Hajj according to the Hanafi school and identify the consequence of omitting each.

Core Idea
Hajj has two pillars that invalidate it if missed and two wajibat that require a sacrifice if omitted.

Hajj, like other acts of worship, has essential components that define its validity. In the Hanafi school, the pillars (arkan) are the irreducible core; missing them destroys the Hajj. The obligations (wajibat) are necessary but less severe; omitting them can be compensated. This lesson anchors the key terms and their practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the shurut
The passage begins by stating that Hajj requires two conditions: ihram and Islam. These are prerequisites, not pillars.
Shurut must be present before the acts.
2
List the two pillars (arkan)
The first pillar is standing at Arafat (wuquf) for any moment between noon of the 9th and dawn of the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, while in ihram and without prior intercourse. The second pillar is performing the majority (four rounds) of Tawaf al-Ifadah after dawn of the 10th.
The majority is four rounds; the remaining three are wajib.
3
Identify the two wajibat
The two obligatory acts are: (1) entering ihram from the designated miqat, and (2) prolonging the standing at Arafat until sunset.
Omitting a wajib requires a dam (sacrifice) but does not invalidate Hajj.
4
Understand the consequence of omission
If a pillar is omitted, the Hajj is batil (invalid) and must be repeated. If a wajib is omitted, the Hajj is valid but a dam is owed.
This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويصح أداء فرض الحج بأربعة أشياء للحر الإحرام، والإسلام، وهما شرطان ثم الإتيان ،بركنيه، وهما الوقوف محرما بعرفات لحظة من زوال يوم التاسع إلى فجر يوم النحر بشرط عدم الجماع قبله محرما، والركن الثاني هو أكثر طواف الإفاضة في وقته وهو ما بعد طلوع فجر النحر.
وواجبات الحج: إنشاء الإحرام من الميقات ومدُّ الوقوف بعرفات إلى الغروب، الغاية داخلة في المغيا
And the performance of the obligatory Hajj is valid with four things for the free person: ihram and Islam — these are two conditions — then the performance of its two pillars: they are standing at Arafat in the state of ihram for a moment from noon of the 9th to dawn of the 10th, with the condition that there is no sexual intercourse before it while in ihram; and the second pillar is the majority of Tawaf al-Ifadah in its time, which is after the dawn of the 10th. And the obligations of Hajj: initiating ihram from the miqat and extending the standing at Arafat until sunset, the goal is included in the reached thing.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage lists the essential components for a valid obligatory Hajj. According to the Hanafi school, the Hajj of a free person requires ihram and Islam as preconditions (shurut). Then two pillars (arkan): first, standing at Arafat for at least a moment between noon of the 9th of Dhul Hijjah and dawn of the 10th, while in ihram and without prior intercourse. The second pillar is performing at least four cycles (the majority) of Tawaf al-Ifadah (the obligatory circumambulation) after dawn of the 10th. In addition to the pillars, there are obligatory acts (wajibat): entering ihram from the designated miqat (boundary) and prolonging the standing at Arafat until sunset. If one omits a pillar, the Hajj is invalid; if one omits an obligation, it must be compensated by a sacrifice (dam).

Key Terms
ركن (rukn): A pillar of Hajj, omission invalidates the Hajj completely.
واجب (wājib): An obligatory act that does not invalidate Hajj if omitted but requires a dam.
وقوف عرفات (wuqūf ʿArafāt): Standing at Arafat, the key pillar of Hajj.
طواف الإفاضة (ṭawāf al-ifāḍah): The obligatory circumambulation after returning from Mina.
ميقات (mīqāt): Designated boundary for ihram; spatial miqat here.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how much of Tawaf al-Ifadah is considered a pillar (rukn) of Hajj?
A) All seven rounds
B) The first four rounds
C) The last three rounds
D) One round

Key Takeaway
Hajj has two pillars (wuquf at Arafat and majority of Tawaf al-Ifadah) and two wajibat (ihram from miqat and extending wuquf to sunset); missing a pillar invalidates Hajj, missing a wajib requires a dam.

The Two Miqats: Dhu al-Hulayfah and Dhat ‘Irq
Definition of spatial miqats for ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two miqats described in the passage, state their locations, and explain their function for pilgrims from specific regions.

Core Idea
The miqat is the boundary for ihram; Dhu al-Hulayfah and Dhat 'Irq are two of the five, each serving a specific region.

This passage from Nur al-Idah defines the spatial miqat (mīqāt) as the place which the non-Makkan (āfāqī) may not pass except in the state of ihram. While the text mentions there are five, it fully describes only the first two: Dhu al-Hulayfah for the people of Madinah and Dhat 'Irq for those coming from the east (Iraq region). These boundaries ensure that pilgrims do not cross a certain point without having entered ihram, a key requirement for Hajj and Umrah.

Guided Path
1
Define the miqat
Understand that miqat is a spatial boundary (place) for entering ihram, distinct from the temporal miqat (time). The term is general but here refers to the location.
The passage clarifies: 'the miqat is common between the specified time and the specified place, and what is meant here is the latter.'
2
Locate Dhu al-Hulayfah
Identify that this is the miqat for the people of Madinah, located about six miles from Madinah and nine to ten marhalahs from Makkah. It is the farthest miqat and includes wells called 'Abu Ali' wells.
The passage provides distances: 6 or 7 miles from Madinah, 9-10 marhalahs from Makkah.
3
Locate Dhat 'Irq
Identify that this is the miqat for the people of the east (Iraq region), situated between the east and west of Makkah, about two marhalahs from Makkah.
The passage notes it is used by 'all the people of the east' and is two marhalahs from Makkah.
4
Recognize the incomplete list
Acknowledge that the passage begins to list five miqats but only details the first two; the remaining three (al-Juhfah, Qarn al-Manazil, Yalamlam) are known from other texts.
The text cuts off after describing Dhat 'Irq, but the Hanafi school consistently recognizes five miqats.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الميقات: أي المكان الذي لا يتجاوزه الآفاقي إلا محرما خمسة، فالميقات مشترك بين الوقت المعين والمكان المعين، والمراد هنا الثاني. الأول: ذو الحليفة - بضم الحاء المهملة وبالفاء - بينه وبين مكة نحو عشر مراحل أو تسع، وبينه وبين المدينة ستة أميال، وقيل: سبعة، وهو ميقات أهل المدينة وهو أبعد المواقيت وبهذا المكان آبار تسميه العوام: آبار عليه قيل: لأن علي بن أبي طالب قاتل الجن في بعض تلك الآبار، والثاني: ذات عرق بكسر العين وسكون الراء - الجميع أهل المشرق، وهي بين المشرق والمغرب من مكة، -
قيل وبينها وبين مكة مرحلتان.
The miqat: i.e., the place which the non-Makkan may not pass except in ihram; they are five. So al-miqat is common between the specified time and the specified place, and what is meant here is the latter. The first: Dhu al-Hulayfah — with a damma on the ha' and alif and fa' — between it and Makkah is about ten or nine marhalahs, and between it and Madinah is six miles, or seven; it is the miqat of the people of Madinah and it is the farthest of the miqats. In this place there are wells that the common people call 'Abu 'Ali' wells; it is said that 'Ali ibn Abi Talib fought the jinn in some of those wells. The second: Dhat 'Irq — with a kasra on the 'ayn and sukun on the ra' — all the people of the east [use it], and it is between the east and west of Makkah; it is said that between it and Makkah is two marhalahs.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage defines the spatial miqats (boundaries) for entering ihram. The Hanafi school mentions five miqats, but only the first two are described here. Dhu al-Hulayfah is the miqat for those coming from Madinah and the west, located about six miles from Madinah and about nine to ten marhalahs from Makkah. It is the farthest miqat. The common people call its wells 'Abu 'Ali' wells. Dhat 'Irq is the miqat for those coming from the east (Iraq, etc.), located two marhalahs from Makkah. The text cuts off before mentioning the remaining three miqats: al-Juhfah for the people of Sham, Qarn al-Manazil for the people of Najd, and Yalamlam for the people of Yemen.

Key Terms
ميقات (mīqāt): Designated boundary for entering ihram; here spatial miqat.
آفاقي (āfāqī): A person living outside the miqat boundaries, not a Makkan.
ذو الحليفة (Dhū al-Ḥulayfah): Miqat for those coming from Madinah, near Bi'r Ali.
ذات عرق (Dhāt ʿIrq): Miqat for those coming from the east (Iraq region).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The miqat is a spatial boundary; Dhu al-Hulayfah and Dhat 'Irq are two of the five Hanafi miqats serving different regions.

Conditions and Pillars of Hajj
Ruling statement on conditions and pillars of Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a woman's travel for Hajj and identify the two pillars of Hajj in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Four circuits of Tawaf al-Ifadah form its pillar; the remaining three are wajib, requiring compensation if omitted.

In this lesson, we examine the conditions that make Hajj obligatory and the essential components for its validity. The Hanafi school distinguishes between conditions (shurut) that must be present for obligation, conditions for performance, and pillars (arkan) whose omission invalidates the Hajj. We will also clarify the role of the mahram for women travelers and the exact definition of the two pillars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions for obligation
The passage lists: having a mahram (for women) or husband, safety of route, Islam, sanity, adulthood.
These are conditions for the Hajj to be obligatory, not for its validity.
2
Distinguish conditions from pillars
Ihram and Islam are conditions for valid performance, while standing at Arafah and Tawaf al-Ifadah are pillars.
Conditions must be present; pillars are integral components.
3
Analyze the standing at Arafah
Its time is from zawal on 9th Dhul-Hijjah to dawn of 10th. It requires ihram and abstaining from intercourse before it.
Intercourse before standing invalidates the Hajj completely.
4
Understand the Tawaf al-Ifadah
The pillar is the majority (four circuits); the remaining three are wajib. The time extends from dawn of 10th to the end of life, but performing it on the days of sacrifice is wajib.
Omission of a wajib requires a sacrifice (dam).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج شروط وجوب أداء الحج وصلية وخروج محرم ولو من رضاع أو مصاهرة، مسلم مأمون عاقل بالغ، أو زوج لامرأة في سفر، والعبرة بغلبة السلامة برّا وبحرا على المفتى ،به ويصح أداء فرض الحج بأربعة أشياء للحر الإحرام، والإسلام، وهما شرطان ثم الإتيان ،بركنيه، وهما الوقوف محرما بعرفات لحظة من زوال يوم التاسع إلى فجر يوم النحر بشرط عدم الجماع قبله محرما، والركن الثاني هو أكثر طواف الإفاضة في وقته وهو ما بعد طلوع فجر النحر. وخروج محرم إلخ هو من لا يجوز له مناكحتها على التأبيد بقرابة أو رضاع أو مصاهرة، أطلقه فشمل الحر والعبد. مسلم : الأولى أن يقول: غير مجوسي كما في "التنوير"؛ لما مر أنه يكفي الذمي. (حاشية الطحطاوي بتصرف) مأمون إلخ وخرج به المجوسي الذي يعتقد إباحة نكاحها، والمسلم القريب إذا لم يكن مأمونا، والصبي الذي لم يحتلم والمجنون؛ لأن المقصود من المحرم الحفظ والصيانة لها، وهو مفقود في هؤلاء الأربعة. [البحر الرائق: ٤٩١/٢] لامرأة أطلق المرأة فشمل الشابة والعجوز؛ لإطلاق النصوص والمرأة هي البالغة؛ لأن الكلام فيمن يجب عليه الحج، فلذا قالوا في الصبية التي لم تبلغ حد الشهوة تسافر بلا محرم؛ فإن بلغتها لا تسافر إلا به البحر الرائق بتصرف: ٤٩١/٢] في سفر قيد بالسفر، وهو ثلاثة أيام بلياليها؛ لأنه يباح لها الخروج إلى ما دون ذلك لحاجة بغير محرم، وأشار بعدم اشتراط رضا الزوج إلى أنه ليس له منعها عن حجة الإسلام إذا وجدت محرما؛ لأن حقه لا يظهر في الفرائض، بخلاف حج التطوع والمنذور. البحر الرائق: ٤٩١/٢] عدم الجماع: فإن فعل ذلك فسد حجه، وعليه أن يمضي فيه كالصحيح، وأن يقضي من قابل [حاشية الطحطاوي: (۷۲۹] هو أكثر إلخ: هو أربعة أشواط، والثلاثة الباقية واجبة يجبر تركها بالدم [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٢٩] فجر النحر إلى آخر العمر، والواجب فعله أيام النحر [حاشية الطحطاوي: (۷۲۹]
The Book of Hajj. Conditions for the obligation of performing Hajj: [having] a Mahram even if through breastfeeding or marriage, a trustworthy Muslim, sane, adult, or a husband for a woman in travel. Consideration is given to the prevailing safety by land and sea (according to the mufta bihi position). And the performance of the obligatory Hajj is valid with four things for a free person: ihram and Islam – these are two conditions; then performing its two pillars, which are standing at Arafah in the state of ihram for a moment from the decline of the sun on the ninth day until the dawn of the Day of Sacrifice, provided that there is no intercourse before it while in ihram. The second pillar is the majority of Tawaf al-Ifadah in its time, which is after the dawn of the Day of Sacrifice. 'And a Mahram etc.' means one whom she is permanently forbidden to marry due to kinship, breastfeeding, or marriage; he [the author] made it general to include free and slave. 'Muslim' – it is better to say 'non-Majus' as in al-Tanwir because a dhimmi is sufficient (from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi with modification). 'Trustworthy etc.' excludes the Majusi who believes that marrying her is permissible, and the Muslim relative if he is not trustworthy, and the boy who has not had a wet dream, and the insane; because the purpose of the mahram is protection and safeguarding for her, and that is absent in these four. [al-Bahr al-Raiq: 2/491] 'A woman' – he made it general to include young and old because of the general application of the texts, and 'woman' means an adult; because the discussion is about one upon whom Hajj is obligatory. Therefore they said about a girl who has not reached the age of desire: she travels without a mahram; if she reaches it, she does not travel except with him (al-Bahr al-Raiq with modification: 2/491). 'In travel' – restricted to travel, which is three days and nights; because it is permissible for her to go out for less than that for need without a mahram. And he indicated by the non-requirement of the husband's consent that he cannot prevent her from the Hajj of Islam if she finds a mahram; because his right is not evident in obligations, unlike voluntary Hajj and vowed Hajj. (al-Bahr al-Raiq: 2/491) 'Absence of intercourse' – if he does that, his Hajj becomes invalid, but he must continue in it like a sound one, and he must make it up the next year. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 729] 'Most of it etc.' – it is four circuits, and the remaining three are obligatory; omitting them is compensated by a sacrifice. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 729] 'Dawn of the Day of Sacrifice to the end of life, and the obligatory performance is on the days of sacrifice.' [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 729]
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from Nur al-Idah outlining the conditions for the obligation (shurut wujub) of Hajj and the conditions for its valid performance, as well as the two pillars (arkan). The author begins with the conditions for obligation: a woman must have a mahram (a permanently unmarriageable relative) for travel, the mahram must be a trustworthy Muslim, sane adult, or a husband. The preferred view (mufta bihi) considers safety of route. Then for valid performance of obligatory Hajj, four things are required: ihram and Islam (conditions), and performing the two pillars. The first pillar is standing at Arafah for even a moment between the decline of sun on 9th Dhul-Hijjah and dawn of 10th, provided no intercourse before it. The second pillar is performing most of Tawaf al-Ifadah (four out of seven circuits) after dawn of the 10th. The commentary from al-Bahr al-Raiq and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi explains each term: mahram includes free and slave; a Muslim mahram should be a non-Majusi, but a dhimmi suffices; a trustworthy person is one who does not believe in marrying the woman; a minor or insane does not suffice. The woman is an adult; a girl below age of desire can travel without mahram for short journeys of less than three days. The husband cannot prevent the obligatory Hajj. If intercourse occurs before the first standing, the Hajj is invalidated but must be continued and repeated next year. The majority of Tawaf al-Ifadah means four circuits, which is the pillar; the remaining three are wajib and omission requires compensation with a sacrifice (dam). The time for Tawaf al-Ifadah extends from dawn of 10th to the end of life, but performing it on the days of sacrifice is wajib.

Key Terms
مَحْرَم (mahram): A person whom a woman is permanently prohibited from marrying due to blood, breastfeeding, or marriage relationship, and who is trustworthy, adult, and sane, and who must accompany her for Hajj travel.
رُكْن (rukn): A fundamental component of Hajj; omission of a pillar invalidates the Hajj. The two pillars here: standing at Arafah and the majority of Tawaf al-Ifadah.
طَوَاف الإفَاضَة (tawaf al-ifadah): The obligatory circumambulation of the Kaaba performed after standing at Arafah and during the days of sacrifice. Its pillar is four circuits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a pilgrim omits three circuits of Tawaf al-Ifadah?
A) The Tawaf is invalid and must be repeated entirely.
B) The Tawaf is valid but a sacrifice (dam) is required for the omission.
C) The Tawaf is valid and no compensation is needed.
D) The pilgrim must restart the Tawaf from the beginning.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires four circuits of Tawaf al-Ifadah as a pillar; omission of three circuits requires a sacrifice but does not invalidate the Tawaf.

The Positive Wajibat of Hajj
Positive wajibat of Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the positive wajibat of Hajj according to the Hanafi school and explain the consequence of omitting any of them.

Core Idea
Hajj has wajibat whose omission requires a sacrifice (dam), but does not invalidate the pilgrimage.

This lesson covers the obligatory acts (wajibat) of Hajj that must be performed. Unlike the pillars (arkan), if a wajib is missed, the Hajj is still valid but a sacrifice (dam) becomes obligatory. We will go through each act and its conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initiation wajib
The first wajib is starting ihram from the designated miqat (time or place). This establishes the state of consecration.
If ihram is begun after the miqat, a dam is required.
2
Identify the standing wajibat
You must stand at Arafah (extending it until sunset) and at Muzdalifah (from dawn to sunrise). These are separate wajibat.
The sunset is included in the time for Arafah; the standing at Muzdalifah is wajib per Hanafi.
3
Identify the subsequent wajibat
These include stoning the jamarat, slaughtering for qarin/mutamatti', shaving or trimming hair – all in the Haram and the prescribed order (stoning before shaving).
Slaughtering is wajib for qarin and mutamatti', not for ifrad.
4
Identify the tawaf and sa'y wajibat
Tawaf al-Ziyarah must be performed during the days of sacrifice, followed by sa'y between Safa and Marwah after a valid tawaf. Walking is wajib for those without excuse.
Sa'y is wajib (not rukn) per Hanafi; Shafi'i considers it a rukn.
5
Identify the farewell and detailed rules
Non-residents must perform Tawaf al-Wada. Additionally, each tawaf must start at the Black Stone, be performed counterclockwise (yatayamun), and the person must be in a state of purity (wudu) and covering the awrah.
The minimum circuits after performing the majority of Tawaf al-Ziyarah is also counted as a wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وواجبات الحج: إنشاء الإحرام من الميقات ومدُّ الوقوف بعرفات إلى الغروب، الغاية داخلة في المغيا والوقوف بالمزدلفة فيما بعد فجر يوم النحر وقبل طلوع الشمس، ورمي الجمار، وذبح القارن والمتمتع، والحلق، أو التقصير وتخصيصه بالحرم وأيام النحر، وتقديم الرمي على الحلق، ونحر القارن والمتمتع بينهما، وإيقاع طواف الزيارة في أيام النحر، والسعي بين الصفا والمروة في أشهر الحج، وحصوله بعد طواف معتد به، والمشي فيه لمن لا عذر له وبداءة السعي من الصفا، وطواف الوداع للآفاقي، وبداءة كل طواف بالبيت من الحجر الأسود، والتيامن فيه والمشي فيه لمن لا عذر له والطهارة من الحدثين، وستر العورة، وأقل الأشواط بعد فعل الأكثر من طواف الزيارة، وترك المحظورات كلبس الرجل المخيط، وستر رأسه ووجهه وستر المرأة وجهها، والرفث، والفسوق، والجدال . الرفث إلخ الرفث: الجماع، وقيل: الكلام الفاحش إلا أن ابن عباس يقول: إنما يكون الكلام الفاحش رفتا بحضرة النساء والفسوق المعاصي، وهو منهي عنه في الإحرام وغيره، إلا أنه في الإحرام أشد كلبس الحرير في الصلاة، والتطريب في قراءة القرآن والجدال الخصومة مع الرفقاء والخدم والمكارين. البحر الرائق بحذف: ٥٠١/٢]
And the obligatory acts (wajibat) of Hajj: initiating ihram from the miqat; prolonging the standing at Arafah until sunset (the limit is included in what is limited); standing at Muzdalifah after the dawn of the Day of Sacrifice and before sunrise; stoning the jamarat; slaughtering for the qarin and mutamatti'; shaving or shortening the hair, and restricting it to the Haram and the days of sacrifice; giving precedence to stoning over shaving; slaughtering the qarin and mutamatti' between them; performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah during the days of sacrifice; the sa'y between Safa and Marwah during the months of Hajj, and its occurrence after a tawaf that is considered valid; walking during it for one without excuse; beginning the sa'y from Safa; the farewell tawaf for the non-resident (afaqi); beginning every tawaf at the House from the Black Stone; moving to the right (yatayamun) during it; walking during it for one without excuse; purification from both hadaths; covering the private parts; the minimum circuits after performing the majority of Tawaf al-Ziyarah; and refraining from prohibitions such as a man wearing sewn garments, covering his head and face, a woman covering her face, rafath, fusuq, and jidal. 'Rafath etc.' – rafath is intercourse, and it is said: obscene speech, except that Ibn Abbas says: obscene speech is only rafath in the presence of women. Fusuq is disobedience, and it is forbidden during ihram and otherwise, but it is more severe during ihram, like wearing silk in prayer, and singing/chanting in Quran recitation. Jidal is quarreling with companions, servants, and transporters. Al-Bahr al-Raiq abridged: 2/501.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage lists the wajibat (obligatory acts) of Hajj according to the Hanafi school. Unlike pillars (arkan), omission of a wajib does not invalidate the Hajj but requires compensation (dam). The list includes: 1) Starting ihram from the designated miqat (specific place or time). 2) Extending the standing at Arafah until sunset (the sunset is included in the time). 3) Standing at Muzdalifah after dawn of the 10th until sunrise. 4) Stoning the three jamarat. 5) Slaughtering for the qarin (one performing Hajj and Umrah together) and the mutamatti' (one performing Umrah then Hajj). 6) Shaving or shortening hair, which must be done in the Haram on the days of sacrifice. 7) Preferring stoning before shaving. 8) Slaughtering (for qarin and mutamatti') between stoning and shaving. 9) Performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah during the days of sacrifice. 10) Sa'y between Safa and Marwah during the months of Hajj, after a valid tawaf. 11) Walking during sa'y for those without excuse. 12) Beginning sa'y from Safa. 13) Farewell tawaf for non-residents. 14) Starting each tawaf from the Black Stone. 15) Moving to the right (counterclockwise). 16) Walking during tawaf for those without excuse. 17) Being pure from both major and minor impurities (hadath). 18) Covering the private parts. 19) The minimum number of circuits after performing the majority of Tawaf al-Ziyarah (i.e., the wajib remainder). 20) Refraining from prohibitions: men wearing sewn clothes, covering head and face; women covering face; rafath (intercourse or obscenity), fusuq (sin), and jidal (quarreling). The commentary explains rafath: it means intercourse or, according to some, obscene speech, but Ibn Abbas restricts it to obscenity in the presence of women. Fusuq is disobedience, more severe during ihram, analogous to wearing silk in prayer. Jidal is fighting with companions, servants, or transporters.

Key Terms
وَاجِب (wajib): An obligatory act in Hajj that is not a pillar (rukn); omission requires compensation (dam) but does not invalidate the Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Prohibitions (Muharramat) and Etiquette of Tawaf and Sa'y
Prohibitions and definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the prohibited acts during ihram, state the Hanafi legal definitions of rafath, fusuq, and jidal, and apply the rules for tawaf and sa'y.

Core Idea
Prohibitions during Hajj, like wearing sewn clothes or quarreling, require compensation (dam) and are more severe in ihram.

The final part of the passage details the prohibitions (muharramat) that must be avoided during Hajj, along with definitions of key terms. Additionally, it reiterates rules for tawaf and sa'y regarding walking, purity, and covering. Understanding these prohibitions is essential to avoiding sins and penalties.

Guided Path
1
List the prohibitions mentioned
The passage lists: men wearing sewn garments, covering the head and face, women covering the face, rafath, fusuq, and jidal.
Each of these, if violated knowingly, requires a dam (or invalidates if rafath before tahallul).
2
Define rafath, fusuq, and jidal
Rafath is sexual intercourse or obscene speech in the presence of women. Fusuq is disobedience, more severe in ihram. Jidal is quarreling with companions, servants, or transporters.
These definitions are from the commentary.
3
Understand the severity
Fusuq during ihram is compared to wearing silk in prayer, indicating heightened gravity.
Jidal is not just any argument but quarreling over worldly matters.
4
Revisit tawaf and sa'y rules
The passage also restates: tawaf must start at the Black Stone, be performed counterclockwise, walking for those able, with purity and covering awrah. Sa'y must begin at Safa.
These are wajib conditions; omitting them requires dam.

The Five Miqat Places for Ihram
Lists the five miqat places for ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to name the five miqat places and identify which pilgrims use each.

Core Idea
There are five fixed places outside Makkah where pilgrims must enter ihram – each serves a specific regional group.

The term 'miqat' can refer to either a time or a place for entering ihram. In this lesson, we focus on the five geographical miqat places that pilgrims from outside the Haram (afaqi) must use. Knowing these locations ensures that one fulfills the obligation of ihram at the correct boundary.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concept of miqat
Recognize that miqat here means the appointed place (zaman vs. makan). The lesson clarifies that the intended meaning is the place.
Miqat can also refer to time (e.g., the months of Hajj), but here it is place.
2
Memorize the five place names
Learn the names: Dhu al-Hulaifah, Dhat 'Irq, al-Juhfah, Qarn, and Yalamlam. Associate each with a region or direction.
Use mnemonic: Madinah → Dhu al-Hulaifah; East → Dhat 'Irq; Syria/Egypt → al-Juhfah; Najd → Qarn; Yemen → Yalamlam.
3
Locate each miqat relative to Makkah
Note the distances: Dhu al-Hulaifah is farthest (9-10 stages), Dhat 'Irq about 2 stages, al-Juhfah about 3 stages, Qarn about 2 stages, Yalamlam about 2 stages.
Distances in 'stages' (marhalah) are approximate travel distances.
4
Apply the rule for an afaqi
Understand that any afaqi (person residing outside the miqat area) must assume ihram before crossing their respective miqat. Failure to do so requires returning to the miqat or offering a dam.
Residents of the Haram or within the miqat area do not have this obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الميقات: أي المكان الذي لا يتجاوزه الآفاقي إلا محرما خمسة، فالميقات مشترك بين الوقت المعين والمكان المعين، والمراد هنا الثاني. الأول: ذو الحليفة - بضم الحاء المهملة وبالفاء - بينه وبين مكة نحو عشر مراحل أو تسع، وبينه وبين المدينة ستة أميال، وقيل: سبعة، وهو ميقات أهل المدينة وهو أبعد المواقيت وبهذا المكان آبار تسميه العوام: آبار عليه قيل: لأن علي بن أبي طالب قاتل الجن في بعض تلك الآبار، والثاني: ذات عرق بكسر العين وسكون الراء - الجميع أهل المشرق، وهي بين المشرق والمغرب من مكة، - قيل وبينها وبين مكة مرحلتان. قائله . كذب وهو من والثالث: الجحفة بضم الجيم وسكون الحاء المهملة، واسمها في الأصل مهيعة، قال النووي: بينها وبين مكة ثلاث مراحل، وهي قرية بين المغرب والشمال من مكة من طريق تبوك، وهي طريق أهل الشام ونواحيها اليوم، وهي ميقات أهل مصر والمغرب والشام. والرابع: قرن بفتح القاف وسكون الراء، وهو جبل مطل على عرفات بينه وبين مكة نحو مرحلتين، وهو ميقات أهل نجد. والخامس: يلملم، وهو ميقات أهل اليمن، وهو مكان جنوبي مكة، وهو جبل من جبال تهامة على مرحلتين من مكة. [البحر الرائق بزيادة وتصرف: ٤٩٣/٢]
The miqat: i.e., the place which the one coming from outside (afaqi) should not pass except in ihram; there are five. The miqat is shared between the specified time and the specified place, and the intention here is the second (place). First: Dhu al-Hulaifah – with a damm on the ha and a fa – between it and Makkah is about ten or nine stages, between it and Madinah is six miles, some say seven. It is the miqat of the people of Madinah and it is the farthest of the mawaqit. At this place there are wells that the common people call 'Abu 'Ali' because it is said that Ali ibn Abi Talib fought the jinn in some of those wells. Second: Dhat 'Irq – with a kasr on the 'ain and sukun on the ra – for all people of the east. It is between the east and west of Makkah. It is said that between it and Makkah is two stages. Its speaker: [corrupted phrase] 'kadhiba wa huwa min'. Third: al-Juhfah – with a damm on the jim and sukun on the ha – its original name is Mahya'ah. An-Nawawi said: between it and Makkah is three stages. It is a village between the west and north of Makkah on the road to Tabuk. It is the route of the people of Sham today, and it is the miqat of the people of Egypt, Maghreb, and Sham. Fourth: Qarn – with a fatha on the qaf and sukun on the ra – it is a mountain overlooking Arafat, between it and Makkah about two stages. It is the miqat of the people of Najd. Fifth: Yalamlam – it is the miqat of the people of Yemen. It is a place south of Makkah, a mountain of Tihama, two stages from Makkah. [al-Bahr al-Raiq with additions and modification: 2/493]
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage defines the miqat (appointed place) for entering ihram. There are five such places for those coming from outside the Haram (afaqi). The term miqat can also refer to time, but here it means place. The five places are: (1) Dhu al-Hulaifah, near Madinah, the furthest miqat, about 9-10 stages from Makkah. It is the miqat for people of Madinah and those coming from that direction. There is a popular story about Ali (RA) fighting jinn there. (2) Dhat 'Irq, for people coming from the east (Iraq, Iran, etc.), located between east and west of Makkah, about two stages away. (3) al-Juhfah, originally called Mahya'ah, for people from Syria, Egypt, Maghreb, etc., about three stages from Makkah. (4) Qarn al-Manazil, a mountain overlooking Arafat, for people of Najd, about two stages away. (5) Yalamlam, south of Makkah, for Yemenis, about two stages away. These places are boundaries beyond which a pilgrim must be in ihram.

Key Terms
مِيقَات (miqat): The appointed place (or time) for entering ihram. Here it specifically means the five geographical places from which pilgrims from outside the Haram must assume ihram.
آفَاقِي (afaqi): A person who resides outside the Miqat (the areas surrounding Makkah). Such a person must enter ihram before crossing the miqat.
ذُو الْحُلَيْفَة (Dhu al-Hulaifah): The miqat for the people of Madinah, located about 6-7 miles from Madinah and 9-10 stages from Makkah. It is the farthest miqat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Dhat 'Irq
B) Dhu al-Hulaifah
C) al-Juhfah
D) Yalamlam

Key Takeaway
The five miqat places – Dhu al-Hulaifah, Dhat 'Irq, al-Juhfah, Qarn, and Yalamlam – serve as obligatory boundaries for pilgrims from different regions to enter ihram.

Wajibat and Prohibitions of Hajj
Lists wajibat and prohibitions of Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the wajibat of Hajj according to the Hanafi school and distinguish between wajib and haram acts during ihram.

Core Idea
The wajibat of Hajj include standing at Muzdalifah, throwing pebbles, sacrificing, shaving, Tawaf al-Ziyarah, and Sa'y; prohibitions incur penalties.

In Hanafi fiqh, Hajj comprises a set of obligatory (wajib) acts and prohibitions (muharramat) during ihram. This lesson examines the specific actions listed in our text that must be performed and the prohibitions that must be avoided.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being described and its legal classification (wajib, haram, etc.). The text lists actions like standing at Muzdalifah and prohibitions like wearing sewn garments.
2
Distinguish between wajib and haram
Note that most listed actions are wajib (obligatory), while the prohibitions (like covering the face for men) are haram during ihram. Omission of a wajib requires a dam, while violation of a haram requires fidyah.
3
Understand conditions for specific acts
For Sa'y and Tawaf, conditions are mentioned: Sa'y must be after a valid Tawaf, Tawaf requires purity and covering awrah. Identify these conditions.
4
Note the Hanafi classification
In Hanafi fiqh, these acts are wajib, not fard. Understand the difference: wajib is proven by zanni dalil, and its omission requires compensation.
This is a distinct Hanafi position.

شروط وجوب أداء الحج والوقوف بالمزدلفة فيما بعد فجر يوم النحر وقبل طلوع الشمس، ورمي الجمار، وذبح القارن والمتمتع، والحلق، أو التقصير، وتخصيصه بالحرم وأيام النحر، وتقديم الرمي على الحلق، ونحر القارن والمتمتع بينهما، وإيقاع طواف الزيارة في أيام النحر، والسعي بين الصفا والمروة في أشهر الحج، وحصوله بعد طواف معتد به، والمشي فيه لمن لا عذر له وبداءة السعي من الصفا، وطواف الوداع للآفاقي، وبداءة كل طواف بالبيت من الحجر الأسود، والتيامن فيه والمشي فيه لمن لا عذر له والطهارة من الحدثين، وستر العورة، وأقل الأشواط بعد فعل الأكثر من طواف الزيارة، وترك المحظورات كلبس الرجل المخيط، وستر رأسه ووجهه وستر المرأة وجهها، والرفث، والفسوق، والجدال .
والثالث: الجحفة بضم الجيم وسكون الحاء المهملة، واسمها في الأصل مهيعة، قال النووي: بينها وبين مكة ثلاث مراحل، وهي قرية بين المغرب والشمال من مكة من طريق تبوك، وهي طريق أهل الشام ونواحيها اليوم، وهي ميقات أهل مصر والمغرب والشام.
والرابع: قرن بفتح القاف وسكون الراء، وهو جبل مطل على عرفات بينه وبين مكة نحو مرحلتين، وهو ميقات أهل نجد.

Conditions for the obligation of performing Hajj: standing at Muzdalifah after dawn of the Day of Sacrifice and before sunrise, throwing the pebbles, slaughtering for the qarin and mutamatti', shaving or trimming, confining it to the Haram and the days of sacrifice, giving precedence to throwing over shaving, slaughtering for the qarin and mutamatti' between them, performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah on the days of sacrifice, Sa'y between Safa and Marwah in the months of Hajj, it being after a valid Tawaf, walking in it for one without excuse, beginning Sa'y from Safa, Tawaf al-Wada' for the non-Makki, beginning every Tawaf at the House from the Black Stone, going rightward in it, walking in it for one without excuse, purity from both hadaths, covering the awrah, the minimum number of circuits after performing the majority of Tawaf al-Ziyarah, avoiding prohibitions like a man wearing sewn garments, covering his head and face, a woman covering her face, obscenity, sin, and quarrelling. And the third: al-Juhfah, with dammah on the jeem and sukoon on the important ha, its original name Mahya'ah, al-Nawawi said: between it and Makkah are three stages, it is a village between the west and north of Makkah on the Tabuk route, it is today the route of the people of Sham and its environs, and it is the miqat of the people of Egypt, the Maghrib, and Sham. And the fourth: Qarn, with fatha on the qaf and sukoon on the ra, it is a mountain overlooking Arafat between it and Makkah about two stages, and it is the miqat of the people of Najd. And the fifth: Yalamlam, it is the miqat of the people of Yemen, it is a place south of Makkah, it is a mountain from the mountains of Tihamah two stages from Makkah. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq with addition and adaptation: 2/493]

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from a Hanafi fiqh work that lists the conditions for the obligation of performing Hajj along with the miqat locations. It begins by enumerating the required actions and prohibitions: standing at Muzdalifah, throwing pebbles, sacrificing for qarin and mutamatti', shaving or trimming, confining rituals to the Haram, ordering certain acts, performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah and Sa'y with their conditions, and avoiding prohibitions like sewn garments for men, covering the face for women, and sins. Then it describes the third, fourth, and fifth miqats: al-Juhfah (for Egypt, Maghrib, Sham), Qarn (for Najd), and Yalamlam (for Yemen), citing al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The first two miqats (Dhu al-Hulayfah and al-Juhfah? Actually the first is Dhu al-Hulayfah) are not included here as they were on a previous page. The passage serves as a memorization anchor for students to learn the key obligations and boundaries of Hajj.

Key Terms
ميقات (miqat): A specific place or time for entering ihram; here the five spatial miqats are mentioned.
قارن (qarin): One who performs Hajj and Umrah together in a single ihram.
