The Five Miqat Locations for Hajj
Describes three of the five miqat locations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to name the five miqat locations for Hajj and identify which region each serves.

Core Idea
The miqat is the place where one enters ihram; there are five fixed miqats for different regions.

The spatial miqats are fixed points beyond which one may not pass without ihram. Our text describes the last three (Juhfah, Qarn, Yalamlam). The first two are Dhu al-Hulayfah for Madinah and al-Juhfah? Actually, the first is Dhu al-Hulayfah, second is al-Juhfah, but the text lists Juhfah as third. We will cover all five based on standard Hanafi sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the miqat and its location
For each miqat, note its name in Arabic, its geographical location, and its distance from Makkah.
2
Know the region it serves
Each miqat is associated with a specific region or route. For example, Qarn is for people of Najd.
3
Understand the ruling
Entering ihram at the miqat is wajib. Passing the miqat without ihram requires a dam.
4
Memorize the five miqats
Use mnemonic devices: Dhu al-Hulayfah (Madinah), al-Juhfah (Syria/Egypt), Qarn (Najd), Yalamlam (Yemen), Dhat Irq (Iraq).
Our text only mentions three; the first two are from other sources.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
6 min
Sunnas of Hajj
Enumerates recommended acts (sunan) of Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the sunnas of Hajj as per the Hanafi school and distinguish them from wajibat and arkan.

Core Idea
The sunnas of Hajj are beloved acts that perfect the pilgrimage; omitting them reduces reward but does not invalidate.

In this lesson, we examine the enumerated sunnas (recommended acts) of Hajj from the Hanafi text. These acts, while not obligatory, are highly meritorious and complete the Hajj experience. Memorizing them helps a pilgrim perform the rites with greater mindfulness and reward.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the category
Understand that these acts are sunnah muakkadah, not fard or wajib. Omission does not hinder validity.
Sunnah muakkadah is a stressed recommendation.
2
List the sunnas before ihram
Identify the acts preparatory to ihram: ghusl (even for menstruating/postpartum women) or wudu, wearing new white garments, applying perfume, and praying two rak'ahs.
Perfume is applied to the body, not the garment if trace remains.
3
List the sunnas after ihram
Identify the sunnas performed after entering ihram: reciting talbiyah loudly, repeating it at specific times and places, sending blessings on the Prophet, asking for Paradise, accompanying the righteous, and seeking refuge from the Fire.
Raising the voice in talbiyah is recommended for men.
4
List the sunnas upon entering Makkah
Identify the sunnas when approaching and entering Makkah: ghusl for entry, entering from Bab al-Ma'lah during the day, saying takbir and tahlil facing the Kaaba, and making supplication upon seeing the House.
Bab al-Ma'lah is a specific gate known as the upper gate.
5
Recall exceptions and details
Note that the ghusl is sunna even for women in menstruation/postpartum, and that the list does not include obligatory acts.
The two rak'ahs after ihram are performed after the obligatory prayer if the time has entered.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسنن الحج منها : الاغتسال ولو لحائض ونفساء، أو الوضوء إذا أراد الإحرام، ولبس إزار ورداء جديدين أبيضين والتطيب وصلاة ركعتين، والإكثار من التلبية بعد الإحرام رافعا بها صوته متى صلى أو علا شرفا أو هبط واديا أو لقى ركبا وبالأسحار، وتكريرها كلّما أخذ فيها، والصلاة على النبي، وسؤال الجنة، وصحبة الأبرار والاستعاذة من النار، والغسل لدخول مكة، ودخولها من باب المعلاة نهارا والتكبير والتهليل تلقاء البيت الشريف، والدعاء بما أحب عند رؤيته،
And the sunnas of Hajj include: bathing even for a menstruating woman and a woman in postpartum bleeding, or performing wudu if one intends ihram, wearing a new white waistcloth and cloak, applying perfume, praying two rak'ahs, increasing the talbiyah after ihram raising the voice with it whenever one prays or ascends a high place or descends a valley or meets a caravan and at dawn, repeating it every time one begins it, sending blessings on the Prophet, asking for Paradise, accompanying the righteous, seeking refuge from the Fire, bathing for entering Makkah, entering it from the Bab al-Ma'lah during the day, saying takbir and tahlil facing the noble House, and supplicating with whatever one likes upon seeing it.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement detailing the recommended acts (sunan) of Hajj according to the Hanafi school. It lists the sunnas in sequence: bathing or wudu before ihram, wearing new white garments, applying perfume, praying two rak'ahs, reciting talbiyah loudly at specific times, repeating it, sending blessings on the Prophet, asking for Paradise, accompanying the righteous, seeking refuge from the Fire, bathing for entering Makkah, entering from Bab al-Ma'lah during the day, saying takbir and tahlil upon seeing the Kaaba, and making supplication. These acts are not obligatory but bring reward. The text also notes that women in menstruation or postpartum bleeding still perform the sunna of bathing. The commentary (not shown here) explains details like the impermissibility of applying perfume to the garment if its trace remains. Students should memorize these sunnas to practice a complete Hajj.

Key Terms
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act that carries reward but is not obligatory.
تلبية (talbiyah): The phrase 'Labbayka Allahumma labbayk...' recited by pilgrims.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate

Sunnahs of Hajj and Their Explanations
List of sunnah acts of Hajj with marginal commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the sunnah acts of Hajj according to the Hanafi school, explain the conditions and details of each (including idtiba', ramal, harwalah, and the day of tarwiyah), and distinguish them from wajibat.

Core Idea
Sunnah acts of Hajj are recommended enhancements; their omission does not invalidate the Hajj nor require a sacrifice.

This passage from Nur al-Idah systematically enumerates the sunnah (recommended) acts of Hajj according to the Hanafi school. While often mistaken for obligations, these acts are voluntary and carry reward but no penalty if omitted. Understanding each act's specific conditions—such as when ramal is performed or how idtiba' is done—ensures that the pilgrim can follow the sunnah correctly without confusion. The passage also includes marginal notes clarifying rulings, such as the prohibition of perfume on the garment and the recommended raising of voice in talbiyah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overarching category
The passage explicitly states 'Sunan al-Hajj' (Sunnahs of Hajj). Recognise that these are recommended acts (sunnah), not obligatory (wajib) or pillars (arkan). Omission does not require dam (compensatory sacrifice) and does not invalidate the Hajj.
This distinction is critical to avoid overburdening the pilgrim.
2
Categorize by timeline
Group the sunnah acts chronologically: before ihram (ghusl, perfume, two rak'ahs), at entering Mecca (ghusl, entry from al-Ma'la, takbir), during tawaf (idtiba', ramal), during sa'y (harwalah between the green milestones), and on the days of Hajj (khutbah on 7th, going to Mina on 8th, etc.). This helps in memorisation and application.
The passage follows this order implicitly.
3
Detail the conditions of each sunnah
For each act, note the specific conditions mentioned in the commentary. For example, ramal is only for men, only in the first three circuits of tawaf, and only if sa'y follows in the Hajj months. Harwalah is between the two green milestones in sa'y. Idtiba' is done by placing the upper garment under the right armpit.
These conditions prevent incorrect practice.
4
Understand the Hanafi grading
The passage uses the term 'sunnah' explicitly. In Hanafi fiqh, sunnah is a recommended act that carries reward if done and no sin if omitted. This is distinct from wajib (required, omission requires dam) and fard (pillar, omission invalidates). The commentary reinforces this by noting that missing ramal does not require repetition.
Some sunnahs like tawaf al-qudum are stressed but still sunnah.
5
Note intra-school differences
The passage mentions an ikhtilaf regarding perfume on the garment: one narration from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf forbids it if the scent remains, and the relied-upon position is to apply perfume only on the body. Recognise that such differences exist within the Hanafi school and the mufta bihi is given.
This helps in understanding the development of fiqh rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج
سنن الحج
وقتل الصيد، والإشارة إليه، والدلالة عليه.
وسنن الحج منها : الاغتسال ولو لحائض ونفساء، أو الوضوء إذا أراد الإحرام، ولبس إزار ورداء جديدين أبيضين والتطيب وصلاة ركعتين، والإكثار من التلبية بعد الإحرام رافعا بها صوته متى صلى أو علا شرفا أو هبط واديا أو لقى ركبا صل الله وبالأسحار، وتكريرها كلّما أخذ فيها، والصلاة على النبي ، وسؤال الجنة، أي في جنة النعيم عطف على التلبية وصحبة الأبرار والاستعاذة من النار، والغسل لدخول مكة، ودخولها من باب المعلاة نهارا والتكبير والتهليل تلقاء البيت الشريف، والدعاء بما أحب عند رؤيته،
إسناد القتل إليه.
وقتل الصيد : أريد بالصيد ههنا المصيد؛ إذ لو أريد به المصدر – وهو الاصطياد - لما صح البحر الرائق: ٥۰۲/۲] والدلالة عليه الفرق بين الإشارة والدلالة: أن الإشارة تقتضي الحضرة، والدلالة تقتضي الغيبة البحر الرائق ٥۰۲/۲] إزار ورداء أولهما لستر العورة، وثانيهما لستر الكتفين، فإن الصلاة مع كشفهما أو كشف أحدهما مكروهة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٣٠]
والتطيب أي يسن له استعمال الطيب في بدنه قبيل الإحرام. أطلقه فشمل ما تبقى عينه بعده كالمسك والغالية، وما لا تبقى. وقيدنا بالبدن؛ إذ لا يجوز التطيب في الثوب بما تبقى عينه على قول الكل على إحدى الروايتين عنهما، قالوا: وبه نأخذ. [البحر الرائق بحذف : ٤٩٨/٢] رافعا إلخ اعلم أن المستحب عندنا في الدعاء والأذكار الخفية، إلا فيما تعلق بإعلانه مقصود كالأذان والخطبة ،وغيرهما، والتلبية أيضا للشروع فيما هو من أعلام الدين، فلهذا كان المستحب رفع الصوت بها، كذا في "المبسوط". [الكفاية ٣٥١/٢] صوته: فإن ترك رفع الصوت كان مسيئا، ولا شيء عليه، ولا يبالغ فيه، فيجهد نفسه؛ كيلا يتضرر. فتح القدير بتصرف: ٣٥١/٢] صلى: أطلق الصلاة فشمل فرضها وواجبها ونفلها وهو ظاهر الرواية، وخصها الطحاوي بالمكتوبات قياسا على تكبيرات التشريق. [البحر الرائق: ٥٠٥/٢] أو لقي ركبا: جمع راكب كتير جمع تاجر. [البحر الرائق: ٥٠٥/٢] وتكريرها أي يكررها كلما أخذ فيها ثلاث مرات، ويأتي بها على الولاء، ولا يقطعها بكلام البحر الرائق: ٥٠٥/٢] المعلاة أي من ثنية كداء بالفتح والمد الثنية العليا بأعلى مكة عند المقبرة، ولا ينصرف للعلمية والتأنيث، وتسمى تلك الجهة المعلى، وترك الحاج ذلك في هذه الأيام. [حاشية الطحطاوي بحذف: ٧٣٠] والتكبير والتهليل أي حين مشاهدة البيت المكرم ومعناه : الله أكبر من الكعبة والتوحيد؛ لئلا يقع نوع شرك. حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٣٠]
وهو مستجاب، وطواف القدوم، ولو في غير أشهر الحج والاضطباع فيه، والرمل للأفاقي إن سعى بعده في أشهر الحج والهرولة فيما بين الميلين الأخضرين للرجال، والمشي راجع إلى الرمل والهرولة على هيئة في باقي السعي، والإكثار من الطواف، وهو أفضل من صلاة النفل أي الإسراع في المشي للآفاقي، والخطبة بعد صلاة الظهر يوم سابع الحجة بمكة، وهي خطبة واحدة بلا وكره قبله جلوس يعلم المناسك فيها، والخروج بعد طلوع الشمس يوم التروية من هو ثامن ذي الحجة مكة لمنى، والمبيت بها، ثم الخروج منها بعد طلوع الشمس يوم عرفة إلى عرفات، فيخطب الإمام بعد الزوال قبل صلاة الظهر والعصر مجموعة جمع تقديم مع الظهر خطبتين حال من العصر يجلس بينهما، والاجتهاد في التضرع والخشوع والبكاء بالدموع، والدعاء للنفس والوالدين والإخوان المؤمنين بما شاء من أمر الدارين في الجمعين،
والاضطباع هو أن يدخل ثوبه تحت يده اليمنى، ويلقيه على عاتقه الأيسر. [البحر الرائق: ٥٠٨/٢] والرمل : هو المشي بسرعة مع تقارب الخُطا وهز الكتفين في الثلاثة الأول استنانا، فلو ترك أو نسيه في الثلاثة الأول لم يرمل في الباقي، ولو زحمه الناس وقف حتى يجد فرجة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٣٠] الميلين الأخضرين هما شيئان على شكل الميلين منحوتان من نفس جدار المسجد الحرام، إلا أنهما منفصلان عنه، وهما علامتان لموضع الهرولة في ممر بطن الوادي بين الصفا والمروة. [البحر الرائق: ٥١٥/۲] على هيئة أي على السكينة والوقار، فعلة من الهون. (العناية) للآفاقي: وأما غيره، وهو المقيم بالحرم ، فإن كان زمن الموسم فالنفل أفضل من الطواف، وفي غيره الأفضل له الطواف أيضا.
يوم التروية: قيل: إنما سمي بذلك؛ لأن إبراهيم الما رأى ليلة التروية كأن قائلا يقول له: إن الله يأمر بذبح ابنك هذا، فلما أصبح تروى أي تفكر في ذلك من الصباح إلى الرواح، أ من الله تعالى هذا الحكم أم من الشيطان؟ فمن ثمه سمي يوم التروية، فلما أمسى رأى مثل ذلك، فعرف أنه من الله تعالى، فمن ثم سمي يوم عرفة، ثم رأى مثله في الليلة الثالثة فهم بنحره، فسمي اليوم بيوم النحر. وقيل: إنما سمي يوم التروية بذلك؛ لأن الناس يروون بالماء من العطش في هذا اليوم، ويحملون الماء بالروايا إلى عرفات ومنى، وإنما سمي يوم عرفة به؛ لأن جبريل عليه علم إبراهيم عليها المناسك كلها يوم عرفة، فقال له أعرفت في أي موضع تطوف؟ وفي أي موضع تسعى؟ وفي أي موضع تقف؟ وفي أي موضع تنحر وترمي؟ فقال: عرفت فسمي يوم عرفة [العناية: ٣٦٨/٢]
Book of Hajj. Sunnahs of Hajj. And killing game, and pointing to it, and guiding to it. And from the sunnahs of Hajj: taking a bath even for a menstruating woman and a woman in postpartum bleeding, or performing wudu if one intends ihram; wearing a new white waistcloth and outer garment; applying perfume; praying two rak'ahs; increasing the talbiyah after ihram, raising one's voice with it whenever one prays or ascends a high place or descends a valley or meets a rider, and at dawns; repeating it whenever one begins it; and sending blessings upon the Prophet, and asking for Paradise, i.e. the Garden of Bliss, which is an apposition to talbiyah; and companionship of the righteous; and seeking refuge from the Fire; and bathing for entering Mecca; entering it from the gate of al-Ma'la during the day; saying Allahu Akbar and la ilaha illa Allah in front of the noble House; and supplicating as one wishes when seeing it. Attribution of killing to him. And killing game: what is meant by 'sayd' here is the hunted animal; for if the source meaning were intended—which is hunting—it would not be correct. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 2:502] And guiding to it: the difference between pointing and guiding is that pointing requires presence, while guiding requires absence. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 2:502] Waistcloth and outer garment: the first is to cover the private parts, and the second is to cover the shoulders, for prayer with them uncovered or one of them uncovered is disliked. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 730] And applying perfume: it is sunnah for him to use perfume on his body just before ihram. He [the author] made it absolute, so it includes what remains after it like musk and ghalia, and what does not remain. We restricted it to the body because perfume on the garment with what remains is not permissible according to all on one of two narrations from them [Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf?], and they said: we adopt this. [al-Bahr al-Raiq adapted 2:498] Raising the voice, etc.: Know that with us the recommended thing in supplications and remembrances is quietness, except regarding what is intended to be announced, like the adhan and khutbah, etc., and also talbiyah because it is entering into that which is among the symbols of the religion; for this reason raising the voice with it is recommended, as in al-Mabsut. [al-Kifaya 2:351] His voice: if he leaves off raising his voice, he is doing wrong, but nothing [required] upon him, and he should not exaggerate, straining himself, so that he is not harmed. [Fath al-Qadir adapted 2:351] He prayed: he made prayer absolute, so it includes obligatory, necessary, and supererogatory, and that is the apparent narration; al-Tahawi specified it with the prescribed prayers by analogy to the takbirs of tashriq. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 2:505] Or meets a rider: plural of rider like tijar is plural of tajir. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 2:505] And repeating it: he repeats it each time he begins it three times, and he performs them consecutively, and does not interrupt them with speech. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 2:505] Al-Ma'la: it is from the upper pass of Kada' with fatha and madd, the upper pass at the top of Mecca near the cemetery, and it is indeclinable due to being proper and feminine, and that area is called al-Ma'la, and the pilgrims have abandoned this in these days. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi adapted 730] And takbir and tahlil: i.e. when seeing the honored House, and its meaning: Allah is greater than the Ka'ba and unity, lest some type of shirk occur. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 730] And it is answered, and tawaf of arrival, even if not in the months of Hajj, and idtiba' in it, and ramal for the out-of-town person if he performs sa'y after it in the months of Hajj, and harwalah between the two green milestones for men, and walking returning to ramal and harwalah in a sedate manner in the rest of the sa'y, and increasing tawaf, and it is better than supererogatory prayer for the out-of-town person, and the khutbah after zuhr prayer on the seventh day of Dhu al-Hijjah in Mecca, and it is one sermon without sitting before it, teaching the rites in it, and going out after sunrise on the day of tarwiyah, which is the eighth of Dhu al-Hijjah, from Mecca to Mina, and spending the night there, then going out after sunrise on the day of Arafah to Arafat, then the imam gives two sermons after noon before the zuhr and asr prayers combined with zuhr as jam' taqdim, sitting between them, and striving in supplication, humility, and weeping with tears, and supplicating for oneself, parents, and believing brothers for whatever one wishes of the matters of this world and the Hereafter in the two gatherings. And idtiba' is that he places his garment under his right armpit and throws it over his left shoulder. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 2:508] And ramal: it is walking quickly with close steps and shaking the shoulders in the first three [circuits] as an established sunnah; if he leaves or forgets in the first three, he does not do ramal in the remaining, and if people crowd him, he stops until he finds a gap. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 730] The two green milestones: they are two things shaped like two milestones carved from the same wall of the Sacred Mosque, but separate from it, and they are markers for the place of harwalah in the passage of the valley floor between Safa and Marwah. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 2:515] In a sedate manner: i.e. with tranquility and dignity, from hawn (gentleness). (al-Inayah) For the out-of-town person: as for others, i.e. the resident of the Haram, if it is the season of Hajj, supererogatory prayer is better than tawaf, and at other times, tawaf is also better for him. Day of tarwiyah: it is said that it is named thus because Ibrahim, peace be upon him, on the night of tarwiyah saw as if someone said to him: Allah commands you to slaughter this son of yours. When morning came, he considered (tarawwa) i.e. thought about it from morning until afternoon, [wondering] is this command from Allah or from Satan? Hence it was named day of tarwiyah. Then in the evening he saw the like of it, so he knew it was from Allah, hence it was named day of Arafah. Then he saw the like of it on the third night and resolved to slaughter him, so the day was named day of Nahr. And it is said that it was named day of tarwiyah because people water themselves (yarwun) against thirst on this day, carrying water in water-skins to Arafat and Mina, and day of Arafah was named thus because Jibril, peace be upon him, taught Ibrahim, peace be upon him, all the rites on the day of Arafah, saying to him: Do you know ('arafta) in which place to circumambulate? In which place to perform sa'y? In which place to stand? In which place to slaughter and throw? He said: I know ('araftu). So it was named day of Arafah. [al-Inayah 2:368]
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage from 'Nur al-Idah' lists the sunnahs (recommended acts) of Hajj according to the Hanafi school. The author begins by mentioning the prohibition of killing game while in ihram, but quickly moves to enumerate the sunnahs. The sunnahs include: performing ghusl (or wudu if ghusl is not possible) before ihram, wearing two new white garments, applying perfume on the body (not on the garment), praying two rak'ahs before ihram, reciting the talbiyah aloud and increasing it especially at certain times, sending blessings on the Prophet, asking for Paradise, seeking refuge from the Fire, bathing for entering Mecca, entering from the high gate of al-Ma'la, reciting takbir and tahlil upon seeing the Ka'bah, and supplicating. Then he mentions tawaf al-qudum (arrival tawaf), which is sunnah even outside the Hajj months, and details the sunnah acts within tawaf like idtiba' (wrapping the upper garment under the right armpit) and ramal (quick walking with shoulder movement in the first three rounds). The passage also covers the area between the two green milestones where harwalah (a fast walk) is sunnah for men during sa'y, then walking calmly for the rest. It states that increasing tawaf is better than supererogatory prayer for non-residents of the Haram. For those residing in the Haram during the season, nafl prayer is better; otherwise tawaf is better. The passage then describes the sunnahs of the days: the khutbah on the 7th of Dhu al-Hijjah, going to Mina on the 8th (yawm al-tarwiyah), spending the night there, going to Arafat on the 9th after sunrise, the imam giving two sermons combining zuhr and asr, and engaging in supplication. Finally, the passage provides detailed definitions of idtiba', ramal, the two green milestones, and a historical etymology of the names 'tarwiyah' and 'Arafah' based on the story of Prophet Ibrahim. The commentary draws from authoritative Hanafi sources like al-Bahr al-Raiq, Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, and al-Inayah. Students should note that these are sunnah acts—not obligatory—so omission does not invalidate the Hajj, but one loses the reward.

Key Terms
الاضطباع (al-idtiba'): To place the upper garment under the right armpit and throw it over the left shoulder, leaving the right shoulder uncovered.
الرمل (al-ramal): Quick walking with close steps and moving the shoulders, done in the first three circuits of tawaf for men.
الهرولة (al-harwalah): A fast walk between the two green milestones during sa'y between Safa and Marwah for men.
يوم التروية (yawm al-tarwiyah): The 8th of Dhu al-Hijjah; pilgrims go to Mina and spend the night. The name is derived from Ibrahim's deliberation or from watering.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a person who omits the ramal (quick walking) in the first three circuits of tawaf?
A) He must repeat the tawaf.
B) He should perform ramal in the remaining circuits.
C) He does not do ramal in the remaining circuits; it is not compensated.
D) He must offer a sacrifice (dam).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi sunnah acts of Hajj are recommended practices that enhance the pilgrimage; they are not obligatory, so their omission does not require sacrifice or invalidation.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Sunan of Tawaf and Sa'i
Listing sunan of tawaf and sa'i with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the sunan of tawaf and sa'i and identify their specific conditions according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The sunan of tawaf and sa'i enhance the pilgrimage; they include raml, idtiba', and harwala with conditions based on pilgrim type and timing.

This lesson outlines the recommended acts (sunan) of tawaf (circumambulation) and sa'i (walking between Safa and Marwah) as taught in the Hanafi school. These acts, such as idtiba' and raml, are not obligatory but hold great virtue. Understanding when and for whom they apply—such as the distinction between an afaqi (non-Makkan) and a Makkan resident—ensures they are performed correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunan of tawaf
List the recommended acts mentioned for tawaf: tawaf al-qudum, idtiba', and raml (with conditions).
Tawaf al-qudum is sunnah even outside Hajj months.
2
Note the conditions for raml
Raml is sunnah only for the afaqi if he will perform sa'i afterward during the Hajj months.
If raml is forgotten in the first three circuits, it is not made up.
3
Identify the sunan of sa'i
List the recommended acts for sa'i: harwala between the two green markers (for men) and walking at a steady pace for the rest.
The two green markers are carved stone markers on the valley floor.
4
Understand the superiority of tawaf
For an afaqi, tawaf is superior to nafl prayer; for a Makkan resident, nafl prayer is superior during Hajj season, otherwise tawaf is better.
5
Review definitions from commentaries
Read the definitions of idtiba', raml, and the green markers from the commentaries to solidify understanding.
Idtiba': place garment under right arm, over left shoulder.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سنن الحج وسنية وهو مستجاب، وطواف القدوم، ولو في غير أشهر الحج والاضطباع فيه، والرمل للأفاقي إن سعى بعده في أشهر الحج والهرولة فيما بين الميلين الأخضرين للرجال، والمشي راجع إلى الرمل والهرولة على هيئة في باقي السعي، والإكثار من الطواف، وهو أفضل من صلاة النفل للآفاقي. والاضطباع هو أن يدخل ثوبه تحت يده اليمنى، ويلقيه على عاتقه الأيسر. [البحر الرائق: ٥٠٨/٢] والرمل : هو المشي بسرعة مع تقارب الخُطا وهز الكتفين في الثلاثة الأول استنانا، فلو ترك أو نسيه في الثلاثة الأول لم يرمل في الباقي، ولو زحمه الناس وقف حتى يجد فرجة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٣٠] الميلين الأخضرين هما شيئان على شكل الميلين منحوتان من نفس جدار المسجد الحرام، إلا أنهما منفصلان عنه، وهما علامتان لموضع الهرولة في ممر بطن الوادي بين الصفا والمروة. [البحر الرائق: ٥١٥/۲] على هيئة أي على السكينة والوقار، فعلة من الهون. (العناية) للآفاقي: وأما غيره، وهو المقيم بالحرم ، فإن كان زمن الموسم فالنفل أفضل من الطواف، وفي غيره الأفضل له الطواف أيضا.
The recommended acts of Hajj: and it is sunnah and it is mustajab; the tawaf of arrival, even outside the months of Hajj; idtiba' (placing the upper garment under the right armpit and over the left shoulder) during it; raml (quick walking with shoulder movement) for the afaqi (non-Makkan) if he performs sa'i after it in the months of Hajj; harwala (quick pace) between the two green markers for men; walking [normally] returning from raml and harwala in the remaining part of sa'i; performing tawaf abundantly, which is superior to supererogatory prayer for the afaqi. Idtiba' is to place his garment under his right armpit and throw it over his left shoulder. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 2/508] Raml is walking quickly with close steps and shaking the shoulders in the first three [circuits] as sunnah; if he leaves it or forgets it in the first three, he does not perform raml in the remaining [circuits]; and if people crowd him, he stops until he finds a gap. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 730] The two green markers are two objects shaped like miles carved from the wall of the Sacred Mosque, but they are separate from it; they are markers for the place of harwala in the passage of the valley floor between Safa and Marwah. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 2/515] 'At a steady pace' means with tranquility and dignity, derived from 'hawn' (gentleness). (al-'Inayah) For the afaqi: as for other than him, i.e., the resident of the Haram, if it is the season of Hajj, then supererogatory prayer is superior to tawaf; otherwise, tawaf is superior for him.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage lists the sunan (recommended acts) of tawaf (circumambulation) and sa'i (walking between Safa and Marwah) in Hajj. It begins by stating that tawaf qudum (arrival tawaf) is sunnah, and it is performed even outside the months of Hajj. Idtiba' (wrapping the ihram under the right arm and over the left shoulder) is sunnah during this tawaf. Raml (quick walking with short steps and shoulder movement) is sunnah for the afaqi (a pilgrim from outside Makkah) in the first three circuits of tawaf, provided he follows it with sa'i during the Hajj months. If he misses raml in the first three circuits, he does not make it up in the remaining circuits. Harwala (quick pace) is sunnah for men only between the two green markers on the Safa-Marwah course during sa'i; the rest of sa'i is performed at a normal, dignified pace. The passage emphasizes that increasing tawaf is superior to supererogatory prayer for the afaqi. For a resident of Makkah, during the Hajj season, nafl prayer is better than tawaf; otherwise, tawaf is better. The passage then provides detailed definitions from the commentaries: idtiba' and raml with conditions, and the identification of the two green markers as carved stone markers at the valley floor. As for the meaning of 'steady pace', it denotes tranquility and gravity.

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (tawaf al-qudum): The first tawaf performed upon arriving in Makkah for Hajj or 'Umrah.
الاضطباع (al-idtiba'): Placing the upper garment under the right armpit and over the left shoulder, leaving the right shoulder bare.
الرمل (al-raml): Quick walking with short steps and shoulder movement, performed in the first three circuits of tawaf.
الهرولة (al-harwala): Quick pace between the two green markers in sa'i, men only.
الآفاقي (al-afaqi): A pilgrim who comes from outside the Miqat boundaries, i.e., non-Makkan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on raml for an afaqi pilgrim who forgets to perform it in the first three circuits of tawaf?
A) He must repeat the first three circuits with raml.
B) He does not perform raml in the remaining circuits.
C) He performs raml in the remaining circuits but without the shoulder movement.
D) His tawaf is invalid and must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
The sunan of tawaf and sa'i, including idtiba', raml, and harwala, are conditional based on pilgrim type and timing; missing them does not invalidate the ritual.

Sunnan of Hajj: From the 7th to the 9th of Dhul Hijjah
Describing recommended acts and their spiritual context

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the recommended acts from the khutbah on the 7th to the wuquf at Arafat on the 9th and explain their significance.

Core Idea
The sunan from the 7th to the 9th of Dhul Hijjah—khutbah, Mina stay, and Arafah focus—complete the Prophet's practice.

This lesson covers the sunan (recommended acts) from the 7th of Dhul Hijjah, when the imam delivers a special khutbah, through the 8th (Yawm al-Tarwiyah) and the 9th (Yawm Arafah). These acts are not obligatory but highly rewarded; performing them follows the Sunnah of the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Guided Path
1
Identify the sequence of sunan
Go through the passage and list each recommended act in chronological order: khutbah on 7th, departure to Mina on 8th, night in Mina, departure to Arafat on 9th, two khutbahs at Arafat, and supplication.
These are sunan, not wajibat or arkan.
2
Understand the etymology of the days
The passage explains why the 8th is called Yawm al-Tarwiyah (from Ibrahim's deliberation) and the 9th Yawm Arafah (from recognition). This aids memorization and spiritual connection.
The name helps recall the events.
3
Differentiate sunan from obligations
Note that these acts are sunnah muakkadah; omitting them does not invalidate Hajj but reduces reward. Compare with arkan like wuquf at Arafat which is obligatory.
Sunnan are meritorious but not required for validity.
4
Apply the sequence to a pilgrimage plan
Visualize a pilgrim's timeline: attend khutbah on 7th after Zuhr, travel to Mina on 8th after sunrise, sleep there, travel to Arafat on 9th after sunrise, listen to khutbahs, and make du'a.
This practical sequence helps in planning one's own Hajj.

الخطبة بعد صلاة الظهر يوم سابع الحجة بمكة، وهي خطبة واحدة بلا وكره قبله جلوس يعلم المناسك فيها، والخروج بعد طلوع الشمس يوم التروية من هو ثامن ذي الحجة مكة لمنى، والمبيت بها، ثم الخروج منها بعد طلوع الشمس يوم عرفة إلى عرفات، فيخطب الإمام بعد الزوال قبل صلاة الظهر والعصر مجموعة جمع تقديم مع الظهر خطبتين حال من العصر يجلس بينهما، والاجتهاد في التضرع والخشوع والبكاء بالدموع، والدعاء للنفس والوالدين والإخوان المؤمنين بما شاء من أمر الدارين في الجمعين. يوم التروية: قيل: إنما سمي بذلك؛ لأن إبراهيم الما رأى ليلة التروية كأن قائلا يقول له: إن الله يأمر بذبح ابنك هذا، فلما أصبح تروى أي تفكر في ذلك من الصباح إلى الرواح، أ من الله تعالى هذا الحكم أم من الشيطان؟ فمن ثمه سمي يوم التروية، فلما أمسى رأى مثل ذلك، فعرف أنه من الله تعالى، فمن ثم سمي يوم عرفة، ثم رأى مثله في الليلة الثالثة فهم بنحره، فسمي اليوم بيوم النحر. وقيل: إنما سمي يوم التروية بذلك؛ لأن الناس يروون بالماء من العطش في هذا اليوم، ويحملون الماء بالروايا إلى عرفات ومنى، وإنما سمي يوم عرفة به؛ لأن جبريل عليه علم إبراهيم عليها المناسك كلها يوم عرفة، فقال له أعرفت في أي موضع تطوف؟ وفي أي موضع تسعى؟ وفي أي موضع تقف؟ وفي أي موضع تنحر وترمي؟ فقال: عرفتُ فسمي يوم عرفة [العناية: ٣٦٨/٢] والدفع بالسكينة والوقار بعد الغروب من عرفات والنزول بمزدلفة مرتفعا عن بطن الوادي بقرب جبل قزح والمبيت بما ليلة النحر بمنى أيام منى بجميع أمتعته، وكره تقديم ثقله إلى مكة إذ ذاك، ويجعل منى عن يمينه ومكة عن يساره حالة الوقوف لرمي الجمار، وكونه راكبا حالة رمي جمرة العقبة في كلّ الأيام، ما شيا في الجمرة الأولى التي تلى المسجد، والوسطى، والقيام في بطن الوادي حالة الرمي، وكون الرمي في مسجد الخيف اليوم الأول فيما بين طلوع الشمس وزوالها، وفيما بين الزوال وغروب الشمس في باقي الأيام، وكره الرمي في اليوم الأول والرابع فيما بين طلوع الفجر والشمس، و كره في الليالي الثلاث، وصح؛ لأن الليالي كلّها تابعة لما بعدها من الأيام إلا الليلة التي تلي عرفة حتى صح فيها الوقوف بعرفات وهي ليلة العيد، وليالي رمي أي تأتي ! بعد يوم عرفة فإنها تابعة لما قبلها، والمباح من أوقات الرمي ما بعد الزوال إلى غروب الشمس من اليوم الأول، وبهذا علمت أوقات الرمي كلها جوازا وكراهة واستحبابا، الثلاث؛ بمزدلفة وكلها موقف إلا بطن محسر. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۷۳۱] قزح: بضم ففتح، لا ينصرف للعلمية والعدل عن قازح بمعنى مرتفع، والأصح أنه المشعر الحرام. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٣١] عند عدم إذ ذاك: أي أيام الرمي والمبيت بها ، وظاهر كلامهم أن كراهية التقديم ،تحريمية، وأشار إلى أنه يكره ترك أمتعته بمكة، والذهاب إلى عرفات بالطريق الأولى؛ لأنها العبادة المقصودة، بخلاف الرمي، وينبغي أن يكون محل الكراهة في المسألتين الأمن عليها بمكة، أما إن أمن فلا؛ لعدم شغل القلب . [ البحر الرائق: ٥٣٥/٢ وحاشية الطحطاوي]
The khutbah after Zuhr prayer on the seventh day of Dhul Hijjah in Makkah: it is a single khutbah without a break, before it he sits teaching the rites. Then after sunrise on Yawm al-Tarwiyah (the eighth of Dhul Hijjah) he departs from Makkah to Mina and spends the night there. Then after sunrise on Yawm Arafah he goes from Mina to Arafat. The Imam gives two khutbahs after noon, before Zuhr and Asr combined with Zuhr at the earlier time, with a sitting between them. He strives in supplication, humility, weeping, and supplicates for himself, his parents, and believing brothers with whatever he wishes of worldly and religious matters in both gatherings. Yawm al-Tarwiyah: it is said it is named because Ibrahim (upon him peace) saw on the night of Tarwiyah as if a speaker said to him: 'Allah commands you to sacrifice this son of yours.' In the morning he deliberated (tarawa) from morning to evening: is this command from Allah or from Satan? So it was named Yawm al-Tarwiyah. In the evening he saw the same dream, so he knew it was from Allah; thus it was named Yawm Arafah. Then he saw the same on the third night and resolved to sacrifice him, so that day was named Yawm al-Nahr. It is also said that Yawm al-Tarwiyah is named because people quench (yarwun) their thirst with water on this day, carrying water skins to Arafat and Mina. Yawm Arafah is named because Jibril (upon him peace) taught Ibrahim the rites on that day, saying: 'Do you recognize (a'raft) in which place to circumambulate? In which place to run? In which place to stand? In which place to sacrifice and stone?' He said: 'I recognized' so it was named Yawm Arafah. [al-'Inayah: 2/368] The departure (daf) from Arafat after sunset with tranquility and dignity, and descending at Muzdalifah in a high place above the valley floor near Jabal Qazh, and spending the night there with all his belongings, and staying at Mina on the days of Mina. He dislikes (makruh) sending his luggage to Makkah at that time. He makes Mina to his right and Makkah to his left when standing for stoning the Jamarat. He is mounted when stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah on all days, but walking for the first Jamarah (which is nearest the mosque) and the middle Jamarah, and standing in the valley floor when stoning. Stoning is in Masjid al-Khayf on the first day between sunrise and noon, and between noon and sunset on the remaining days. Stoning is disliked on the first and fourth days between dawn and sunrise, and disliked during the three nights, but valid, because the nights follow the subsequent days except the night after Arafah (the night of Eid), where standing at Arafat is valid. The nights of stoning after Yawm Arafah follow the preceding days. The permissible time for stoning is after noon until sunset on the first day. From this, all times of stoning are known in terms of permissibility, dislike, and recommendation. The three [nights] at Muzdalifah are all a standing place except Batn Muhassir. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 731] Qazh: with a dammah then fatha, it is diptote for proper noun and for being changed from 'Qazih' meaning high. The correct view is that it is al-Mash'ar al-Haram. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 731] 'At that time' means the days of stoning and staying there. The apparent implication of their words is that the dislike of sending luggage ahead is tahrimi (close to impermissible). He indicated that it is disliked to leave his belongings in Makkah, and even more so to go to Arafat without them, because it is the intended worship, unlike stoning. The place of dislike in both cases is when there is no safety for them in Makkah; if he feels safe, there is no dislike because his heart is not occupied. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 2/535 and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi]
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage details the sunan (recommended acts) from the 7th to the 9th of Dhul Hijjah. It begins with the khutbah on the 7th in Makkah after Zuhr, which is a single khutbah where the khatib teaches the rites. On Yawm al-Tarwiyah (the 8th), after sunrise, the pilgrim goes to Mina and spends the night. On Yawm Arafah (the 9th), after sunrise, he goes to Arafat. The imam delivers two khutbahs after zawal (noon) before combining Zuhr and Asr at the earlier time (jama' taqdim). He emphasizes supplication, humility, and crying. The passage then provides the etymologies of Yawm al-Tarwiyah and Yawm Arafah, linking them to the story of Ibrahim. After sunset on the 9th, the pilgrim departs from Arafat with tranquility (daf) and spends the night at Muzdalifah in a high area near Jabal Qazh (al-Mash'ar al-Haram). On the days of Mina, he stays at Mina with all his belongings. It is disliked to send luggage to Makkah during the stay, but if the belongings are safe, the dislike lifts. The pilgrim stands with Mina on his right and Makkah on his left when stoning. He is mounted for stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah but walks for the first and middle Jamarat, standing in the valley floor. The stoning on the first day (Eid) is between sunrise and noon; on remaining days between noon and sunset. Stoning between dawn and sunrise on the first and fourth days is disliked, and stoning at night is disliked but valid. The note on Qazh explains the diptote name and identifies it as al-Mash'ar al-Haram.

Key Terms
يوم التروية (yawm al-tarwiyah): The eighth day of Dhul Hijjah; the day pilgrims go to Mina.
يوم عرفة (yawm arafah): The ninth day of Dhul Hijjah; the day pilgrims stand at Arafat.
الدفع (al-daf'): The departure from Arafat to Muzdalifah after sunset.
المزدلفة (muzdalifah): A place between Arafat and Mina where pilgrims spend the night of the 10th.
جبل قزح (jabal quzah): A hill in Muzdalifah, identified with al-Mash'ar al-Haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the pilgrim depart from Makkah to Mina on the 8th of Dhul Hijjah?
A) After Fajr prayer
B) After sunrise
C) After Zuhr prayer
D) Before Maghrib

Key Takeaway
The sunan from the 7th to the 9th of Dhul Hijjah—khutbah, Mina, Arafat—are a virtuous sequence that every pilgrim should strive to follow.

Sunnan of Hajj: Departure from Arafat, Muzdalifah, and Stoning Times
Detailing sunan and rulings for daf, Muzdalifah stay, and stoning timings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the recommended acts for departing from Arafat to Muzdalifah, staying there, and the times for stoning the Jamarat.

Core Idea
After Arafat, the sunnah is to depart calmly, stay at Muzdalifah, and stone the Jamarat at prescribed times.

This lesson covers the sunan after sunset on the 9th: the departure (daf) from Arafat to Muzdalifah, spending the night there, and the stoning of the Jamarat during the days of Mina. It also addresses disliked acts such as sending luggage ahead when unsafe.

Guided Path
1
Outline the post-Arafat sequence
After sunset on the 9th, the pilgrim departs from Arafat with tranquility (daf), goes to Muzdalifah, stays in a high place near Jabal Qazh, spends the night, then on the 10th goes to Mina for stoning.
Motion with calm is emphasized.
2
List the stoning times and rulings
On the first day (Eid), stoning is between sunrise and noon. On subsequent days, between noon and sunset. Stoning at dawn or night is disliked but valid.
Dislike is tahrimi or tanzihi based on context.
3
Identify the disliked act of sending luggage
Sending luggage to Makkah during the Mina days is disliked (makruh tahrimi) unless the belongings are safe; if safe, no dislike.
The dislike is due to potential distraction from the rites.

Timings of Rami on the Days of Tashriq
Detailed timing rulings for rami.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi classification of times for stoning the Jamarat on each day of Tashriq and identify which time slots are sunnah, mubah, makruh, or not permissible.

Core Idea
Stoning times are precisely regulated: not all daylight hours are equal and each period has a distinct ruling.

The timing of stoning the Jamarat is not left to general permissibility; the Hanafi school has detailed rulings for each part of the day across the four days of Tashriq. This passage from Nur al-Idah outlines those rulings, distinguishing between disliked (makruh), recommended (sunnah), permissible (mubah), and impermissible (la yajuz) times. Understanding these classifications ensures that the pilgrim performs the wajib act at the correct time and avoids invalidity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four days of rami
Recognize that stoning occurs over four days: the Day of Sacrifice (Yawm al-Nahr) and the three days of Tashriq (11th, 12th, 13th Dhul Hijjah).
The first day is distinct; the second and third are similar; the fourth has an intra-madhhab difference.
2
Classify time slots for the first day
On the first day, note the ruling for each segment: from dawn to sunrise (makruh), sunrise to noon (sunnah), noon to sunset (mubah), and after sunset to dawn (makruh).
Night stoning is permissible but disliked; no penalty for doing so.
3
Classify time slots for the second and third days
On these days, stoning from sunrise to noon is not permissible (la yajuz – invalid and must be repeated). The sunnah time is from noon to sunset. Night stoning is makruh but valid.
The ruling 'la yajuz' indicates invalidity; if done before noon, it must be repeated after noon.
4
Note the ruling for the fourth day (Abu Hanifa's view)
According to Abu Hanifa, stoning is permitted from dawn to sunset, but the time before noon is makruh. The view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is not given in this excerpt; typically they equate the fourth day with the second and third days.
The mufta bihi position follows the Sahibayn: stoning on the fourth day is only valid from noon to sunset.
5
Apply the rulings to a practical scenario
Given a specific time and day, determine the ruling: e.g., stoning at 9 AM on the 12th is not permissible (invalid); stoning at 3 PM on the 11th is sunnah.
Always check the day and time window.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أوقات الرمي إلخ اعلم أن أوقات الرمي أربعة أيام يوم النحر، وثلاثة أيام بعده، ففي الأول وقت مكروه: وهو ما بعد طلوع الفجر إلى طلوع الشمس، ومسنون وهو ما بعد طلوع الشمس إلى الزوال، ومباح: وهو ما بعد الزوال إلى الغروب، وما بعد ذلك إلى طلوع الفجر مكروه، وفي اليوم الثاني والثالث من طلوع الشمس إلى الزوال لا يجوز، وما بعده إلى الغروب مسنون ومن بعد الغروب إلى طلوع الفجر مكروه، فإن رمى بالليل قبل طلوع الفجر جاز، ولا شيء عليه، وأما اليوم الرابع فعند أبي حنيفة : من طلوع الفجر إلى الغروب إلا أن ما قبل الزوال مكروه، =
The timings of stoning, etc. Know that the timings of stoning are four days: the Day of Sacrifice and three days after it. On the first day: a disliked time from dawn to sunrise, a recommended time from sunrise to noon, a permissible time from noon to sunset, and what follows that until dawn is disliked. On the second and third days: from sunrise to noon is not permissible, what follows it to sunset is recommended, and from after sunset to dawn is disliked. If one stoned at night before dawn, it is permissible and nothing is due. As for the fourth day, according to Abu Hanifa: from dawn to sunset, except that what is before noon is disliked. =
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed breakdown of the timings for stoning the Jamarat over the four days of Tashriq. It classifies each time segment as either makruh (disliked), sunnah (recommended), mubah (permissible), or non-permissible. On the first day (Yawm al-Nahr), the time from dawn to sunrise is makruh, from sunrise to noon is sunnah, from noon to sunset is mubah, and night after sunset is makruh. On the second and third days, stoning from sunrise to noon is not permissible (la yajuz), from noon to sunset is sunnah, and night is makruh. If one stoned at night before the next dawn, it is valid with no penalty. For the fourth day, Abu Hanifa’s view is that stoning is permitted from dawn to sunset, but the period before noon is makruh. The passage is cut off before stating the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, but the mention of 'according to Abu Hanifa' indicates an intra-madhhab difference.

Key Terms
أيام التشريق (ayyam al-tashriq): The three days following the Day of Sacrifice (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul Hijjah).
الرمي (al-ramy): The act of throwing pebbles at the Jamarat.
جمرة العقبة (jamrat al-aqabah): The largest Jamarah, near Makkah.
لا يجوز (la yajuz): Not permissible; in this context, it means the act is invalid and must be repeated.
مكروه (makruh): Disliked; the act is valid but earns no reward and is discouraged.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Sunnah.
B) Mubah.
C) Makruh.
D) Not permissible (la yajuz).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has detailed timing classifications for rami: on the first day, dawn-sunrise is makruh, sunrise-noon is sunnah, noon-sunset is mubah; on the second and third days, only noon-sunset is valid (sunnah); on the fourth day, the mufta bihi position follows the Sahibayn: noon-sunset.

Sunan of Movement and Stoning in Hajj
Lists sunan actions for departure and stoning rituals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the sunnah acts related to departure from Arafat, alighting at Muzdalifah, and stoning the Jamarat according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The Hajj rites have specific sunnah practices for movement and stoning that maximize reward when performed with understanding.

This passage from Nur al-Idah enumerates the recommended acts (sunan) during the Hajj journey from Arafat to Mina. These practices enhance the spiritual quality of the pilgrimage and reflect the Prophet's ﷺ way. Understanding them helps pilgrims perform Hajj with completeness and mindfulness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah of departure from Arafat
Note that departing after sunset with tranquility and dignity is sunnah. The pilgrim should not rush or push.
Hanafi school: leaving before sunset is makruh.
2
Identify the sunnah of alighting at Muzdalifah
The pilgrim should alight at Muzdalifah in an elevated area near Mount Qazah, avoiding the bottom of the valley. This is the place where the Prophet ﷺ stayed.
The valley bottom is considered a place of punishment.
3
Identify the sunnah of staying overnight at Mina
It is sunnah to spend the night of the 10th (Yawm al-Nahr) at Mina with all one's belongings. Sending luggage ahead to Makkah during these days is makruh.
This ensures the pilgrim remains focused on the rites.
4
Identify the orientation and posture for stoning
When stoning the Jamarat, one should stand with Mina on the right and Makkah on the left. For Jamrat al-Aqabah, it is sunnah to be mounted; for the first and middle Jamrah, one should walk.
Being mounted for Jamrat al-Aqabah distinguishes it from the others.
5
Identify the sunnah of standing position during stoning
While stoning, it is sunnah to stand in the bottom of the valley (batin al-wadi) for all Jamarat except where otherwise specified.
This position is aligned with the Prophet's practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدفع بالسكينة والوقار بعد الغروب من عرفات والنزول بمزدلفة مرتفعا عن بطن الوادي بقرب جبل قزح والمبيت بما ليلة النحر بمنى أيام منى بجميع أمتعته، وكره فيها تقديم ثقله إلى مكة إذ ذاك، ويجعل منى عن يمينه ومكة عن يساره حالة الوقوف لرمي الجمار، وكونه راكبا حالة رمي جمرة العقبة في كلّ الأيام، ماشيا في الجمرة الأولى التي تلى المسجد، والوسطى، والقيام في بطن الوادي حالة الرمي
And departing with tranquility and dignity after sunset from Arafat, and alighting at Muzdalifah in a high place away from the bottom of the valley near Mount Qazah, and staying overnight on the night of Nahr at Mina during the days of Mina with all his belongings, and it is disliked to send his heavy luggage ahead to Makkah at that time, and to make Mina on his right and Makkah on his left while standing for stoning the Jamarat, and being mounted while stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah on all days, walking for the first Jamrah that is next to the mosque and the middle one, and standing in the bottom of the valley while stoning.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage enumerates the Sunnah (recommended) acts related to movement and stoning in Hajj. It begins with the departure from Arafat after sunset, which should be done with calmness and dignity. Then it mentions alighting at Muzdalifah in an elevated area near Mount Qazah, avoiding the bottom of the valley (which is a place of punishment). Staying overnight at Mina on the night of the 10th (Yawm al-Nahr) with all one's belongings is sunnah. It is makruh (disliked) to send heavy luggage ahead to Makkah during the days of Mina because it distracts the pilgrim. While standing to stone the Jamarat, one should orient himself such that Mina is on his right and Makkah on his left. For stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah, it is sunnah to be mounted (riding), whereas for the first and middle Jamrah, one should walk. Standing in the bottom of the valley (batin al-wadi) during the stoning is also sunnah.

Key Terms
الدفع (al-daf'): Departure from Arafat after sunset on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah.
النزول (al-nuzul): Alighting and staying at Muzdalifah on the night of the 10th.
مزدلفة (Muzdalifah): A place between Arafat and Mina where pilgrims spend the night.
جبل قزح (Jabal Qazah): A mountain in Muzdalifah near which it is sunnah to alight.
الرمي (al-ramy): Stoning the Jamarat pillars with pebbles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The sunan of movement and stoning in Hajj include departing from Arafat after sunset, alighting at Muzdalifah near Jabal Qazah, staying overnight at Mina, and stoning the Jamarat with specific postures and orientations.

Times of Ramy and the Dispute on the Fourth Day
Details permissible, disliked, and recommended times for stoning each day

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time rulings for stoning on each day of Tashriq and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the fourth day, identifying the qiyas used by each side and the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa allows stoning on the fourth day from dawn; the Sahibayn restrict it to after zenith.

The stoning of the Jamarat is a wajib rite of Hajj with precise time windows. This passage from Nur al-Idah details the permissible, disliked, and recommended times for each day. It then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: on the fourth day (13th Dhul Hijjah), Imam Abu Hanifa extends the time from dawn to sunset, while his two leading disciples restrict it to after zenith. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply qiyas (analogy) within the Hanafi school and to recognize how differences in analogy lead to practical differences in rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the time rules for each day
Read the passage carefully. On the first day (Yawm al-Nahr), stoning is between sunrise and zenith (recommended) or between zenith and sunset (permissible). On the remaining days (second, third, fourth), the basic permissible time is after zenith until sunset. Note the special rule for night stoning.
The first day is unique because it is the day of sacrifice.
2
Understand the disliked (makruh) and recommended (masnun) times
Stoning between dawn and sunrise on the first and fourth days is disliked but valid. Stoning after zenith on the fourth day is recommended (masnun). Night stoning on the three nights is also disliked but valid.
Makruh in Hanafi fiqh means the act is valid but contrary to the best practice.
3
Analyze the dispute on the fourth day
The text presents a clear disagreement: Abu Hanifa says the time is from dawn to sunset (with makruh before zenith and masnun after). The two disciples (Sahibayn) say the time is only after zenith, and stoning before is invalid.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, not between madhahib.
4
Examine the analogical reasoning (qiyas)
Abu Hanifa analogizes the fourth day to the first day (Yawm al-Nahr), both being ends of the tashriq period, allowing a broad time window. The Sahibayn analogize to the second and third days, which are strictly after zenith. Identify the asl (original case), far' (new case), and illa (effective cause) for each qiyas.
This is a classic example of how different analogies lead to different rulings.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its consequence
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa, which gives more flexibility. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that a pilgrim who stones before zuhr on the fourth day does so validly (though makruh) and does not need to repeat or sacrifice, whereas according to the Sahibayn he would need to repeat and possibly pay dam.
Knowing the mufta bihi is essential for issuing fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كون الرمي في اليوم الأول فيما بين طلوع الشمس وزوالها، وفيما بين الزوال وغروب الشمس في باقي الأيام، وكره الرمي في اليوم الأول والرابع فيما بين طلوع الفجر والشمس، وكره في الليالي الثلاث، وصح؛ لأن الليالي كلّها تابعة لما بعدها من الأيام إلا الليلة التي تلي عرفة حتى صح فيها الوقوف بعرفات وهي ليلة العيد، وليالي رمي أي تأتي بعد يوم عرفة فإنها تابعة لما قبلها، والمباح من أوقات الرمي ما بعد الزوال إلى غروب الشمس من اليوم الأول، وبهذا علمت أوقات الرمي كلها جوازا وكراهة واستحبابا، ثم قال: وأما اليوم الرابع فعند أبي حنيفة : من طلوع الفجر إلى الغروب إلا أن ما قبل الزوال مكروه، وما بعده مسنون وعندهما وقته ما بعد الزوال، ولا يجوز قبله قياسا على اليوم الثاني والثالث، وأبو حنيفة قاسه على اليوم الأول، فإذا غربت الشمس اليوم الرابع لا يجوز أن يرمي بالليل؛ لأنه قد مضى وقت الرمي، فسقط فعله، ويجب عليه دم للسقوط
The stoning on the first day is between sunrise and zenith, and between zenith and sunset on the remaining days. Stoning is disliked on the first and fourth days between dawn and sunrise, and disliked during the three nights, but valid because all nights are attached to the following day except the night after Arafat. The permissible time for stoning is after zenith to sunset on the first day. As for the fourth day, according to Abu Hanifa, it is from dawn to sunset, except that before zenith is disliked, and after zenith is recommended. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), its time is after zenith, and it is not valid before that, by analogy to the second and third days. Abu Hanifa analogized it to the first day. If the sun sets on the fourth day, stoning at night is not permitted, and a dam (sacrifice) is required for missing it.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage discusses the times of stoning (ramy) over the four days. On the first day (Yawm al-Nahr), the stoning is done between sunrise and zenith (recommended) or between zenith and sunset (permissible). Stoning before sunrise (from dawn) is makruh but valid. On the second and third days, stoning is only permissible after zenith until sunset; before zenith is not valid. Night stoning is makruh but valid for all days except if the sun has set on the fourth day, it is not valid. The key dispute is on the fourth day (13th of Dhul Hijjah): Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the time extends from dawn to sunset, with dislike before zenith, while the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) restrict it to after zenith, analogizing to days 2 and 3. Abu Hanifa analogizes to the first day, allowing a broader window. If one misses stoning on the fourth day until sunset, the stoning is no longer valid, and a dam (penalty sacrifice) is wajib. This dispute illustrates the Hanafi method of qiyas and istihsan.

Key Terms
اليوم الأول (al-yawm al-awwal): Yawm al-Nahr, the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, the first day of stoning.
اليوم الرابع (al-yawm al-rabi'): The 13th of Dhul Hijjah, the last day of stoning.
مكروه (makruh): Disliked; the act is valid but contrary to best practice.
مسنون (masnun): Recommended; acts that the Prophet ﷺ performed regularly.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (goat or sheep) wajib as a penalty for missing an obligatory act of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) From fajr to zuhr only

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accommodates flexibility on the fourth day, accepting stoning from dawn as valid though disliked, based on Abu Hanifa's analogy to the first day.

Additional Sunan Acts in Hajj
Lists six additional sunan acts in Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the six additional sunan acts mentioned in the text and state their specific details.

Core Idea
Six sunan acts complement the pillars and wajibat of Hajj: hadi, khutbah, hastening departure, alighting at Muhassab, drinking Zamzam, and iltizam.

This passage from Nur al-Idah outlines acts that are sunnah (recommended) during Hajj beyond the basic obligations. These acts enhance the spiritual experience and follow the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him). Mastering them helps a pilgrim maximize rewards and avoid negligence.

Guided Path
1
Identify each sunnah act
Read the passage and list the acts introduced by 'ومن السنة'. There are six: hadi for mufrid, khutbah on Nahr, hastening departure, alighting at Muhassab, drinking Zamzam, and iltizam.
The passage also mentions eating from the hadi and pouring Zamzam on oneself as part of the sunan.
2
Note the details of each act
For hadi: it is for the mufrid pilgrim, and one eats from it. For khutbah: it is on the day of Nahr, similar to the first khutbah. For departure: hasten before sunset on the 12th; staying until sunset is disliked but no penalty; staying until dawn of 13th makes stoning wajib. For Muhassab: alight for an hour after leaving Mina. For Zamzam: drink to satiety facing the Kaaba, pour on head and body; intention matters. For iltizam: place chest and face on the Multazam.
3
Understand the consequences of omission
Omitting any sunnah does not invalidate Hajj nor require compensation, but the pilgrim misses reward and deviates from the ideal prophetic practice.
The exception: staying at Mina until dawn of 13th makes stoning wajib (not sunnah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن السنة: هدي المفرد بالحج، والأكل منه ومن هدي التطوع والمتعة والقران ثالثة السنة: الخطبة يوم النحر مثل الأولى يعلم فيها بقية المناسك، وهي خطب الحج، وتعجيل النفر إذا أراده من من قبل غروب الشمس من اليوم الثاني عشر، وإن أقام بها حتى غربت الشمس من اليوم الثاني عشر، فلا شيء عليه، وقد أساء، وإن أقام بمنى إلى طلوع فجر اليوم الرابع لزمه رميه. ومن السنة: النزول بالمحصب ساعة بعد ارتحاله من منى وشرب ماء زمزم والتضلع منه، واستقبال البيت، والنظر إليه قائما والصب منه على رأسه وسائر جسده، وهو لما شرب له من أمور الدنيا والآخرة. ومن السنة التزام الملتزم، وهو أن يضع صدره ووجهه عليه
And among the sunnah: a sacrificial animal for the one performing Hajj ifrad, and eating from it and from the voluntary sacrifice and that of tamattu' and qiran. Third of the sunnah: the sermon on the day of Nahr (10th) like the first, informing the remaining rituals, and these are the sermons of Hajj. And hastening the departure if he wishes, before sunset on the 12th day; if he stays until sunset on the 12th, nothing is upon him, but he has sinned, and if he stays at Mina until dawn of the fourth day, stoning becomes obligatory. And among the sunnah: alighting at Muhassab for an hour after leaving Mina, and drinking Zamzam water to satiety, facing the House, looking at it while standing, pouring it on his head and body, and it is for whatever worldly or religious purpose he drinks it. And among the sunnah: iltizam of the Multazam, which is to place his chest and face upon it.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage lists additional sunan acts in Hajj. First, for a pilgrim performing Hajj ifrad (only Hajj), it is sunnah to bring a sacrificial animal (hadi) and eat from it, as well as from the hadi of tamattu' and qiran (the other two types of Hajj). It is also permissible to eat from a voluntary sacrifice. Second, the khutbah on the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah) is sunnah, similar to the khutbah on the 8th (yaum al-tarwiyah), teaching the remaining rites like ramy, tawaf al-ifadah, etc. Third, regarding departure from Mina: if one wishes to leave early (the 12th evening), it is sunnah to leave before sunset; if one stays until sunset, it is valid but makruh; but if one stays until dawn of the 13th, stoning becomes wajib. Fourth, alighting at Muhassab (a place near Makkah) for an hour after leaving Mina is sunnah. Fifth, drinking Zamzam water to satiety, facing the Kaaba, looking at it while standing, and pouring it on oneself is sunnah. The text notes that drinking Zamzam is for whatever purpose one intends, worldly or religious. Sixth, iltizam of the Multazam (between the Black Stone and the door of the Kaaba) is sunnah, placing the chest and face on it.

Key Terms
هدي المفرد (hady al-mufrid): A sacrificial animal brought by a pilgrim performing Hajj ifrad (Hajj alone, not combined with Umrah).
النفر (al-nafr): Departure from Mina; either the first (12th) or second (13th).
المحصب (al-muhassab): Al-Abtah, a valley near Makkah between Mina and the Kaaba.
الملتزم (al-multazam): The area between the Black Stone and the door of the Kaaba.
زمزم (Zamzam): The well of Zamzam in the Sacred Mosque.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
These six sunan complement the main Hajj rituals; performing them follows the Sunnah and completes the spiritual experience.

Sunnan al-Hajj and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Ramy Timing
Lists sunnah acts of Hajj and records an intra-Hanafi dispute on ramy timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the sunnah acts of Hajj according to the Hanafi school and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the timing of ramy on the 13th of Dhul Hijjah, identifying the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The sunnah acts of Hajj are recommended but omission is blameworthy; ramy on the 13th is valid from sunrise per Abu Hanifa, the relied-upon view.

This passage from Nur al-Idah enumerates the sunnah acts of Hajj, from the sacrifice to visiting the Prophet's ﷺ tomb. It also records a key intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two leading disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, regarding the permissible time for ramy on the fourth day of Tashriq (the 13th of Dhul Hijjah). Understanding these sunnan helps the pilgrim perform Hajj with completeness, while knowing the dispute clarifies the operative fatwa for those who stay beyond the 12th.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah acts listed
Read the passage and note each act described as 'min al-sunnah' – from the sacrifice (hady) to clinging to the curtains of the Kaaba and visiting Madinah.
There are at least eight distinct sunnan mentioned.
2
Understand the hukm level for each sunnah
These acts are sunnah muakkadah (emphatically recommended), not fard or wajib. Omitting them is makruh tanzih (blameworthy) but does not require compensation.
Exception: ramy on the 13th becomes wajib if one stays until dawn of the fourth day.
3
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute on ramy timing
The passage states: Abu Hanifa permits ramy on the 13th from sunrise (like the 10th), while the Sahibayn require after zawal (like the 11th and 12th).
The dispute arises from different analogical reasoning.
4
Analyze the qiyas used by each side
Abu Hanifa analogizes the 13th to the day of Nahr (10th) because both are days of departure (nafr). The Sahibayn analogize it to the 11th and 12th because ramy on those days is after zawal.
The key difference: which day is the more appropriate analog?
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon view in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's, so ramy before zawal on the 13th is valid. The Sahibayn's view is a valid ikhtilaf within the school.
Later Hanafi works (e.g., al-Hidayah, al-Durr al-Mukhtar) adopt Abu Hanifa's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سنن الحج
ومن السنة: هدي المفرد بالحج، والأكل منه ومن هدي التطوع والمتعة والقران ثالثة السنة: الخطبة يوم النحر مثل الأولى يعلم فيها بقية المناسك، وهي خطب الحج، وتعجيل النفر إذا أراده من من قبل غروب الشمس من اليوم الثاني عشر، وإن أقام بها حتى غربت الشمس من اليوم الثاني عشر، فلا شيء عليه، وقد أساء، وإن أقام بمنى إلى طلوع فجر اليوم الرابع لزمه رميه. ومن السنة: النزول بالمحصب ساعة بعد ارتحاله من منى وشرب ماء زمزم والتضلع منه، واستقبال البيت، والنظر إليه قائما والصب منه على رأسه وسائر جسده، وهو لما شرب له من أمور الدنيا والآخرة. ومن السنة التزام الملتزم، وهو أن يضع صدره ووجهه عليه،
=
وما بعده ،مسنون وعندهما وقته ما بعد الزوال، ولا يجوز قبله قياسا على اليوم الثاني والثالث، وأبو حنيفة قاسه على اليوم الأول، فإذا غربت الشمس اليوم الرابع لا يجوز أن يرمي بالليل؛ لأنه قد مضى وقت الرمي، فسقط فعله، ويجب عليه دم للسقوط الجوهرة النيرة: ١٩٣/١] فقط: أي لا يأكل من هدي الجنايات. (حاشية الطحطاوي) وتعجيل النفر: بفتح النون وسكون الفاء، وهو الرجوع، فاليوم الأول يسمى يوم النحر، والثاني: يوم القرّ بالقاف؛ لأن الناس يقرون فيه، واليوم الثالث: النفر الأول، واليوم الرابع يسمى يوم النفر الثاني، واليوم الرابع هو اليوم الثالث عشر [الجوهرة النيرة: ١٩٤/١] بالمخصب بضم ففتحتين: الأبطح، وليست المقبرة منه، وهو موضع بقرب مكة، يقال له: الأبطح ذو حصى، والتحصيب النزول فيه، وذكر في المبسوط": أنه سنة عندنا، حتى لو تركه يصير مسيئا [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٣٢] وشرب ماء زمزم وكيفيته أن يأتي ،زمزم فيستقي بنفسه الماء، ويشربه مستقبل القبلة، ويتضلع منه، ويتنفس فيه مرّات، ويرفع بصره في كل مرة وينظر إلى البيت ويمسح برأسه ووجهه وجسده، ويصب عليه إن تيسر. تبيين الحقائق: ۳۱۸/۲] والتضلع منه : تضلع الرجل امتلأ شبعا وريا. (أقرب الموارد) من أمور الدنيا وقد شربه جماعة من العلماء المطالب جليلة فنالوها ببركته تبيين الحقائق: ٣١٩/٢] الملتزم وهو مابين الحجر وباب البيت. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٣٢]
والتشبث بالأستار ساعة داعيا بما أحب، وتقبيل عتبة البيت، ودخوله بالأدب
هي أسكفة الباب
والتعظيم، ثم لم يبق عليه إلا أعظم القربات، وهي زيارة النبي وأصحابه، فينويها
عند خروجه من مكة من باب سَبيكة من الثَّنِيَّة السفلى، وسنذكر للزيارة فصلا على حدته إن شاء الله تعالى.
Sunnan al-Hajj. From the sunnah: the sacrificial animal of the one performing ifrad is from the sunnah, and eating from it and from the voluntary sacrifice and the sacrifice of tamattu' and qiran. Third of the sunnah: the sermon on the day of Nahr like the first one, in which he teaches the remaining rituals, and they are the sermons of Hajj. And hastening the departure if he wishes before sunset on the twelfth day. And if he stays there until sunset on the twelfth day, nothing is upon him, but he has done wrong. And if he stays in Mina until dawn of the fourth day, ramy is obligatory upon him. From the sunnah: stopping at al-Muhassab for a while after departing from Mina, and drinking the water of Zamzam and drinking one's fill of it, facing the House, looking at it standing, and pouring it over one's head and all his body; it is for whatever he drinks it for of worldly and otherworldly matters. From the sunnah: iltizam of the Multazam, which is to place his chest and face upon it. = And what follows is sunnah. And according to both of them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), its time is after zawal, and it is not permissible before it by analogy to the second and third days. Abu Hanifa analogized it to the first day. So if the sun sets on the fourth day, it is not permissible to ramy at night because the time for ramy has passed, so the act is dropped, and a dam is required for the omission. (Marginal notes on definitions of naqr, Muhassab, drinking Zamzam, Multazam...) And clinging to the curtains for an hour supplicating as he likes, and kissing the threshold of the House, and entering it with respect (al-uskuffa is the threshold), and reverently then nothing remains upon him except the greatest of acts of devotion: the visitation of the Prophet and his companions; so he intends it when leaving Mecca from Bab Subaykah from the lower Thaniyyah, and we will mention a separate chapter on visitation if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage lists the sunnah (recommended) acts of Hajj according to the Hanafi school, followed by an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the timing of ramy on the fourth day of Tashriq (the 13th of Dhul Hijjah). The passage begins by stating that the sacrifice for the one performing ifrad, and eating from it, is sunnah. It then mentions the sermon on the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), which teaches the remaining rituals. Hastening the departure from Mina before sunset on the 12th is sunnah; if one stays until sunset, it is permissible but blameworthy. If one stays in Mina until dawn of the 13th (fourth day), ramy becomes obligatory. Other sunan include stopping at al-Muhassab (al-Abtah), drinking Zamzam water to one's fill facing the qibla and looking at the Kaaba, and performing iltizam at the Multazam (between the Black Stone and the door). Clinging to the Kiswah curtains, kissing the threshold, and entering the Kaaba with respect are also sunnah. Finally, the greatest act is visiting the Prophet's ﷺ tomb and his companions, intending it upon leaving Mecca. Regarding the timing of ramy on the 13th, the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is only after zawal (noon), analogously to the 11th and 12th, while Abu Hanifa says it is like the 10th (from sunrise). If the sun sets on the 13th, ramy is invalid and a dam must be given. The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's view, as indicated by the structure of the text.

Key Terms
الملتزم (al-multazam): The area between the Black Stone and the door of the Kaaba where one presses his chest and face.
المحصب (al-muhassab): A place near Mecca called al-Abtah, where it is sunnah to stop after departing Mina.
النفر (al-nafr): Departure from Mina; the first naft on the 12th (if hastened) and the second on the 13th.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on ramy on the 13th of Dhul Hijjah before zawal according to Abu Hanifa?
A) Valid because it is like the first day
B) Invalid because it is only after zawal
C) Valid only if one is a traveler
D) Invalid because it is haram

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's sunan of Hajj enhance the pilgrimage, and the relied-upon view is that ramy on the 13th is valid from sunrise, following Abu Hanifa's analogy to the day of Nahr.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Preparing for Ihram: Ghusl, Grooming, and Garments
Describes the initial steps before assuming ihram for Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended actions before assuming ihram for Hajj and identify the correct ihram garments for a man.

Core Idea
Before ihram for Hajj, perform ghusl, complete grooming, and wear an unsewn izaar and rida'.

This lesson covers the initial steps when intending Hajj: the miqat, purification, grooming, and the specific garments required. These actions are mostly recommended (mustahabb) but the garments are a condition for valid ihram. Understanding them ensures a proper start to the pilgrimage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the starting point — the miqat
The pilgrim must enter ihram from the designated miqat (e.g., Rabigh). This is a requirement (wajib).
Rabigh is a valley near al-Juhfah; other mawaqit exist for different routes.
2
Perform purification — ghusl or wudu
Ghusl is preferred (mustahabb) but wudu suffices. Even menstruating and postpartum women do ghusl if it does not harm them.
This is for cleanliness and entering the state of ihram in a pure state.
3
Complete grooming and cleanliness
It is recommended to trim nails, mustache, pluck armpit hair, shave pubic hair, and have marital intimacy before ihram. Applying oil (even perfumed) is also recommended.
These acts are mustahabb, not obligatory.
4
Wear the correct ihram garments
A man wears an izaar (lower wrap) and rida' (upper wrap) – new or washed, white preferred. They must be unsewn: no buttons, knots, or stitching.
This is a condition for the validity of ihram for men.
5
Note the exception: women and ghusl
A menstruating or postpartum woman should still perform ghusl for ihram if it does not harm her health.
This is based on the general recommendation of ghusl for ihram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في كيفية تركيب أفعال الحج
إذا أراد الدخول في الحج أحرم من الميقات كرابغ فيغتسل أو يتوضأ، والغسل، وهو أحب للتنظيف، فتغتسل المرأة الحائض والنفساء إذا لم يضرها، ويستحبّ كمال النظافة بقص الظفر والشارب ونتف الإبط وحلق العانة وجماع الأهل، والدهن ولو مطيبا، ويلبس الرجل إزارا ورداء جديدين أو غسيلين والجديد الأبيض أفضل ولا يزره ولا يعقده ولا يخلّله . أي بقطعه
التشبث إلخ هو التعلق، والمراد بالأستار أستار الكعبة إن كانت بحيث ينالها وإلا وضع يديه فوق رأسه مبسوطتين على الجدار ،قائمتين ويجتهد في إخراج الدمع من عينه و لم يذكر المصنف أنه يمشي القهقرى، وذكره في "المجمع" لكن يفعله على وجه لا يحصل منه صدم أو وطء لأحد، وهو باك متحسر على فراق البيت الشريف، وبصره ملاحظ له حتى يخرج من المسجد البحر الرائق: ۵۳۷/۲] :كرابغ هو بكسر الموحدة: واد بين الحرتين،

(أقرب الموارد) النظافة : نظف الشيء - من كرم - نظافة نقي من الوسخ والدنس وحسن وبهؤ، فهو نظيف. (أقرب الموارد) الشارب: هو ما ينبت من الشعر على الشفة العليا من الإنسان أقرب الموارد نتف: نتف الشعر والريش ونحوه: نزعه أقرب الموارد ولا يزره من زر القميص زرّا شد أزراره، وأدخلها في العرى، والزر بالكسر : وهو الحبة تجعل في العروة، والجمع أزرار وزرور أقرب الموارد ولا يعقده بأن يعقد طرفيه ببعضهما. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ۷۳۳] ولا يخلله أي بنحو مخيط يدخله خلاله. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٣٣]
Chapter on how to combine the actions of Hajj. When he intends to enter Hajj, he assumes ihram from the miqat such as Rabigh. He performs ghusl or wudu, and ghusl is more beloved for cleanliness. The menstruating woman and postpartum woman perform ghusl if it does not harm them. Complete cleanliness is recommended by trimming the nails, mustache, plucking the armpit, shaving the pubis, intimacy with his wife, and applying oil even if perfumed. The man wears an izaar and a rida', both new or washed, and the new white is best; he does not button it, nor tie the ends, nor stitch it. (Marginal notes on clinging to the curtains, meaning of Rabigh, nifas, cleanliness, etc.)
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage explains the first steps for performing Hajj. When one intends to begin Hajj, they assume ihram from the designated miqat (e.g., Rabigh, a valley near al-Juhfah). It is recommended (mustahabb) to perform a full ghusl, though wudu is sufficient. Even a menstruating or postpartum woman should perform ghusl if it does not harm her. The text recommends complete grooming: trimming nails, mustache, plucking armpit hair, shaving pubic hair, and marital intimacy (which is permissible before ihram). Applying oil, even if perfumed, is allowed before ihram. For men, the ihram garments are an izaar (lower wrap) and a rida' (upper wrap), which should be new or washed; new white is best. The garments should not be buttoned, tied with knots, or stitched (i.e., they should be seamless). The marginal notes explain that 'clinging to the curtains' described earlier is done by placing hands on the wall if the curtains are not reachable, and one should weep and not push others. The author's mention of not walking backwards is noted from another source. The commentary clarifies the meaning of 'Rabigh' and other terms. This chapter sets the foundation for the Ihram procedure in Hajj.

Key Terms
الميقات (al-miqat): The specific boundary or station where one must enter ihram; Rabigh is one miqat for those not coming via other routes.
الإزار والرداء (al-izaar wa al-rida'): The two-piece unsewn garment for ihram: the izaar wraps the lower body, the rida' covers the upper body.
كرابغ (ka-Rabigh): A miqat near al-Juhfah, a valley between the two lava tracts close to the sea.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Any stitched clothes
D) A traditional thobe

Key Takeaway
Before ihram, perform ghusl, complete grooming, and wear the two-piece unsewn izaar and rida'.
