Preparatory Acts Before Ihram: Ghusl and Clothing
Details the sunan and prohibitions before entering ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunan acts before ihram and identify the prohibitions regarding the ihram clothing according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Ihram preparation is sunnah muakkadah: ghusl, grooming, and wearing two unsewn white cloths without buttons or knots.

Before entering the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah, certain recommended acts ensure physical and spiritual cleanliness. These acts are sunnah muakkadah — highly recommended but not obligatory. This passage from Nur al-Idah outlines the specific sunan (ghusl, trimming nails, shaving pubic hair, etc.) and the correct way to wear the ihram garments, including what to avoid (buttoning, tying, stitching). Understanding these prepares you to practice the sunnah correctly and avoid common misunderstandings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunan acts before ihram
List all acts mentioned as recommended for cleanliness and preparation: ghusl (or wudu), trimming nails, trimming mustache, plucking armpit hair, shaving pubic hair, intercourse with wife, applying oil.
Intercourse is sunnah before ihram for those who can manage, but it is not wajib.
2
Identify the recommended clothing details
The man wears an izār (lower wrapper) and ridā' (upper sheet). They should be new or washed, preferably white. The cloths must not be sewn, buttoned, tied, or pierced with a needle.
These prohibitions ensure the garment remains unsewn as required in ihram.
3
Determine the legal ruling of these acts
All listed acts are sunnah muakkadah. The prohibitions (buttoning, tying, stitching) are makruh tanzihi, not haram. If done, the ihram remains valid but the act is disliked.
No penalty (dam) is required for these makruh acts.
4
Note the exception for women
A menstruating or postpartum woman may perform ghusl if it does not harm her. This shows the sunnah is conditional on lack of harm.
This is specific to women in ritual impurity; for others, ghusl is unconditionally recommended.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a man who ties a knot in his ridā', the ruling is makruh tanzihi; his ihram is valid and no penalty. If he buttons a shirt instead of wearing an unsewn cloth, that would be a greater issue (not allowed).
The prohibition is specific to the two-piece ihram; ordinary sewn clothes are not worn in ihram.

The chapter on Hajj. If he intends to enter Hajj, he performs ihram from the miqat, such as Rabigh. He performs ghusl or wudu; ghusl is preferable for cleanliness. The menstruating woman and the woman in postpartum bleeding perform ghusl if it does not harm her. Complete cleanliness is recommended by trimming the nail, mustache, plucking armpit hair, shaving pubic hair, and intercourse with one's wife; and applying oil even if perfumed. The man wears an izār and a ridā', new or washed, and the new white is best. He does not button it, tie it, or stitch it. 'Tashabbuth' etc. means clinging, and by 'astār' is meant the curtains of the Ka'bah if he can reach them, otherwise he places his hands above his head, extended on the wall, standing, and strives to bring tears from his eyes. The author did not mention walking backward; it is mentioned in al-Majma', but he does it in a way that does not cause pushing or stepping on anyone, while weeping and sorrowful at leaving the noble House, his gaze on it until he leaves the mosque. Al-Bahr al-Rā'iq: 2/537. 'Rabigh' is with kasra of the bā': a valley between two lava fields, near the sea, a little before al-Juhfah on the left of the one going to Makkah. [Hāshiyat al-Tahtāwī: 732] 'Nufasā': with damm of first and fatḥ of second, or fatḥ of first and sukūn of second, or with two fatḥas: she is the woman who has given birth. (Aqrab al-Mawārid) 'Nazāfah': 'nazufa al-shay' - from karama - nazāfatan: pure from dirt and filth, good and beautiful, so it is nazīf. (Aqrab al-Mawārid) 'Shārib': it is the hair that grows on the upper lip of a person. (Aqrab al-Mawārid) 'Natf': plucking hair, feathers, etc.: pulling it out. (Aqrab al-Mawārid) 'Lā yazurruh': from 'zarra al-qamīs', zarrā: he fastened its buttons and inserted them into the buttonholes. 'Zirr' (with kasra): the button that goes into the buttonhole; plural azrār and zurūr. (Aqrab al-Mawārid) 'Lā ya'qiduh': that he ties its two ends together. [Hāshiyat al-Tahtāwī: 733] 'Lā yukhalliluh': i.e., he does not pierce it with something like a needle. [Hāshiyat al-Tahtāwī: 733]
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_statement from Nur al-Idah detailing the recommended acts before entering ihram for Hajj. The author lists the sunan of cleanliness: performing ghusl (or wudu if unable), trimming nails, mustache, plucking armpit hair, shaving pubic hair, and having intercourse with one's wife. These are all to ensure physical purity and are not obligatory. The woman in menses or postpartum bleeding may also perform ghusl if it does not harm her. The man wears two white cloths (izār and ridā'), new or washed, preferably white, and must not button, tie, or stitch them, as these would resemble sewn garments which are prohibited in ihram. If he does any of these, it is makruh but no penalty is required. The commentary explains terms: 'tashabbuth' is clinging to the Ka'bah curtains, and 'Rabigh' is a miqat location. The marginal notes from various sources clarify linguistic meanings. This passage is from the matn and the commentary (tahtawi) expands on it.

Key Terms
الإزار (al-izār): A waist-wrapper worn below the navel, covering the lower body.
الرداء (ar-ridā'): A cloth draped over the shoulders, covering the upper body.
لا يزره (lā yazurruh): He does not button it, meaning he does not fasten the izār or ridā' with buttons.
لا يعقده (lā ya'qiduh): He does not tie the ends of the cloth together.
لا يخلله (lā yukhalliluh): He does not pierce the cloth with a needle or pin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a man ties a knot in his ihram cloth?
A) The ihram is invalid and must be repeated.
B) It is makruh tanzihi, but the ihram is valid and no penalty is required.
C) It is haram and a dam is required.
D) It is recommended to tie the cloth for security.

Key Takeaway
Before ihram, the Hanafi school recommends ghusl and grooming, and requires the ihram cloths to be unsewn, unbuttoned, and untied, with no penalty for minor violations.

Entering Ihram: Intention and Talbiyah
Ruling statement on the sunan, wajibat, and prohibitions of entering ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the required elements for entering ihram and explain the Hanafi position that both intention and talbiyah are necessary.

Core Idea
Ihram requires both intention and talbiyah; intention alone is insufficient.

This lesson unpacks the actions one must perform to properly enter the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah according to the Hanafi school. While some schools accept mere intention, the Hanafi school emphasizes that intention must be accompanied by the talbiyah or an equivalent glorification of Allah. We'll examine the sunan (recommended acts) and the wajibat (obligatory acts) as outlined in the source passage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunan before ihram
List the recommended acts: applying perfume (tatayyub) and praying two rak'ahs. Note the preferred surahs to recite (al-Kafirun and al-Ikhlas).
These are sunnah muakkadah, not obligatory.
2
Understand the role of intention (niyyah)
The intention must be present in the heart. It is the first rukn of ihram. The passage says 'tanwi biha' (you intend by it).
Intention can be made even in Persian if one cannot speak Arabic.
3
Recognize the talbiyah as the second rukn
The talbiyah is the specific declaration that accompanies intention. The passage gives the exact wording and commands not to omit any part.
Additional phrases are sunnah, not obligatory.
4
Apply the rule: both are necessary
The text states 'fa idha labbayta nawiyan fa qad ahramta' – when you recite talbiyah with intention, you have entered ihram. Commentary clarifies that one does not enter by intention alone.
Analogy with prayer: intention alone at takbir is insufficient without the takbir.
5
Note the prohibitions after ihram
After entering ihram, avoid rafath (sexual intercourse/obscene talk), fisq (sin), and disputes. These are mufsidat if committed intentionally.
Rafath includes mentioning intercourse in the presence of women.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن فعل كره ولا شيء عليه، وتطيب وصل ركعتين، وقل: "اللهم إني أريد الحج فيسره لي، وتقبله منّي، ولب دبر صلواتك تنوي بها الحج، وهي: "لبيك اللهم لبيك لا شريك لك لبيك إن الحمد والنعمة والملك لك، لا شريك لك"، ولا تنقص من هذه الألفاظ شيئا، وزد فيها : لبيك وسعديك، والخير كله بيديك لبيك، والرغبى إليك"، والزيادة سنة، فإذا لبيت ناويا فقد أحرمت فاتَّق الرفث: وهو الجماع، وقيل: ذكره بحضرة النساء والكلام الفاحش والفسوق والمعاصي . وتطيب أي أيها الطالب حجا أو عمرة، وقال العيني : وإنما ذكر هذا الفصل بالخطاب تحريضا على تعلم أمور الإحرام واهتماما لشدة الاحتياج إلى معرفته [حاشية الشلبي: ٢٤٩/٢] ركعتين ويقرأ فيهما ما شاء، وإن قرأ في الأولى بفاتحة الكتاب وقل يأيها الكافرون وفي الثانية بفاتحة الكتاب وقل هو الله أحد؛ تبركا بفعله الصلاة والسلام فهو أفضل. [العناية: ۳۳۹/۲] :ولب أمر من التلبية من لبى يلبي: قال: لبيك. تنوي بها إلخ بيان للأكمل، وإلا فيصح الحج بمطلق النية ولو بقلبه بشرط مقارنتها لذكر يقصد به التعظيم كتسبيح وتهليل ولو بالفارسية وإن أحسن العربية والتلبية حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٣٣] إن الحمد إلخ: اختلف في همز "إن الحمد" بعد الاتفاق على جواز الكسر والفتح، واختار في "الهداية" أن الأوجه الكسر على استئناف الثناء، وتكون التلبية للذات وقال الكسائي : الفتح أحسن على أنه تعليل للتلبية أي لبيك؛ لأن الحمد إلخ، ورجح الأول في "فتح القدير" بأن تعليق الإجابة التي لا نهاية لها بالذات أولى منه باعتبار صفة هذا وإن كان استئناف الثناء لا يتعين مع الكسر ؛ الجواز كونه تعليلا مستأنفا كما في قولك: علم ابنك العلم إن العلم نافعه، قال تعالى: وَصَل عَلَيْهِمْ إِنَّ صَلاتَكَ سَكَنْ لَهُمْ ﴾ (التوبة: (۱۰۳)، وهذا مقرر في مسالك العلة . من علم الأصول، لكن لما جاز فيه كل منهما يحمل على الأول؛ لأولويته ولأكثريته، بخلاف الفتح ليس فيه سوى أنه تعليل. [البحر الرائق: ٥٠٠/٢] فقد أحرمت أفاد أنه لا يكون محرما إلا بهما، فإذا أتى بهما فقد دخل في حرمات مخصوصة، فهما عين الإحرام شرعا، وذكر حسام الدين الشهيد أنه يصير شارعا بالنية لكن عند التلبية لا بالتلبية كما يصير شارعا في الصلاة بالنية، لكن عند التكبير لا بالتكبير، ولا يصير شارعا بالنية وحدها قياسا على الصلاة [البحر الرائق: ٥٠١/٢] بحضرة النساء: قيد بحضرتهمن؛ لأن ذكر الجماع في غير حضرتهن ليس من الرفث. [الكفاية: ٣٤٥/٢] والمعاصي: لعل الواو ههنا زيدت من بعض الناسخين والأصل: "الفسوق المعاصي" بغير الواو كما عليه عامة الكتب الفقهية.
If he does that, it is disliked and nothing is upon him. And he applies perfume, prays two rak'ahs, and says: 'O Allah, I intend Hajj, so make it easy for me and accept it from me.' And he recites the talbiyah after his prayers, intending Hajj by it. And it is: 'Labbaik Allahumma labbaik, la sharika laka labbaik, innal hamda wan ni'mata wal mulka laka, la sharika lak.' Do not omit anything from these words, and add to them: 'Labbaik wa sa'daik, wal khairu kulluhu bi yadaika labbaik, war raghba ilaik.' The addition is sunnah. When you have recited the talbiyah with intention, you have entered ihram. So beware of rafath: which is sexual intercourse, and it is said: mentioning it in the presence of women, and obscene speech, and fisq (sin), and disobedience. 'Wa tatayyab' means: O you who seek Hajj or Umrah. Al-‘Ayni said: He only mentioned this section in the second person to encourage learning the matters of ihram and due to the great need for its knowledge. [Hashiyat al-Shalabi: 2/249] Two rak'ahs: he recites in them whatever he wishes, and if he recites in the first Surah al-Fatiha and Surat al-Kafirun, and in the second Surah al-Fatiha and Surat al-Ikhlas, following the Prophet's practice (peace be upon him), it is best. [al-‘Inaya: 2/339] 'Wa labb' is a command from talbiyah, from labba yulabbi: he said: labbaik. 'Tanwi biha' etc. is an explanation of the complete form; otherwise, Hajj is valid with absolute intention even if only in the heart, provided it coincides with a dhikr meant for glorification, such as tasbih or tahlil, even in Persian if he cannot do Arabic, and the talbiyah. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 733] 'Innal hamd' etc.: There is a difference of opinion on the hamza of 'inna' after agreement on the permissibility of kasr and fath. In al-Hidaya, it is chosen that kasr is preferable as an independent praise, and the talbiyah is for the essence. Al-Kisa’i said: fath is better as it is a cause for the talbiyah, i.e., labbaik because the praise etc. In Fath al-Qadir, the first is preferred because linking the unlimited response to the essence is better than to an attribute. Although independent praise is not determined with kasr, it is possible as an independent cause, as in your statement: 'Teach your son knowledge, for knowledge benefits him.' Allah said: 'And pray for them, indeed your prayer is a comfort for them' (9:103). This is established in the methods of cause from usul. But since both are permissible, it is taken as the first due to its priority and frequency. As for fath, it is only a cause. [al-Bahr al-Ra’iq: 2/500] 'Fa qad ahramta' indicates that one is not in ihram except with both (intention and talbiyah). When he performs both, he has entered into specific prohibitions; they are the essence of ihram legally. Husam al-Din al-Shahid mentioned that one becomes a pilgrim by intention at the time of talbiyah, not by the talbiyah itself, just as one enters prayer by intention at the time of takbir, not by the takbir. One does not enter by intention alone, by analogy with prayer. [al-Bahr al-Ra’iq: 2/501] 'Bi hadrat al-nisa’' is a condition specific to their presence; because mentioning intercourse not in their presence is not rafath. [al-Kifaya: 2/345] 'Wal ma'asi': perhaps the waw here was added by some copyists, and the original is 'al-fusq al-ma'asi' without waw, as in most fiqh books.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_statement continuing the actions before and at the moment of entering ihram. First, it clarifies that if one previously buttoned, tied, or stitched the ihram cloth, it is makruh but no penalty. Then it lists the sunan: applying perfume (even if scented), praying two rak'ahs (preferably reciting al-Fatiha with al-Kafirun and al-Ikhlas), and making intention by reciting the talbiyah. The talbiyah is the essential declaration for entering ihram. The exact wording is given: 'Labbaik Allahumma labbaik...' and it is recommended to add extra phrases. One must intend Hajj or Umrah with the talbiyah; the intention alone is sufficient if accompanied by a glorification of Allah. The talbiyah and intention together constitute ihram; neither alone suffices. After ihram, one must avoid rafath (sexual intercourse or obscene talk), fisq (sin), and arguments. The commentary elaborates on the linguistic nuances of 'inna' and the legal ruling that the Prophet's practice of reciting specific surahs is best. The ikhtilaf about the hamza is noted but the preferred view is kasr. The passage emphasizes that ihram is entered by both intention and talbiyah, not by intention alone, analogously to prayer.

Key Terms
التلبية (at-talbiyah): The declaration 'Labbaik Allahumma labbaik...' recited to enter ihram.
الرفث (ar-rafath): Sexual intercourse or obscene speech, especially in the presence of women.
الفسوق (al-fusūq): Committing sins or disobedience to Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what constitutes entering ihram?
A) Only the intention in the heart.
B) Only reciting the talbiyah.
C) Both the intention and reciting the talbiyah (or equivalent dhikr).
D) Performing two rak'ahs and then reciting the talbiyah.

Key Takeaway
Ihram is entered by combining intention with the talbiyah (or equivalent dhikr); intention alone is insufficient in the Hanafi school.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
15 min
The Rulings of Ihram: Entering, Prohibitions, and Sunnahs
Rulings on ihram, talbiyah, prohibitions, and entry into Makkah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for entering ihram, list the prohibitions and allowances for a muhrim, and identify the preferred wording of the talbiyah.

Core Idea
Ihram requires both intention and talbiyah; the talbiyah's wording is sunnah, and its prohibitions are many.

This passage from Nur al-Idah provides a comprehensive guide to the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah. It covers the recommended preliminaries, the essential combination of intention and talbiyah, the detailed prohibitions, and the sunnah acts upon entering Makkah. Understanding these rulings ensures the pilgrim avoids violations and performs the rites correctly.

Guided Path
1
Entering Ihram
Identify the two essential elements: intention and talbiyah. Note that both are required for ihram. The intention must accompany a glorifying remembrance; the talbiyah is the verbal declaration.
The text states 'fala yakun muhrim illa bihima' (he is not a muhrim except by both).
2
Wording of the Talbiyah
Compare the two readings (kasr and fath) of 'inna al-hamd'. Note the Hanafi preference for kasr based on theological and linguistic grounds: attributing the praise to Allah's Essence rather than to the act of talbiyah.
Al-Hidayah and Fath al-Qadir prefer kasr; al-Kisa'i preferred fath.
3
Prohibitions of Ihram
List the major prohibited acts: rafath (sexual intercourse/obscene speech), fusuq (sins), jidal (disputation), hunting land game, pointing/guiding to game, wearing sewn clothes, covering head/face, applying perfume, shaving or removing hair.
Each prohibition has specific definitions; e.g., rafath includes mentioning intercourse in the presence of women.
4
Allowances and Sunnahs
Identify what is permissible: ghusl, seeking shade under tent/litter, tying a himyan (money belt), reciting talbiyah frequently at set times, raising voice moderately.
Also noted: covering part of the head is prohibited, but placing hands on the nose is allowed.
5
Entry into Makkah
Recognize the sunnah acts: perform ghusl (even for menstruating woman), enter from Bab al-Mu'alla to face the Kaaba, continue talbiyah until reaching Bab al-Salam.
Entry by day is preferred, but night entry is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كيفية تركيب أفعال الحج
فإن فعل كره ولا شيء عليه، وتطيب وصل ركعتين، وقل: "اللهم إني أريد الحج فيسره لي، وتقبله منّي، ولب دبر صلواتك تنوي بها الحج، وهي: "لبيك اللهم لبيك لا شريك لك لبيك إن الحمد والنعمة والملك لك، لا شريك لك"، ولا تنقص من هذه الألفاظ شيئا، وزد فيها : لبيك وسعديك، والخير كله بيديك لبيك، والرغبى إليك"، والزيادة سنة، فإذا لبيت ناويا فقد أحرمت فاتَّق الرفث: وهو الجماع، وقيل: ذكره بحضرة النساء والكلام الفاحش والفسوق والمعاصي
وتطيب أي أيها الطالب حجا أو عمرة، وقال العيني : وإنما ذكر هذا الفصل بالخطاب تحريضا على تعلم أمور الإحرام واهتماما لشدة الاحتياج إلى معرفته [حاشية الشلبي: ٢٤٩/٢] ركعتين ويقرأ فيهما ما شاء، وإن قرأ في الأولى بفاتحة الكتاب وقل يأيها الكافرون وفي الثانية بفاتحة الكتاب وقل هو الله أحد؛ تبركا بفعله الصلاة والسلام فهو أفضل. [العناية: ۳۳۹/۲] :ولب أمر من التلبية من لبى يلبي: قال: لبيك.
تنوي بها إلخ بيان للأكمل، وإلا فيصح الحج بمطلق النية ولو بقلبه بشرط مقارنتها لذكر يقصد به التعظيم كتسبيح وتهليل ولو بالفارسية وإن أحسن العربية والتلبية حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٣٣] إن الحمد إلخ: اختلف في همز "إن الحمد" بعد الاتفاق على جواز الكسر والفتح، واختار في "الهداية" أن الأوجه الكسر على استئناف الثناء، وتكون التلبية للذات وقال الكسائي : الفتح أحسن على أنه تعليل للتلبية أي لبيك؛ لأن الحمد إلخ، ورجح الأول في "فتح القدير" بأن تعليق الإجابة التي لا نهاية لها بالذات أولى منه باعتبار صفة هذا وإن كان استئناف الثناء لا يتعين مع الكسر ؛ الجواز كونه تعليلا مستأنفا كما في قولك: علم ابنك العلم إن العلم نافعه، قال تعالى: وَصَل عَلَيْهِمْ إِنَّ صَلاتَكَ سَكَنْ لَهُمْ ﴾ (التوبة: (۱۰۳)، وهذا مقرر في مسالك العلة . من علم الأصول، لكن لما جاز فيه كل منهما يحمل على الأول؛ لأولويته ولأكثريته، بخلاف الفتح ليس فيه سوى أنه تعليل. [البحر الرائق: ٥٠٠/٢] فقد أحرمت أفاد أنه لا يكون محرما إلا بهما، فإذا أتى بهما فقد دخل في حرمات مخصوصة، فهما عين الإحرام شرعا، وذكر حسام الدين الشهيد أنه يصير شارعا بالنية لكن عند التلبية لا بالتلبية كما يصير شارعا في الصلاة بالنية، لكن عند التكبير لا بالتكبير، ولا يصير شارعا بالنية وحدها قياسا على الصلاة [البحر الرائق: ٥٠١/٢] بحضرة النساء: قيد بحضرتهمن؛ لأن ذكر الجماع في غير حضرتهن ليس من الرفث. [الكفاية: ٣٤٥/٢] والمعاصي: لعل الواو ههنا زيدت من بعض الناسخين والأصل: "الفسوق المعاصي" بغير الواو كما عليه عامة الكتب الفقهية.
والجدال مع الرفقاء والخدم، وقتل صيد البرّ، والإشارة إليه، والدلالة عليه، ولبس المخيط والعمامة والخفين وتغطية الرأس والوجه ومس الطيب، وحلق الرأس والشعر، يجوز الاغتسال والاستظلال بالخيمة والمحمل وغيرهما، وشد الهميان في الوسط، وأكثر التلبية متى صلّيت، أو علوت شرفا، أو هبطت واديا، أو لقيت ركبا، وبالأسحار رافعا صوتك بلا جهد مضر، وإذا وصلت إلى مكة يستحب أن تغتسل، وتدخلها من باب المعلى؛ لتكون مستقبلا في دخولك باب البيت الشريف تعظيما، ويستحب أن تكون ملبيا في دخولك حتى تأتي باب السلام،
وقتل صيد البر : قيد به؛ لأن صيد البحر يجوز للمحرم والإشارة إليه : الإشارة تقتضي الحضرة، والدلالة تقتضي الغيبة (الكفاية) وتغطية الرأس إلخ أي واجتنب تغطيتهما، والمراد بستر الرأس تغطيته بما يغطى به عادة كالثوب، احترازا عن شيء لا يغطى به عادة كالعدل والطبق، ولا فرق بين ستر الكل والبعض والعصابة، ولهذا ذكر قاضي خان في "فتاواه": أنه لا يغطي فاه ولا ذقنه ولا عارضه، ولا بأس بأن يضع يديه على أنفه. [البحر الرائق: ٥٠٣/٢] الطيب: أي واجتنبه مطلقا في الثوب والبدن [البحر الرائق: ٥٠٤/٢] و حلق الرأس إلخ أي واجتنب هذين والمراد إزالة الشعر كيفما كان حلقا وقصا ونتفا وتنوّرا وإحراقا، من أي مكان كان من الرأس والبدن مباشرة أو تمكينا لكن قال الحلبي: ويستثنى منه قطع الشعر النابت في العين، فقد ذكر بعض مشايخنا أنه لا شيء فيه عندنا. [البحر الرائق: ٥٠٤/٢]
والاستظلال استظل بالظل مال إليه وقعد فيه أقرب الموارد والمحمل هو بفتح الميم الأولى وكسر الثانية أو وهو مقيد بما إذا لم يصب ولا وجهه، فلو أصاب أحدهما يكره كما لو حمل ثيابا على رأسه فإنه يلزمه الجزاء، بخلاف ما إذا حمل نحو الطبق والإجانة والعدل المشغول [البحر الرائق: ٥٠٥/٢] الهميان هو بالكسر، ما يجعل فيه الدراهم ويشد على الحقوة أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان فيه نفقته أو نفقة غيره؛ لأنه ليس بلبس المخيط ولا في معناه وأشار إلى أنه لا يكره شد المنطقة والسيف والسلاح والتختم بالخاتم. البحر الرائق: ٥٠٥/٢] رافعا إلخ : اعلم أن رفع الصوت بالتلبية سنة، إلا أنه لا يجهد نفسه كما يفعله العوام. البحر الرائق: ٥٠٥/٢] تغتسل: اعلم أن من الاغتسالات المسنونة الاغتسال لدخولها وهو للنظافة، فيستحب للحائض والنفساء، ولم يقيد دخول مكة بزمن خاص، فأفاد أنه لا يضره ليلا دخلها أو نهارا، وأما المستحب فالدخول نهارا. [البحر الرائق: ٥٠٦/٢]
How to combine the actions of Hajj: If he does (the recommended acts), it is disliked and nothing upon him. He should apply perfume and pray two rak'ahs and say: 'O Allah, I intend Hajj, so make it easy for me and accept it from me.' And say the talbiyah after your prayers intending Hajj by it, and it is: 'Here I am, O Allah, here I am. No partner do You have. Here I am. Indeed, all praise, blessing, and sovereignty are Yours. No partner do You have.' Do not omit any of these words, and add to them: 'Here I am, and at Your service, and all good is in Your hands. Here I am, and longing is to You.' The addition is sunnah. When you have said the talbiyah intending (Hajj), you have entered ihram. So beware of rafath: it is sexual intercourse, and some say: mentioning it in the presence of women, and obscene speech, and fusuq (disobedience) and sins. 'Apply perfume' means O you who seek Hajj or Umrah. Al-'Ayni said: This chapter is mentioned in the second person to encourage learning the matters of ihram and to emphasize the extreme need to know it. [Hashiyat al-Shalabi: 2/249] Two rak'ahs: recite in them whatever you wish, and if he recites in the first Surah al-Fatihah and 'Say, O disbelievers', and in the second Surah al-Fatihah and 'Say, He is Allah, One', seeking blessing by his (the Prophet's) action, may peace and blessings be upon him, that is best. [Al-'Inayah: 2/339] 'And say the talbiyah' is an imperative from talbiyah; from labba yalubbu: he said 'labbaika'. 'Intending by it' etc. is clarification of the complete way, otherwise Hajj is valid with absolute intention even in the heart, provided it accompanies a remembrance intended for glorification, like tasbih or tahlil, even in Persian if he knows Arabic well, and the talbiyah. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 733] 'Indeed, all praise' etc.: There is a difference of opinion about the hamzah of 'inna al-hamd' after agreement on the permissibility of kasr and fath. In al-Hidayah, it is chosen that kasr is more appropriate as a renewed praise, and the talbiyah is for the Essence. Al-Kisa'i said: Fath is better as a cause for the talbiyah, i.e., 'I am here because all praise...' The first was preferred in Fath al-Qadir because attributing the answer that has no end to the Essence is more appropriate than considering the attribute. And although renewed praise is not specific with kasr, it is permissible as an independent explanation, as in your saying: 'Teach your son knowledge; indeed, knowledge benefits him.' Allah said: 'And pray for them; indeed, your prayer is a comfort for them' (9:103). This is established in the methods of cause from usul al-fiqh. But since both are permissible, it is taken to the first due to its priority and prevalence, unlike fath which is solely a cause. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 2/500] 'You have entered ihram': It indicates that he is not a muhrim except by both (intention and talbiyah). So when he performs them, he has entered into specific prohibitions. They are the essence of ihram legally. Husam al-Din al-Shahid mentioned that he becomes a starter (in ihram) with the intention but at the time of talbiyah, not by the talbiyah itself, just as he becomes a starter in prayer with the intention but at the time of takbir, not by the takbir. He does not become a starter by intention alone, by analogy with prayer. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 2/501] 'In the presence of women': restricted to their presence because mentioning intercourse outside their presence is not rafath. [Al-Kifayah: 2/345] 'And sins': perhaps the 'waw' here is added by some copyists, and the original is 'al-fusuq al-ma'asi' without waw, as in most fiqh books. And disputes with companions and servants, hunting land game, pointing to it, guiding to it, wearing sewn garments, turban, khuffayn, covering the head and face, touching perfume, shaving the head and hair. It is permissible to perform ghusl, seek shade under tent, litter, and others, and to tie the himyan around the waist, and to increase talbiyah whenever you pray, or ascend a high place, or descend a valley, or meet a caravan, and in the early dawn, raising your voice without harmful exertion. When you reach Makkah, it is recommended to perform ghusl and enter from Bab al-Mu'alla so that you face the door of the noble House when entering, as a veneration. And it is recommended that you be saying talbiyah upon entering until you reach Bab al-Salam. 'Hunting land game': restricted to land because sea game is permissible for the muhrim. 'Pointing to it': pointing requires presence, and guiding requires absence. (Al-Kifayah) 'Covering the head' etc. i.e., avoid covering them. What is meant by covering the head is covering it with what is normally used for covering like a cloth, excluding something not normally used like a large basket or plate. There is no difference between covering all, part, or with a headband. Hence Qadi Khan mentioned in his Fatawa: He does not cover his mouth, chin, or cheek, and there is no harm in placing his hands on his nose. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 2/503] 'Perfume': i.e., avoid it absolutely in clothes and body. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 2/504] 'Shaving the head' etc. i.e., avoid these two. What is meant is removing hair in any manner: shaving, cutting, plucking, depilatory, burning, from any place on head or body, directly or by allowing (someone else). But al-Halabi said: cutting hair growing in the eye is an exception; some of our teachers mentioned that there is nothing (sin) upon him for it according to us. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 2/504] 'Seeking shade': seeking shade means inclining towards it and sitting in it. Minhaj al-Mawarid. 'Al-Mahmil' is with fath of the first meem and kasr of the second, and it is restricted to when it does not touch his head or face. If it touches one of them, it is disliked, just as if he carries clothes on his head, then compensation is required, unlike carrying a plate, basin, or loaded basket. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 2/505] 'Al-Himyan' is with kasr, the thing in which dirhams are placed and tied around the waist. It is general, so it includes whether it contains his expenses or another's expenses because it is not wearing sewn garments nor in its meaning. It indicates that tying a belt, sword, weapon, and wearing a ring are not disliked. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 2/505] 'Raising' etc.: Know that raising the voice in talbiyah is sunnah, but he should not exert himself as the common people do. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 2/505] 'Perform ghusl': Know that among the recommended baths is the bath for entering (Makkah), which is for cleanliness, so it is recommended for the menstruating woman and the woman in post-partum bleeding. Entry into Makkah is not restricted to a specific time, so it indicates that it does not harm him whether he enters by night or day. As for the recommended, it is entering by day. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 2/506]
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah details the method of entering ihram for Hajj, the wording of the talbiyah, and the prohibitions and allowances for the muhrim. The author first instructs the pilgrim to apply perfume and pray two rak'ahs before ihram, reciting specific surahs (al-Kafirun and al-Ikhlas) as a sunnah following the Prophet's practice. The talbiyah is the verbal declaration of intention, and it must accompany the intention in the heart. The Hanafi scholars differ on the correct reading of 'inna al-hamd'—whether with kasra (indicating a new sentence) or fatha (as a cause). The majority prefer kasra based on linguistic and theological grounds, connecting the praise directly to Allah's Essence rather than to the action of talbiyah. The text clarifies that merely having the intention without the talbiyah does not constitute ihram, but both are necessary. The prohibitions for the muhrim are then listed: rafath (sexual intercourse or its mention in the presence of women), fusuq (sins), jidal (disputation with companions and servants), killing land game, pointing to or guiding towards it, wearing sewn clothes, turban, khuffayn, covering the head and face, applying perfume, and shaving or cutting hair. These are all prohibited. However, some acts are permissible: performing ghusl, seeking shade under a tent or litter, tying a himyan (money belt) around the waist, and reciting talbiyah frequently especially at times of prayer, ascending high places, descending valleys, meeting caravans, and at dawn. The voice should be raised but without straining. Upon reaching Makkah, it is recommended to take a bath for cleanliness (even for a menstruating woman), enter from Bab al-Mu'alla to face the Kaaba, and continue the talbiyah until reaching Bab al-Salam. The commentary resolves that covering the head includes any conventional headwear, but covering part of it is also prohibited; however, placing hands on the nose is allowed. Shaving hair by any method from any part of the body is forbidden, except for the hair inside the eye, which some scholars exempt. The himyan is not considered sewn clothing, and tying a belt or sword is also permissible. Raising the voice in talbiyah is sunnah but should not be excessive.

Key Terms
إحرام (ihram): The state of ritual consecration for Hajj or Umrah, entered by intention and talbiyah, which renders certain actions prohibited.
تلبية (talbiyah): The verbal declaration 'labbaika Allahumma labbaik...' recited upon entering ihram and thereafter.
رفث (rafath): Sexual intercourse or its mention in the presence of women; also includes obscene speech.
فسوق (fusuq): Disobedience and sins, including but not limited to prohibited acts during ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is required for a person to enter the state of ihram for Hajj?
A) Intention alone in the heart
B) Reciting the talbiyah alone
C) Both intention and the talbiyah
D) Praying two rak'ahs and applying perfume

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, ihram for Hajj is established by the combination of intention and talbiyah, with the talbiyah recited in the preferred wording with kasr.

Prohibitions and Permissions in Ihram
Lists prohibitions and permissions during ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between prohibited and permissible actions for a Muhrim, and state the specific rulings, conditions, and exceptions for each category.

Core Idea
A Muhrim must avoid specific acts; but many daily necessities like bathing and shade are allowed, with careful conditions.

This passage from Nur al-Idah enumerates the actions forbidden and permitted for a person in ihram. Understanding these distinctions is essential for performing Hajj or Umrah correctly. The author provides detailed conditions for each ruling, drawing from the authoritative Hanafi texts, particularly Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. We will parse the list carefully, noting the exceptions and the rationale behind each rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main categories
The passage opens with a list of prohibitions (mahzurat) then states permissible acts. Note the transition word 'يجوز' (it is permissible). Categorise each act as haram or mubah/sunnah.
The prohibitions include: killing land game, pointing to it, indicating it, wearing sewn garments, turban, khuffs, covering head and face, touching perfume, shaving hair. Permitted: bathing, shade, himyan belt, talbiyah.
2
Analyse the prohibition on covering the head
The text specifies that covering the head is prohibited only with a customary covering (like a garment), not with unusual items like a basket or tray. Also note that covering part of the head is included, and the face is included, but placing hands on the nose is allowed.
This nuance prevents misunderstanding that any object on the head is prohibited.
3
Examine the exception for hair removal
Hair removal in any form (shaving, cutting, plucking, etc.) is prohibited, except for hair growing in the eye according to some Hanafi scholars. This is a specific exception with scholarly difference.
This shows that rulings may have well-considered exceptions.
4
Understand the conditions for taking shade
Taking shade is permissible as long as the shade does not cover the head or face directly. If it does, a penalty is required, analogous to carrying clothes on the head.
The condition is that the shade-providing object must not act as a hat-like covering.
5
Recognize the rationale for the himyan belt
The himyan (money belt) is permissible because it is not a sewn garment tailored to the body. It is tied around the waist like a belt, which is not in the category of al-makheet. This principle extends to other similar items like swords and rings.
This helps apply the rule to modern equivalents like a money belt or a fanny pack.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كيفية تركيب أفعال الحج كتاب الحج والجدال مع الرفقاء والخدم، وقتل صيد البرّ، والإشارة إليه، والدلالة عليه، ولبس المخيط والعمامة والخفين وتغطية الرأس والوجه ومس الطيب، وحلق الرأس، والشعر، يجوز الاغتسال والاستظلال بالخيمة والمحمل وغيرهما، وشد الهميان في الوسط، وأكثر التلبية متى صلّيت، أو علوت شرفا، أو هبطت واديا، أو لقيت ركبا، وبالأسحار رافعا صوتك بلا جهد مضر، وقتل صيد البر : قيد به؛ لأن صيد البحر يجوز للمحرم والإشارة إليه : الإشارة تقتضي الحضرة، والدلالة تقتضي الغيبة (الكفاية) وتغطية الرأس إلخ أي واجتنب تغطيتهما، والمراد بستر الرأس تغطيته بما يغطى به عادة كالثوب، احترازا عن شيء لا يغطى به عادة كالعدل والطبق، ولا فرق بين ستر الكل والبعض والعصابة، ولهذا ذكر قاضي خان في "فتاواه": أنه لا يغطي فاه ولا ذقنه ولا عارضه، ولا بأس بأن يضع يديه على أنفه. [البحر الرائق: ٥٠٣/٢] الطيب: أي واجتنبه مطلقا في الثوب والبدن [البحر الرائق: ٥٠٤/٢] و حلق الرأس إلخ أي واجتنب هذين والمراد إزالة الشعر كيفما كان حلقا وقصا ونتفا وتنوّرا وإحراقا، من أي مكان كان من الرأس والبدن مباشرة أو تمكينا لكن قال الحلبي: ويستثنى منه قطع الشعر النابت في العين، فقد ذكر بعض مشايخنا أنه لا شيء فيه عندنا. [البحر الرائق: ٥٠٤/٢] ومس رأسه عكسه، والاستظلال استظل بالظل مال إليه وقعد فيه أقرب الموارد والمحمل هو بفتح الميم الأولى وكسر الثانية أو وهو مقيد بما إذا لم يصب ولا وجهه، فلو أصاب أحدهما يكره كما لو حمل ثيابا على رأسه فإنه يلزمه الجزاء، بخلاف ما إذا حمل نحو الطبق والإجانة والعدل المشغول [البحر الرائق: ٥٠٥/٢] الهميان هو بالكسر، ما يجعل فيه الدراهم ويشد على الحقوة أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان فيه نفقته أو نفقة غيره؛ لأنه ليس بلبس المخيط ولا في معناه وأشار إلى أنه لا يكره شد المنطقة والسيف والسلاح والتختم بالخاتم. البحر الرائق: ٥٠٥/٢] رافعا إلخ : اعلم أن رفع الصوت بالتلبية سنة، إلا أنه لا يجهد نفسه كما يفعله العوام. البحر الرائق: ٥٠٥/٢]
How to arrange the actions of Hajj. Book of Hajj: and disputing with companions and servants, and killing game of the land, and pointing to it, and indicating it, and wearing sewn garments, turban, khuffs, covering the head and face, touching perfume, shaving the head and hair. It is permissible: bathing, taking shade under a tent, howdah, etc., tying the hemian belt in the middle, and increasing the talbiyah whenever you pray, or ascend a high place, or descend a valley, or meet a caravan, and at dawn raising your voice without harmful effort. Then commentary: 'Killing game of the land': restricted because sea game is permissible for the Muhrim. 'Pointing to it': pointing requires presence, indicating requires absence (Al-Kifayah). 'And covering the head etc.': meaning avoid covering them, and the intent of covering the head is to cover it with what is usually used for covering, like a garment, excluding what is not usually used like a large basket or tray. There is no difference between covering all, some, or part. Qadi Khan mentioned in his Fatawa: he does not cover his mouth, chin, or cheeks, and there is no harm in placing his hands on his nose. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 2/503] 'Perfume': i.e., avoid it absolutely on clothing and body [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 2/504] 'And shaving the head etc.': i.e., avoid these two, and the meaning is removing hair in any manner: shaving, cutting, plucking, depilatory, burning, from anywhere on head or body directly or by enabling; however Al-Halabi said: an exception is cutting hair growing in the eye; some of our scholars mentioned there is no penalty for it according to us. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 2/504] 'And touching his head': opposite. 'And taking shade': seeking shade, leaning towards it and sitting in it. 'The mahmil': is with fath of the first mim and kasr of the second, and it is conditioned that it does not cover his head or face; if it covers either, it is disliked, as if he carries clothes on his head, then he is liable for a penalty, unlike if he carries a tray, basin, or loaded load. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 2/505] 'The himyan': with kasr, the item in which dirhams are placed and tied around the waist; it is general and includes whether he has his own expenses or someone else's; because it is not wearing sewn garments nor in its meaning. And he indicated that tying a belt, sword, weapon, and wearing a ring are not disliked. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 2/505] 'Raising etc.': know that raising the voice with talbiyah is sunnah, but he should not exert himself as the common people do. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 2/505]
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah enumerates the actions prohibited and permitted for a person in the state of ihram. The author lists the major prohibitions: hunting land game, pointing to it, indicating it, wearing stitched garments, turban, khuffs (leather socks), covering the head and face, touching perfume, and shaving or cutting hair. These are all forbidden. He then lists permissible acts: bathing, seeking shade under a tent or howdah, tying a money belt (himyan) around the waist, and increasing the talbiyah (chant) at appropriate times. The commentary explains each item in detail, drawing from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. For example, the prohibition on covering the head includes any customary covering like a garment, but not unusual objects like a basket. A notable point is that a Muhrim may place his hands on his nose without covering it. Shaving hair includes all methods of removal, except for a hair growing in the eye, which according to some Hanafi scholars incurs no penalty. Taking shade is permissible as long as the head and face are not covered; if they are, a penalty (jaza) is owed. The himyan belt is allowed because it is not sewn clothing. Raising the voice in talbiyah is sunnah, but without excessive strain.

Key Terms
المخيط (al-makheet): Sewn garments meaning any fabric stitched in a tailored form such as shirts, pants, etc.
المحرم (al-muhrim): A person who has entered the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
الهميان (al-himyan): A money belt or purse tied around the waist to carry coins or expenses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is PERMISSIBLE for a Muhrim (person in ihram)?
A) Wearing sewn garments
B) Covering the head with a turban
C) Bathing and shading under a tent
D) Applying perfume to the body

Key Takeaway
A Muhrim must avoid sewn garments, head covering, perfume, and hair removal, but may bathe, take shade, and use a money belt.

Etiquettes of Entering Mecca and Beginning Tawaf
Describes recommended actions when entering Mecca and performing tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnan actions for entering Mecca and performing tawaf, and apply the rulings on idtiba', kissing the Black Stone, tawaf outside the Hateem, and raml in sa'y.

Core Idea
The pilgrimage begins with sunnan that teach humility: from the bath to the Black Stone, every step has a prescribed grace.

This passage from Nur al-Idah (with commentary from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) details the recommended actions for a pilgrim upon entering Mecca and starting the tawaf. These sunnan are not merely optional extras—they are the Prophet's way of preparing the heart for the sacred rites. Understanding them ensures you worship with both knowledge and devotion.

Guided Path
1
Start with the sunnah bath
Know that bathing before entering Mecca is a recommended bath even for a woman in menses or post-natal bleeding (though she cannot perform tawaf). Enter the mosque humbly, reciting dhikr and sending blessings.
The bath is for cleanliness and is sunnah muakkadah.
2
Face the Black Stone with reverence
Upon seeing the Kaaba, face the Black Stone, raise hands as in prayer, and kiss it without sound. If unable without harm, gesture from afar while saying takbir and tahlil.
Kissing is sunnah; causing harm is not allowed.
3
Perform tawaf with idtiba'
Begin tawaf by the door, taking to the right. Place the upper garment under the right armpit, leaving the right shoulder bare. Perform seven circuits outside the Hateem.
Idtiba' is sunnah for men only.
4
If sa'y follows, perform raml
If you intend sa'y right after tawaf, do raml (quick walking with shoulder movement) in the first three circuits. If crowded, stop and resume—unlike kissing the Stone, raml has no alternative.
Raml is sunnah for men; women do not do it.
5
Note the Hateem's ruling
The Hateem is not part of the Kaaba; tawaf must be outside it. It contains graves of Hajar and Isma'il (AS). Only six cubits from the House are from the original Kaaba.
Tawaf inside the Hateem would be invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تغتسل: اعلم أن من الاغتسالات المسنونة الاغتسال لدخولها وهو للنظافة، فيستحب للحائض والنفساء، ولم يقيد دخول مكة بزمن خاص، فأفاد أنه لا يضره ليلا دخلها أو نهارا، وأما المستحب فالدخول نهارا. [البحر الرائق: ٥٠٦/٢] فتدخل المسجد الحرام منه متواضعا خاشعا ملبيا ملاحظا جلالة المكان مكبرا مهللا مصليا على النبي متلطفا بالمزاحم داعيا بما أحببت فإنه مستجاب عند رؤية البيت المكرم، ثم استقبل الحجر الأسود مكبرا مهللا رافعا يديك كما في الصلاة، وضعهما على الحجر وقبله بلا صوت، فمن عجز عن ذلك إلا بإيذاء، تركه، ومس الحجر بشيء وقبله أو أشار إليه من بعيد مكبرا مهللا حامدا مصليا على النبي، ثم طف آخذا عن يمينك مما يلي الباب مضطبعا، وهو أن تجعل الرداء تحت الإبط الأيمن وتلقي طرفيه على الأيسر، سبعة أشواط داعيا فيها بما شئت، وطف وراء الحطيم، وإن أردت أن تسعى بين الصفا والمروة عقب الطواف فارمل في الثلاثة الأشواط الأول، وهو المشي بسرعة مع هز الكتفين كالمبارز يتبختر بين الصفين، فإن زحمه الناس وقف، فإذا وجد فرجة رمل لابد له منه فيقف حتى يقيمه على الوجه المسنون، بخلاف استلام الحجر الأسود؛ لأن له بدلا وهو استقباله، متلطفا : أي إذا زاحمه أحد من الحجاج يتلطف بهم داعيا لحديث عطاء أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال إذا لقي البيت: "أعوذ برب البيت من الدين والفقر ومن ضيق الصدر وعذاب القبر تبيين الحقائق: ٢٦٦/٢] وقد ذكر في المناقب أن أبا حنيفة له أوصى رجلا يريد السفر إلى مكة بأن يدعو الله عند مشاهدة البيت باستجابة دعائه، فإن استجيبت هذه الدعوة صار مستجاب الدعوة البحر الرائق: ٥٠٦/٢ وزيلعي] الحطيم: اعلم أن الحطيم له ثلاث أسام: حطيم، وحظيرة وحجر، وهو اسم لموضع متصل بالبيت من الجانب الغربي بينه وبين البيت فرجة؛ وسمي به لأنه حطم من البيت أي كسر، فعيل بمعنى مفعول كالقتيل بمعنى المقتول، أو لأن من دعا على من ظلمه فيه حطمه الله كما جاء في الحديث فهو بمعنى فاعل، وليس كله من البيت بل مقدار ستة أذرع من البيت برواية مسلم عن عائشة لها، وفي غاية البيان: أن فيه قبر هاجر وإسماعيل عليهما السلام البحر الرائق: ٢٦٦/٢] وقد ذكر في المناقب أن أبا حنيفة له أوصى رجلا يريد السفر إلى مكة بأن يدعو الله عند مشاهدة البيت باستجابة دعائه، فإن استجيبت هذه الدعوة صار مستجاب الدعوة البحر الرائق: ٥٠٦/٢ وزيلعي] كالمبارز إلخ: هو الذي يبرز من صف القتال لقتال العدو، فإنه يظهر جلادته وقوته لمن بارزه
Bathing: know that among the recommended baths is the bath for entering Mecca and it is for cleanliness, so it is recommended for a menstruating woman and a woman in post-natal bleeding. The time of entering Mecca is not restricted to a specific time, so it is permissible to enter at night or day, but recommended during the day. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 2/506] Then you enter the Sacred Mosque from it humbly, submissively, reciting talbiyah, observing the grandeur of the place, saying Allahu Akbar and la ilaha illallah, sending blessings on the Prophet, being gentle with those crowding, supplicating as you wish, for it is answered upon seeing the honored House. Then face the Black Stone saying Allahu Akbar and la ilaha illallah, raising your hands as in prayer, placing them on the stone and kissing it without sound. Whoever is unable to do so except by causing harm, leaves it. And touch the stone with something and kiss it, or gesture towards it from afar saying Allahu Akbar, la ilaha illallah, praising Allah, sending blessings on the Prophet. Then perform tawaf taking to your right, by the side of the door, with idtiba' (placing the upper garment under the right armpit and throwing its ends over the left shoulder) for seven circuits, making any supplication you wish. And perform tawaf outside the Hateem. If you wish to perform sa'y between Safa and Marwah after tawaf, then perform raml in the first three circuits — walking quickly with shoulder movements like a wrestler strutting between the two rows; if people crowd him, he stops, and when he finds a gap, he must do raml; he stops until he resumes it in the prescribed manner, unlike touching the Black Stone because it has an alternative: facing it. Then commentary: 'Being gentle': i.e., if someone from the pilgrims crowds him, he should be gentle with them, supplicating based on the hadith of Ata that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said when meeting the House: 'I seek refuge with the Lord of the House from debt, poverty, distress of chest and punishment of the grave.' [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 2/266] And it is mentioned in Al-Manqib that Abu Hanifah advised a man traveling to Mecca to supplicate to Allah upon seeing the House for the acceptance of his supplication; if this supplication is accepted, he becomes one whose supplication is answered. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 2/506 and Zayla'i] 'The Hateem': know that the Hateem has three names: Hateem, Hadhirah, and Hajar. It is a place adjacent to the House on the western side with a gap between it and the House. It is called Hateem because it was broken (hatam) from the House, meaning it was separated, 'fa'eel' in the sense of 'maf'ool' like 'qateel' meaning killed; or because whoever supplicates against his oppressor there, Allah crushes him as in the hadith, so it is in the sense of a doer. Not all of it is from the House; rather, a distance of six cubits from the House is from the House according to Muslim's narration from Aisha. And in Ghayat al-Bayan: that it contains the graves of Hajar and Isma'il (peace be upon them). [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 2/266] 'Like a wrestler etc.': he is the one who emerges from the fighting line to fight the enemy, for he shows his courage and strength to his opponent.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage outlines the recommended actions (sunan) for a pilgrim entering Mecca and beginning tawaf. The author begins by stating that bathing before entering Mecca is sunnah, and it is recommended even for a menstruating woman or one in postnatal bleeding (though she cannot perform tawaf). The pilgrim should enter the Sacred Mosque with humility and reverence, reciting talbiyah, takbir, and tahlil, and sending blessings on the Prophet. He should be gentle with others in the crowd. Upon seeing the Kaaba, he should face the Black Stone, raise his hands, and kiss it without making a sound. If unable due to crowds or harm, he may simply gesture. He then performs tawaf with idtiba' (right shoulder bare) for seven circuits, keeping the Hateem outside his path. If he intends sa'y, he should do raml (quick walking with shoulder movement) in the first three circuits of sa'y. If crowded, he stops and resumes when possible. Unlike touching the Black Stone, raml has no alternative. The commentary explains that raml cannot be waived; the pilgrim must wait until he can perform it properly. The commentary also gives the definition of Hateem, noting that only six cubits from the House are part of the original structure, and mentions the graves of Hajar and Isma'il therein. A special supplication upon seeing the House is mentioned from Abu Hanifah's advice.

Key Terms
مضطبعا (mudtabi'an): The state of wearing the upper garment (rida) under the right armpit and throwing its ends over the left shoulder, leaving the right shoulder bare.
الرمل (ar-raml): Walking quickly with short steps and shoulder movements resembling a wrestler advancing. It is sunnah for men in the first three circuits of sa'y between Safa and Marwah.
الحطيم (al-Hateem): A curved area adjacent to the Kaaba on the western side, approximately six cubits from the House, not part of the Kaaba but containing graves of Hajar and Isma'il.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a Muhrim do if unable to kiss the Black Stone due to crowds?
A) Push through to kiss it
B) Leave immediately and skip it
C) Gesture towards it from afar
D) Perform tawaf without any action towards it

Key Takeaway
The sunnan of entering Mecca and tawaf are not mere customs but the Prophet's way of cultivating reverence; they have specific rulings that ensure both devotion and compassion.

Method of Tawaf
Step-by-step method of tawaf from entering the mosque to completion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the steps of performing tawaf according to the Hanafi school, including the sunnah actions of idtiba', raml, and the ruling on the Hatim.

Core Idea
Tawaf must be performed behind the Hatim with idtiba' and raml in the first three circuits.

This lesson guides you through the procedure of tawaf as described in the Hanafi matn. You will learn the etiquette of entering the Sacred Mosque, the method of istilam (touching the Black Stone), the importance of the Hatim, and the sunnah actions of idtiba' and raml.

Guided Path
1
Entering the Sacred Mosque
Identify the recommended behaviors: humility, talbiyah, takbir, and supplication upon seeing the Kaaba.
This sets the spiritual tone.
2
Facing the Black Stone
Understand the action of istilam: raising hands, touching and kissing the stone if possible, otherwise pointing from afar.
Touching is sunnah; pointing suffices if crowded.
3
Performing tawaf with idtiba'
Begin tawaf from the right side of the door, with the upper garment under the right armpit (idtiba'), making seven circuits counterclockwise behind the Hatim.
Idtiba' is sunnah for men only during tawaf.
4
Including raml in the first three circuits
In the first three circuits, walk briskly with shoulder movements (raml). If crowded, stop and resume when possible. Raml has no alternative.
Unlike touching the Black Stone, raml cannot be substituted.
5
Concluding tawaf
After seven circuits, touch the Black Stone again, pray two rak'ahs at Maqam Ibrahim or elsewhere in the mosque, and then touch the stone again. This completes Tawaf al-Qudum.
Tawaf al-Qudum is sunnah for those coming from outside the Miqat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فتدخل المسجد الحرام منه متواضعا خاشعا ملبيا ملاحظا جلالة المكان مكبرا مهللا مصليا على النبي متلطفا بالمزاحم داعيا بما أحببت فإنه مستجاب عند رؤية البيت المكرم، ثم استقبل الحجر الأسود مكبرا مهللا رافعا يديك كما في الصلاة، وضعهما على الحجر وقبله بلا صوت، فمن عجز عن ذلك إلا بإيذاء، تركه، ومس الحجر بشيء وقبله أو أشار إليه من بعيد مكبرا مهللا حامدا مصليا على النبي، ثم طف آخذا عن يمينك مما يلي الباب مضطبعا، وهو أن تجعل الرداء تحت الإبط الأيمن وتلقي طرفيه على الأيسر، سبعة أشواط داعيا فيها بما شئت، وطف وراء الحطيم، وإن أردت أن تسعى بين الصفا والمروة عقب الطواف فارمل في الثلاثة الأشواط الأول، وهو المشي بسرعة مع هز الكتفين كالمبارز يتبختر بين الصفين، فإن زحمه الناس وقف، فإذا وجد فرجة رمل لابد له منه فيقف حتى يقيمه على الوجه المسنون، بخلاف استلام الحجر الأسود؛ لأن له بدلا وهو استقباله، ويستلم الحجر كلما مر به ويختم الطواف به وبركعتين في مقام إبراهيم عليه السلام، أو من غير إيذاء حيث تيسر من المسجد، ثم عاد فاستلم الحجر، وهذا طواف القدوم، وهو سنة للآفاقي، ثم تخرج إلى الصفا، فتصعد وتقوم عليها حتى ترى البيت فتستقبله مكبرا مهللا ملبيا مصليا داعيا، وترفع يديك مبسوطتين، ثم تهبط نحو المروة على هيئة، فإذا وصل بطن الوادي سعى بين الميلين الأخضرين سعيا حثيثا، فإذا تجاوز بطن الوادي مشى على هيئة حتى يأتي المروة، فيصعد عليها، داعيا ويقول: لا إله إلا الله وحده لا شريك له له الملك وله الحمد يحي ويميت وهو حي لا يموت، بيده الخير، وهو على كل شيء قدير، لا إله إلا الله، ولا نعبد إلا إياه مخلصين له الدين ولو كره الكافرون، يقول ذلك ثلاث مرات.
Then you enter the Sacred Mosque from it, humble, submissive, saying talbiyah, observing the grandeur of the place, saying takbir, tahlil, sending blessings on the Prophet, being gentle with those crowding, supplicating as you wish, for it is answered upon seeing the Noble House. Then face the Black Stone, saying takbir and tahlil, raising your hands as in prayer, place them on the stone and kiss it without sound. Whoever is unable to do that except by causing harm, leaves it, and touches the stone with something and kisses it, or points to it from afar, saying takbir, tahlil, praising, and sending blessings on the Prophet. Then perform tawaf, taking to your right from the side of the door, with idtiba', which is to place the cloak under your right armpit and throw its ends over the left, seven circuits, supplicating therein as you wish. Perform tawaf behind the Hatim. If you wish to perform sa'i between Safa and Marwa after the tawaf, then do raml in the first three circuits, which is walking quickly with shaking of the shoulders like a fighter swaggering between the two rows. If people crowd him, he stops, and when he finds an opening he does raml; it is necessary for him, so he stops until he establishes it in the sunnah manner. Unlike touching the Black Stone, because it has an alternative, which is facing it. And he touches the stone every time he passes by it, and concludes the tawaf with it and with two rak'ahs at Maqam Ibrahim, peace be upon him, or without harm wherever convenient in the mosque. Then he returns and touches the stone. This is the tawaf of arrival, and it is sunnah for the one coming from afar. Then you go out to Safa, ascend and stand upon it until you see the House, then face it saying takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, sending blessings, and supplicating, raising your hands outstretched. Then descend towards Marwa in a calm manner. When you reach the middle of the valley, you run between the two green markers with vigorous running. When you pass the middle of the valley, you walk in a calm manner until you come to Marwa, ascend upon it, supplicating and saying: There is no god but Allah alone, no partner for Him, His is the kingdom and to Him is praise, He gives life and causes death, and He is living and does not die, in His hand is good, and He is powerful over all things. There is no god but Allah, and we worship none but Him, devoting religion sincerely to Him, even if the disbelievers dislike it. He says this three times.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling statement on the method of performing tawaf (circumambulation) and sa'i (walking between Safa and Marwa) during Hajj or Umrah according to the Hanafi school. The text begins with the etiquette of entering the Sacred Mosque: one should be humble, submissive, saying talbiyah, and mindful of the sanctity of the place. Upon seeing the Kaaba, one should make supplication, as it is answered. Then one faces the Black Stone (Hajar al-Aswad), raises hands as in prayer, and touches and kisses it without sound. If unable due to crowding, one may touch it with an object or point from afar. Tawaf begins from the right side of the door, with the upper garment tucked under the right armpit (idtiba'), making seven circuits counterclockwise. Tawaf must be performed behind the Hatim (the semicircular wall), which is part of the Kaaba. After tawaf, if one intends sa'i, the first three circuits of sa'i should be performed with raml (quick walking with shoulder movements) between the two green markers in the valley, while the rest is at a normal pace. Unlike touching the Black Stone, raml has no alternative; it must be done in the first three rounds even if one has to pause and resume. After completing tawaf, one prays two rak'ahs at Maqam Ibrahim or elsewhere in the mosque, then returns to touch the Black Stone. This tawaf is called Tawaf al-Qudum (tawaf of arrival) and is sunnah for those coming from outside Mecca. Then one proceeds to Safa, ascends, faces the Kaaba, and makes supplications. Descending to Marwa, one walks calmly until the valley, then runs vigorously between the two green markers, and walks calmly again until Marwa. Upon ascending Marwa, one repeats the declaration of tawhid three times. The text emphasizes the sunnah actions and the necessary compensations (like stopping if crowded and resuming raml). All rulings are based on the Hanafi school as transmitted in the authoritative commentaries such as al-Bahr al-Raiq and Tabyin al-Haqa'iq.

Key Terms
مضطبع (muḍṭabiʿ): The state in which the upper garment is placed under the right armpit and its ends are thrown over the left shoulder, leaving the right shoulder uncovered. It is sunnah for men during tawaf.
رمل (raml): Walking quickly with short steps and shaking of the shoulders, resembling a warrior's gait. It is sunnah in the first three circuits of tawaf for men.
حطيم (ḥaṭīm): The semicircular wall adjacent to the Kaaba on the western side; it is considered part of the Kaaba. Tawaf must be performed behind it, not between it and the Kaaba.
طواف القدوم (ṭawāf al-qudūm): The circumambulation performed upon arrival in Mecca for Hajj; it is sunnah for those coming from outside the Miqat.
الميلان الأخضران (al-mīlān al-akhḍarān): Two green markers set in the wall of the Sacred Mosque indicating the area of the valley where running (sa'y) between Safa and Marwa is performed vigorously.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is fard; if omitted, tawaf is invalid.
B) It is sunnah; if unable to touch, one can point from afar.
C) It is wajib; if omitted, a dam is required.
D) It is mustahabb but not sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Qudum is performed with idtiba', raml in first three circuits, behind the Hatim, and includes touching the Black Stone and two rak'ahs after.

Method of Sa'i
Step-by-step method of sa'i from Safa to Marwa, including the vigorous running and supplications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the method of performing sa'i between Safa and Marwa according to the Hanafi school, including the running between the green markers and the recommended supplications.

Core Idea
Sa'i includes walking calmly, running vigorously between the green markers, and repeating the tahlil three times on Marwa.

This lesson explains the procedure for sa'i after tawaf, based on the Hanafi text. You will learn the correct method of ascending Safa and Marwa, the place where running is intensified, and the recommended dhikr.

Guided Path
1
Proceeding to Safa
After tawaf, go out to Safa. Ascend it and stand until you see the Kaaba, then face it and make supplications with raised hands.
The supplication is recommended; there is no specific formula besides what is mentioned.
2
Descending to Marwa
Descend from Safa towards Marwa in a calm manner until you reach the middle of the valley (between the two green markers).
The green markers indicate the area where running is prescribed.
3
Running between the green markers
When you reach the valley, run vigorously (sa'y hasitha) between the two green markers. After passing them, resume walking calmly.
This running is a sunnah for men; women do not run.
4
Completing the ascent on Marwa
Upon reaching Marwa, ascend it and repeat the tahlil and related supplications three times.
The text provides the exact wording of the dhikr.

Counting Laps in Sa'y: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Describes how to perform Sa'y and the intra-Hanafi dispute on what constitutes a lap.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on counting laps in Sa'y, identify the opposing intra-Hanafi view of Imam al-Tahawi, and explain the reasoning based on the nature of Sa'y as linear motion.

Core Idea
In Sa'y, each one-way traversal between Safa and Marwah counts as a separate lap, unlike Tawaf's circular circuits.

This passage from Nur al-Idah describes the performance of Sa'y between Safa and Marwah, but it also reveals an important intra-Hanafi dispute: does a round trip count as one lap, or is each crossing a separate lap? The answer affects how many times you must walk from one hill to the other. Let's examine the issue and the reasoning behind the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
What is the controversy? It concerns what constitutes a single lap (sha'f) in Sa'y: Is the return from Marwah to Safa a separate lap or part of the previous lap?
2
Present the two positions
The majority Hanafi view (al-sahih) holds that each one-way traversal is a lap. Imam al-Tahawi holds that a round trip (Safa→Marwah→Safa) is one lap.
3
Analyze the proof of al-Tahawi
Al-Tahawi analogizes Sa'y to Tawaf. In Tawaf, one circuit from the Black Stone to the Black Stone is a lap. He argues similarly for Sa'y.
Qiyas on Tawaf
4
Examine the Hanafi response
The response distinguishes Tawaf (circular motion) from Sa'y (linear motion). Circular motion necessitates return to start; linear does not.
Ta'lil: the difference in nature of the acts.
5
Identify the tarjih
The text declares 'al-sahih anna sha'f akhar' – the correct view is another lap. This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج
كيفية تركيب أفعال الحج
ويفعل كما فعل على الصفا، يستقبل البيت مكبّرا مهلّلا ملبيا مصليا داعيا باسطا أي على المروة يديه نحو السماء، وهذا شوط، ثم يعود قاصدا الصفا فإذا وصل إلى الميلين الأخضرين ،سعى ثم مشى على هيئة حتى يأتي الصفا، فيصعد عليها، ويفعل كما فعل أولا، وهذا شوط ثان فيطوف سبعة أشواط يبدأ بالصفا ويختم بالمروة، ويسعى في بطن الوادي في كل شوط منها ، ثم يقيم بمكة محرما، ويطوف بالبيت كلما بدا له، أي ظهر له وهو أفضل من الصلاة نفلا للآفاقي، فإذا صلى الفجر بمكة ثامن ذي الحجة تأهب للخروج إلى منى، فيخرج منها بعد طلوع الشمس، ويستحب أن يصلي الظهر بمنى، ولا يترك التلبية في أحواله كلها إلا في الطواف، ويمكث بمنى إلى أن يصلي الفجر بها بغلس، وينزل بقرب مسجد الخيف .
كما فعل :إلخ أي كما فعل على الصفا من الصعود والتكبير والتهليل والصلاة والدعاء، والكل سنة، حتى لو ترك الهرولة بين الميلين لا شيء عليه البحر الرائق: ٥١٥/٢] يستقبل إلخ : هذا باعتبار ما كان، وإلا فقد حال البناء بين المروة والبيت الآن، ولكنه يقف مستقبلا. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٣٤]
وهذا شوط ونقل عن الطحاوي: أن الذهاب من الصفا إلى المروة، والرجوع منها إلى الصفا شوط، قياسا على الطواف، فإنه من الحجر إلى الحجر شوط، وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية" ما يخالفه فإنه قال لا خلاف بين أصحابنا أن الصفا إلى المروة شوط محسوب من الأشواط السبعة، فأما الرجوع من المروة إلى الصفا هل هو شوط آخر؟
الذهاب من
قال الطحاوي: لا يعتبر الرجوع من المروة إلى الصفا شوطا آخر ، والصحيح أنه شوط آخر. [البحر الرائق: ٥١٥/٢] فإن قيل: ما الفرق بين الطواف والسعي حتى كان مبدأ الطواف هو المنتهى دون السعي؟ أجيب بأن الطواف دوران لا يتأتى إلا بحركة دورية، فيكون المبدأ والمنتهى واحدا ،بالضرورة، وأما السعي فهو قطع مسافة بحركة مستقيمة، وذلك لا يقتضي عوده على بدايته العناية: ٣٦٢/٢ والبحر الرائق]
Book of Hajj. Method of arranging the actions of Hajj: He acts as he did on Safa, facing the Kaaba, saying takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, sending blessings, making supplication, extending his hands towards the sky on Marwah. This is one lap. Then he returns heading to Safa. When he reaches the two green markers, he runs (s'a) then walks in his manner until he reaches Safa, ascends it, and does as he did first. This is a second lap. So he completes seven laps, starting at Safa and ending at Marwah, and he runs in the bottom of the valley in each lap. Then he stays in Mecca as a muhrim, and circumambulates the House whenever it appears to him (i.e., whenever he wishes). This is superior to supererogatory prayer for the one from outside the Miqat. When he prays Fajr in Mecca on the 8th of Dhul-Hijjah, he prepares to go out to Mina. He leaves after sunrise, and it is recommended to pray Zuhr at Mina. He does not abandon the talbiyah in all his states except during Tawaf. He stays at Mina until he prays Fajr there in the darkness before dawn, and he descends near the Masjid al-Khayf. 'As fa'ala...' i.e., as he did on Safa of ascending, takbir, tahlil, prayer, supplication—all are Sunnah; even if he leaves the running between the two markers, nothing is upon him. [Bahr al-Raiq 2:515] 'Yastaqbil...' this is according to what was; otherwise the building now intervenes between Marwah and the House, but he stands facing it. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi:734] 'Wa hadha sha'f'—It is transmitted from al-Tahawi that going from Safa to Marwah and returning from Marwah to Safa is one lap, by analogy to Tawaf, since from the Black Stone to the Black Stone is one lap. In al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah, it contradicts that, for he said: There is no disagreement among our companions that Safa to Marwah is one lap counted among the seven laps. As for the return from Marwah to Safa—is it another lap? Al-Tahawi said: The return from Marwah to Safa is not considered another lap. The correct view is that it is another lap. [Bahr al-Raiq 2:515] If it is said: What is the difference between Tawaf and Sa'y so that the beginning of Tawaf is the end, unlike Sa'y? The answer: Tawaf is a rotation that can only be achieved by circular motion, so the beginning and end are necessarily one. As for Sa'y, it is crossing a distance in straight motion, and that does not require returning to its starting point. [al-Inayah 2:362 and Bahr al-Raiq]
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the performance of Sa'y between Safa and Marwah, including a significant intra-Hanafi dispute. The author first describes the practical steps: ascending Safa, facing the Kaaba, making dhikr and supplication, then proceeding to Marwah. One full traversal from Safa to Marwah is counted as one lap. The return from Marwah to Safa constitutes a second lap. However, there is disagreement on whether the return counts as a separate lap. Imam al-Tahawi held that the round trip (Safa->Marwah->Safa) constitutes a single lap, analogizing to Tawaf where one complete circuit starts and ends at the Black Stone. But the relied-upon position (al-sahih) is that the return is a separate lap, so seven traversals from Safa to Marwah are required, making fourteen legs if counting each direction. The commentator clarifies that the difference arises from the nature of the acts: Tawaf is circular, so the start and end are identical; Sa'y is linear, so each crossing is distinct. The mention of 'two green markers' indicates the place where running (raml) is performed in the bottom of the valley. The rest of the passage covers other Hajj actions: staying in Mecca as muhrim, the superiority of Tawaf over extra prayer, and the schedule for the 8th of Dhul-Hijjah.

Key Terms
شوط (sha'f): A lap or traversal in Sa'y or Tawaf. In this passage, it refers to one complete crossing from Safa to Marwah (or Marwah to Safa) in Sa'y.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What constitutes a lap (sha'f) in Sa'y according to the correct Hanafi position stated in the text?
A) One round trip Safa-Marwah-Safa
B) One one-way traversal from Safa to Marwah or from Marwah to Safa
C) One complete circuit from the Black Stone to the Black Stone
D) One round trip plus a supplication

Key Takeaway
In Sa'y, each one-way traversal from Safa to Marwah or vice versa is a separate lap, and seven such traverses are required, ending at Marwah.

Staying in Mecca as Muhrim and the Prohibition of Faskh
States the ruling on staying in Mecca as muhrim and the schedule for the 8th of Dhul-Hijjah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on faskh al-hajj and describe the sunnah actions for the 8th of Dhul-Hijjah (Yawm al-Tarwiyah).

Core Idea
Once you enter Hajj, you must complete it — faskh (converting to 'Umrah) is prohibited.

This passage from Nur al-Idah covers the state of a muhrim after entering Mecca and the recommended schedule for the day of Tarwiyah. A critical ruling is that one cannot terminate ihram early or convert the Hajj to 'Umrah – a practice known as faskh. The passage also highlights the virtue of tawaf over supererogatory prayer for those from outside the Miqat and outlines the sunnah sequence for moving to Mina.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overarching ruling
Find the sentence that states the muhrim must stay in Mecca in ihram until all Hajj actions are completed. Note that this directly implies the prohibition of faskh.
The phrase 'fa afada anna faskh al-hajj ila al-'umrah la yajuz' clarifies the Hanafi position.
2
Extract the sunnah actions for the 8th of Dhul-Hijjah
List the recommended actions: praying Fajr in Mecca, leaving after sunrise, praying Zuhr in Mina, staying overnight, and praying Fajr at Mina in deep darkness near Masjid al-Khayf.
These are mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory.
3
Understand the ruling on tawaf and talbiyah
Note that performing tawaf is superior to supererogatory prayer for the afaqi (one from outside the Miqat). Also, talbiyah is recited continuously except during tawaf.
The superiority of tawaf is specific to the afaqi; residents of Mecca may have different rulings.
4
Comprehend the geography of Mina
Mina is described as a village three miles (farsakh) from Mecca, within the Haram, with three roads. This explains the location for the sunnah actions.
Knowing the area helps contextualize the rituals.
5
Synthesize the practical implications
Combine all rulings: a muhrim cannot leave ihram early, must perform the sunnah sequence on 8th Dhul-Hijjah, and should engage in tawaf and talbiyah as prescribed.
These rulings ensure the Hajj is performed correctly according to the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقيم بمكة محرما، ويطوف بالبيت كلما بدا له، أي ظهر له وهو أفضل من الصلاة نفلا للآفاقي، فإذا صلى الفجر بمكة ثامن ذي الحجة تأهب للخروج إلى منى، فيخرج منها بعد طلوع الشمس، ويستحب أن يصلي الظهر بمنى، ولا يترك التلبية في أحواله كلها إلا في الطواف، ويمكث بمنى إلى أن يصلي الفجر بها بغلس، وينزل بقرب مسجد الخيف .
ثم يقيم بمكة: فلا يجوز له التحلل حتى يأتي بأفعاله، فأفاد أن فسخ الحج إلى العمرة لا يجوز. البحر الرائق: ٥١٦/٢] منى وهي قرية فيها ثلاث سكك، بينها وبين مكة فرسخ، وهي من الحرم والغالب عليه التذكير والصرف وقد يكتب بالألف. [البحر الرائق: ٥١٧/٢]
Then he stays in Mecca as a muhrim, and circumambulates the House whenever it appears to him, i.e., whenever he wishes, and it is superior to supererogatory prayer for the one from outside the Miqat. When he prays Fajr in Mecca on the 8th of Dhul-Hijjah, he prepares to go out to Mina. He leaves after sunrise, and it is recommended to pray Zuhr at Mina. He does not abandon the talbiyah in all his states except during Tawaf. He stays at Mina until he prays Fajr there in the darkness before dawn, and he descends near the Masjid al-Khayf. 'Thumma yuqimu bi Makka': It is not permissible for him to remove his ihram (tahallul) until he performs the actions (of Hajj). Thus it indicates that changing Hajj to 'Umrah (faskh) is not permissible. [Bahr al-Raiq 2:516] 'Mina': It is a village with three roads, between it and Mecca is a farsakh. It is part of the Haram. It is generally treated as masculine and declined, and may be written with an alif. [Bahr al-Raiq 2:517]
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that a muhrim must remain in ihram until completing all Hajj actions. It emphasizes that one cannot perform faskh (converting Hajj to 'Umrah) after entering Hajj. The passage then describes the sunnah actions for the day of Tarwiyah (8th Dhul-Hijjah): leaving for Mina after Fajr, praying Zuhr at Mina, staying overnight to pray Fajr in deep darkness near the Masjid al-Khayf. The commentator notes that Tawaf is superior to supererogatory prayer for the person from outside the Miqat (afaqi). The description of Mina as a village with three streets clarifies its geography. The sentence about talbiyah indicates it should be recited continuously except during Tawaf.

Key Terms
التحلل (al-tahallul): Removing the state of ihram, which is not permitted until all Hajj actions are completed.
فسخ الحج إلى العمرة (faskh al-hajj ila al-'umrah): Converting the intention of Hajj to 'Umrah after entering ihram for Hajj.
منى (Mina): A valley near Mecca where pilgrims stay on the 8th-10th of Dhul-Hijjah. It is within the Haram boundaries.

Key Takeaway
