Conditions for Combining Prayers at 'Arafat
Explains the conditions for performing Zuhr and 'Asr at 'Arafat in jam' (combination) with the Imam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for combining Zuhr and 'Asr at 'Arafat and apply them to scenarios involving ihram type and imam presence.

Core Idea
Combining prayers at 'Arafat requires both Hajj ihram and the Supreme Imam; missing either means each prayer in its time.

On the Day of 'Arafah, pilgrims have a special dispensation to combine Zuhr and 'Asr prayers. However, this is not an unconditional rukhsah; the Hanafi school specifies two precise conditions derived from the Prophet's practice. This lesson unpacks those conditions and their practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize that the act is combining Zuhr and 'Asr at 'Arafat. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih) only when specific conditions are met.
The passage states: 'لا يجمع بينهما إلا بشرطين' (he does not combine them except under two conditions).
2
Extract the two conditions
From the text: (1) ihram for Hajj (not 'Umrah), (2) prayer behind the Supreme Imam (imam al-a'zam) or his deputy.
The term 'الإحرام' is clarified as 'إحرام الحج' in the commentary.
3
Apply conditions to each prayer
Both conditions must be fulfilled for each of the two prayers, not just for 'Asr. The text gives an example: if someone is in ihram for 'Umrah during Zuhr and in Hajj ihram during 'Asr, combination is invalid.
The commentary says: 'وهذان الشرطان لابد منهما في كل من الصلاتين'.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
If either condition is missing, the pilgrim must pray Zuhr and 'Asr in their usual times. For example, if the imam is not present, or if one is in 'Umrah ihram, no combination.
The passage says: 'وإن لم يدرك الإمام الأعظم صلى كل واحدة في وقتها المعتاد'.
5
Note the prohibition of supererogatory prayers
No nafl prayer is allowed between the combined prayers. If done, the adhan for 'Asr must be repeated because the continuity (fawr) is broken.
The commentary clarifies that even the post-Zuhr sunnah is omitted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم بعد طلوع الشمس يذهب إلى عرفات فيقيم بها، فإذا زالت الشمس يأتي مسجد نمرة فيصلي مع الإمام الأعظم أو نائبه الظهر والعصر بعد ما يخطب خطبتين يجلس بينهما، ويصلي الفرضين بأذان وإقامتين ولا يجمع بينهما إلا بشرطين: الإحرام، والإمام الأعظم، ولا يفصل بين الصلاتين بنافلة، وإن لم يدرك الإمام الأعظم صلى كل واحدة في وقتها المعتاد، فإذا صلى مع الإمام يتوجه إلى الموقف، وعرفات كلها موقف إلا بطن عُرْنة ويغتسل بعد الزوال في عرفات للوقوف، ويقف بقرب جبل الرحمة مستقبلا مكبّرا مهلّلا ملبيا داعيا ماذا يديه كالمستطعم،
عرفات: وهي علم للموقف، وهي منونة لا غير، ويقال لها عرفة أيضا، ويوم عرفة التاسع من ذي الحجة. البحر الرائق: ٥١٧/٢] والعصر : أشار بذكر العصر بعد الظهر إلى أنه لا يصلي سنة الظهر البعدية، وهو الصحيح كما في "التصحيح"، فبالأولى أن لا يتنفل بينهما، فلو فعل كره وأعاد الأذان للعصر لانقطاع فوره، فصار كالاشتغال بينهما بفعل آخر البحر الرائق: ٥١٨/٢] الإحرام المراد بالإحرام إحرام الحج حتى لو كان محرما بالعمرة يصلي العصر في وقته عنده وهذان الشرطان لابد منهما في كل من الصلاتين لا في العصر وحدها، حتى لو كان محرما بالعمرة في الظهر محرما بالحج في العصر لا يجوز له الجمع عنده كما لم يكن محرما في الظهر، وأطلق في مسجد عرفة، حتى لقد قال بعض الإحرام، فأفاد أنه لا فرق بين أن يكون محرما قبل الزوال أو بعده، وهو الصحيح. [البحر الرائق: ٥١٩/٢] ولا يفصل إلخ : تصريح بما علم سابقا ضمنا في قوله: "الظهر والعصر. عرنة وفي "المغرب": عرنة واد بحذاء عرفات، وبتصغيرها سميت عرينة ينسب إليها العرنيون، وذكر القرطبي في تفسيره أنها بفتح الراء وضمها بغربي العلماء: إن الجدار الغربي من مسجد عرفة لو سقط سقط في بطن عرنة، وحكى الباجي عن ابن جيب أن عرفة في الحل وعرنة في الحرم. [البحر الرائق: ٥١٩/٢]
Then after sunrise he goes to 'Arafat and stays there. When the sun passes the zenith, he comes to Masjid Namirah and prays Zuhr and 'Asr with the Supreme Imam (imam al-a'zam) or his deputy, after he delivers two sermons with a sitting between them. He prays the two obligatory prayers with one adhan and two iqamahs. He does not combine them except under two conditions: ihram (the state of ihrām for Hajj) and the presence of the Supreme Imam. He does not separate between the two prayers with a supererogatory prayer. If he does not catch the Supreme Imam, he prays each prayer in its usual time. When he prays with the Imam, he proceeds to the place of standing (mawqif). All of 'Arafat is a standing place except the bottom of 'Arnah. He performs ghusl after the zenith at 'Arafat for the standing, and stands near the Mountain of Mercy, facing the Qibla, saying takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, supplicating with his hands like a beggar. 'Arafat: It is a proper noun for the standing place, and it is always nunated. It is also called 'Arafah. The Day of 'Arafah is the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah. [Bahr al-Raiq 2:517] 'Wa al-'Asr': Mentioning 'Asr after Zuhr indicates that he does not pray the post-Zuhr Sunnah, and this is the correct view as in 'al-Tashih'. A fortiori, he should not perform supererogatory prayer between them. If he does, it is disliked and he must repeat the adhan for 'Asr because its immediacy is broken, becoming like engaging in another act between them. [Bahr al-Raiq 2:518] 'Al-Ihram': The intended ihrām is the ihrām for Hajj. Even if he is in ihrām for 'Umrah, he prays 'Asr at its usual time according to Abu Hanifah. Condition: These two conditions are necessary for each of the two prayers, not for 'Asr alone, so that if he is in ihrām for 'Umrah during Zuhr and in ihrām for Hajj during 'Asr, it is not permissible for him to combine according to Abu Hanifah, as he was not in ihrām during Zuhr. The expression 'Masjid 'Arafah' is general, even to the extent that some said: 'Al-Ihram' thus it indicates that there is no difference whether he enters ihrām before zenith or after. This is the correct view. [Bahr al-Raiq 2:519] 'Wa la yafsil...' is a clarification of what was previously implied in his statement 'al-Zuhr wa al-'Asr'. 'Arnah: In 'al-Mughrib', 'Arnah is a valley alongside 'Arafat. In its diminutive form, it is called 'Uraynah, to which the 'Uraniyyun are attributed. Al-Qurtubi mentioned in his Tafsir that it is with fatha or damma on the ra', and it is west of the scholars: The western wall of Masjid 'Arafah, if it fell, would fall into the bottom of 'Arnah. Al-Baji narrated from Ibn Jubayb that 'Arafah is in the Hal (area outside the Haram) and 'Arnah is in the Haram. [Bahr al-Raiq 2:519]
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage details the conditions for combining (jam') Zuhr and 'Asr at 'Arafat. The key conditions are: (1) being in the state of ihrām for Hajj (not 'Umrah), and (2) praying behind the Supreme Imam (imam al-a'zam) or his deputy. If one misses the Imam, one prays each prayer in its normal time. The commentator clarifies that 'Asr is mentioned after Zuhr to indicate that the post-Zuhr Sunnah is omitted, and supererogatory prayers between them are disliked. There is also discussion about the location: 'Arafat is the standing place except for the valley of 'Arnah. The Mountain of Mercy (Jabal al-Rahmah) is the recommended spot for standing. The passage includes a note on the definition of 'Arafat and 'Arnah, with some disagreement about whether 'Arafah is in Hal or Haram. The correct Hanafi position is that the conditions are necessary for both prayers, not just 'Asr, as evidenced by the case where someone enters ihrām for Hajj only before 'Asr.

Key Terms
الإمام الأعظم (al-imam al-a'zam): The Supreme Imam, i.e., the caliph or his appointed deputy who leads the congregational Hajj prayer at 'Arafat. In absence, the prayer is performed normally.
بطن عرنة (batn 'urnah): The valley of 'Arnah, a specific area excluded from the standing place at 'Arafat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a pilgrim is in ihrām for 'Umrah at the time of Zuhr on the Day of 'Arafah?
A) He may combine Zuhr and 'Asr behind the Imam
B) He prays Zuhr in its time and 'Asr in its time (no combination)
C) He delays 'Asr to combine with Maghrib
D) He must perform a different prayer

Key Takeaway
The combination of Zuhr and 'Asr at 'Arafat is valid only when the pilgrim is in Hajj ihrām and prays behind the Supreme Imam; otherwise, each prayer is prayed in its time.

Standing at Arafat: Ruling, Recommended Acts, and Supplication
Ruling and sunnah acts for wuquf at Arafat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the boundaries of the valid standing place at Arafat, identify the sunnah acts during wuquf, and recite the authentic supplication reported from Ibn 'Abbas.

Core Idea
All of Arafat is a valid standing place except the valley of 'Arnah; the sunnah includes ghusl, facing Qibla, and humble supplication.

The standing (wuquf) at Arafat is the pinnacle of Hajj. This lesson covers the exact boundaries of the standing place as defined by the Hanafi school, the recommended actions to perform while standing, and the beautiful supplication taught by the Prophet (peace be upon him) at this blessed location. Understanding these points ensures your wuquf is both valid and spiritually rewarding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on the standing place
Locate the key phrase: 'wa 'Arafat kulluha mawqif illa batn 'urnah' (All of 'Arafat is a standing place except the bottom of 'Arnah). This defines the valid area.
Memorize this exception; it is critical for validity.
2
Understand the recommended actions
Find the sequence: ghusl after zenith, standing near Jabal al-Rahmah, facing Qibla, then takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, and du'a with hands raised like a beggar.
These are sunnah, not obligatory, but highly recommended.
3
Learn the definition of 'Arafat
The text notes that 'Arafat is a proper noun always with tanween, also called 'Arafah, and the day is the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah.
This clarifies linguistic and calendrical precision.
4
Memorize the recommended supplication
The passage includes a lengthy du'a from Ibn 'Abbas describing the Prophet's practice. Focus on the key phrases expressing humility and need.
You may also choose any sincere supplication; this one is a model.

عرفات: وهي علم للموقف، وهي منونة لا غير، ويقال لها عرفة أيضا، ويوم عرفة التاسع من ذي الحجة. البحر الرائق: ٥١٧/٢] والعصر : أشار بذكر العصر بعد الظهر إلى أنه لا يصلي سنة الظهر البعدية، وهو الصحيح كما في "التصحيح"، فبالأولى أن لا يتنفل بينهما، فلو فعل كره وأعاد الأذان للعصر لانقطاع فوره، فصار كالاشتغال بينهما بفعل آخر البحر الرائق: ٥١٨/٢] الإحرام المراد بالإحرام إحرام الحج حتى لو كان محرما بالعمرة يصلي العصر في وقته عنده وهذان الشرطان لابد منهما في كل من الصلاتين لا في العصر وحدها، حتى لو كان محرما بالعمرة في الظهر محرما بالحج في العصر لا يجوز له الجمع عنده كما لم يكن محرما في الظهر، وأطلق في مسجد عرفة، حتى لقد قال بعض الإحرام، فأفاد أنه لا فرق بين أن يكون محرما قبل الزوال أو بعده، وهو الصحيح. [البحر الرائق: ٥١٩/٢] ولا يفصل إلخ : تصريح بما علم سابقا ضمنا في قوله: "الظهر والعصر. عرنة وفي "المغرب": عرنة واد بحذاء عرفات، وبتصغيرها سميت عرينة ينسب إليها العرنيون، وذكر القرطبي في تفسيره أنها بفتح الراء وضمها بغربي العلماء: إن الجدار الغربي من مسجد عرفة لو سقط سقط في بطن عرنة، وحكى الباجي عن ابن جيب أن عرفة في الحل وعرنة في الحرم. [البحر الرائق: ٥١٩/٢]
جبل الرحمة هو الجبل الذي بوسط أرض عرفات يقال له: "إلال" على وزن هلال تبيين الحقائق: ۲۸۹/۲] داعيا إلخ: قال ابن عباس : "رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بعرفات يدعو، ويداه إلى صدره كاستطعام المسكين"، رواه أبو ذر، ويقول: "اللهم اجعل في بصري نورا، وفي سمعي ،نورا، واجعلني ممن تباهى به ملائكتك اللهم اشرح لي صدري ويسر لي أمري، اللهم إنك تسمع كلامي وترى مكاني وتعلم سري وعلانيتي، ولا يخفى عليك شيء من أمري، أنا البائس الفقير المستغيث المستجير المغرور أسألك مسألة المسكين وأبتهل إليك ابتهال المذنب الذليل، وأدعوك دعاء الخائف الحقير، ومن خضعت لك رقبته وفاضت لك عيناه، ورغم لك أنفه، ولا تجعلني بدعائك رب شقيا، وكن بي رؤوفاً رحيما، يا خير مسؤول ، ويا أكرم مأمول". ويختار من الدعاء ما شاء [تبيين الحقائق: ٢٩١/٢]
When he prays with the Imam, he proceeds to the standing place. All of 'Arafat is a standing place except the bottom of 'Arnah. He performs ghusl after the zenith at 'Arafat for the standing, and stands near the Mountain of Mercy, facing the Qibla, saying takbir, tahlil, talbiyah, supplicating with his hands like a beggar. 'Arafat: It is a proper noun for the standing place, and it is always nunated. It is also called 'Arafah. The Day of 'Arafah is the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah. [Bahr al-Raiq 2:517] 'Wa al-'Asr': Mentioning 'Asr after Zuhr indicates that he does not pray the post-Zuhr Sunnah, and this is the correct view as in 'al-Tashih'. A fortiori, he should not perform supererogatory prayer between them. If he does, it is disliked and he must repeat the adhan for 'Asr because its immediacy is broken, becoming like engaging in another act between them. [Bahr al-Raiq 2:518] 'Al-Ihram': The intended ihrām is the ihrām for Hajj. Even if he is in ihrām for 'Umrah, he prays 'Asr at its usual time according to Abu Hanifah. Condition: These two conditions are necessary for each of the two prayers, not for 'Asr alone, so that if he is in ihrām for 'Umrah during Zuhr and in ihrām for Hajj during 'Asr, it is not permissible for him to combine according to Abu Hanifah, as he was not in ihrām during Zuhr. The expression 'Masjid 'Arafah' is general, even to the extent that some said: 'Al-Ihram' thus it indicates that there is no difference whether he enters ihrām before zenith or after. This is the correct view. [Bahr al-Raiq 2:519] 'Wa la yafsil...' is a clarification of what was previously implied in his statement 'al-Zuhr wa al-'Asr'. 'Arnah: In 'al-Mughrib', 'Arnah is a valley alongside 'Arafat. In its diminutive form, it is called 'Uraynah, to which the 'Uraniyyun are attributed. Al-Qurtubi mentioned in his Tafsir that it is with fatha or damma on the ra', and it is west of the scholars: The western wall of Masjid 'Arafah, if it fell, would fall into the bottom of 'Arnah. Al-Baji narrated from Ibn Jubayb that 'Arafah is in the Hal (area outside the Haram) and 'Arnah is in the Haram. [Bahr al-Raiq 2:519] 'Jabal al-Rahmah': It is the mountain in the middle of the land of 'Arafat, called 'Ilal, on the pattern of 'hilal'. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 2:289] 'Da'iyan...': Ibn 'Abbas said: 'I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) at 'Arafat supplicating, his hands to his chest like a beggar asking for food.' Narrated by Abu Dharr. He would say: 'O Allah, place light in my sight, light in my hearing, and make me among those whom Your angels boast about. O Allah, expand my chest and make my affair easy. O Allah, You hear my speech, see my place, know my secret and open, and nothing of my affair is hidden from You. I am the miserable, poor, seeking aid, seeking sanctuary, the deluded. I ask of You as a beggar asks, and I beseech You as the sinful lowly one beseeches. I call upon You as the fearful wretched one calls, and to You has bowed my neck, for You have flowed my tears, and for You has been humbled my nose. Do not make me, O Lord, through my supplication, wretched, and be with me kind and merciful, O best of those who are asked, and O most generous of those who are hoped for.' And he may choose whatever supplication he wishes. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 2:291]
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage provides the sunnah acts for the standing (wuquf) at 'Arafat. After combining the prayers, the pilgrim proceeds to the standing place, which is all of 'Arafat except the valley of 'Arnah. The recommended action is to perform ghusl after zenith (not before), then stand near the Mountain of Mercy (Jabal al-Rahmah) facing the Qibla, engaged in dhikr and du'a with hands raised like a beggar. The text then defines 'Arafat as a proper noun for the standing place, always with tanween. The day is the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah. The commentator includes a detailed supplication reported from Ibn 'Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) describing the Prophet's du'a at 'Arafat. The passage also reiterates rulings about the prayer combination (discussed in previous lesson) and the definition of 'Arnah valley. It emphasizes the excellence of making abundant du'a at this lofty station.

Key Terms
الموقف (al-mawqif): The standing place at 'Arafat, encompassing the entire plain of 'Arafat except for the valley of 'Arnah.
جبل الرحمة (jabal al-rahman): The Mountain of Mercy, a specific hill in the center of 'Arafat, also known as Jabal 'Ilal.

The standing at Arafat is valid everywhere within its boundaries except the valley of 'Arnah, and the sunnah includes ghusl, facing Qibla, and humble supplication with raised hands.

Combining Prayers and Standing at Arafat: Conditions and Practices
Explains the combined prayer, standing, and supplication at Arafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for combining Zuhr and Asr at Arafat and explain the recommended manner of standing and supplication.

Core Idea
Combining prayers at Arafat requires ihram for Hajj and the Imam; wuquf excludes Batn 'Urnah.

The Day of Arafat is the climax of Hajj. The Hanafi school prescribes a unique combined prayer at Masjid Namirah, but only under specific conditions. This lesson unpacks those conditions and the etiquettes of standing in supplication, including the posture of the Prophet ﷺ.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
The passage covers two main acts: the combined Zuhr and Asr prayer, and the standing (wuquf) at Arafat. Determine the ruling for each (sunnah muakkadah for the combination, rukn for wuquf).
The combination is not fard; if conditions are missing, pray each at its time.
2
Locate the conditions for combining
The text states: 'لا يجمع بينهما إلا بشرطين: الإحرام، والإمام الأعظم'. Identify that ihram refers to ihram for Hajj, and the Imam must be the supreme leader or his deputy.
If one is in ihram for Umrah at Zuhr, the combination is invalid according to Abu Hanifa.
3
Trace the dalil for supplication
The passage quotes Ibn Abbas describing the Prophet's posture: 'يداه إلى صدره كاستطعام المسكين'. This hadith establishes the recommended manner of raising hands like a beggar.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear (qati al-dalala).
4
Note the ikhtilaf on the condition of ihram
The commentary mentions that if one is in ihram for Umrah at Zuhr and for Hajj at Asr, Abu Hanifa does not permit the combination, while the Sahibayn differ. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view as affirmed by al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.
5
Apply to a scenario
A pilgrim arrives at Arafat after Zuhr but before Asr, having done ihram for Hajj. The Imam is present. Can they combine? Yes, because both conditions are met. If the Imam is absent, they pray each at its time.
The same conditions apply to both prayers, not only the second.

ويجتهد في الدعاء لنفسه ووالديه وإخوانه ويجتهد على أن يخرج من عينيه قطرات من الدمع، فإنه دليل القبول، ويلح في الدعاء مع قوة رجاء الإجابة، ولا يقصر في هذا اليوم؛ إذ لا يمكنه تداركه سيّما إذا كان من الآفاق، والوقوف على الراحلة أفضل، والقائم على الأرض أفضل من القاعد، فإذا غربت الشمس أفاض الإمام معه والناس على هيئتهم، وإذا وجد فرجة يسرع من غير أن يؤذي أحدا، ويتحرز أي يتوقى عما يفعله الجهلة من الاشتداد في السير والازدحام والإيذاء؛ فإنه حرام، حتى يأتي جمع
Then after sunrise he goes to Arafat and stays there. When the sun declines, he comes to Masjid Namirah and prays Zuhr and Asr with the greatest Imam or his deputy after he delivers two sermons with a sitting between them. He prays the two obligatory prayers with one adhan and two iqamas. He does not combine them except with two conditions: ihram and the greatest Imam. He does not separate between the two prayers with a supererogatory prayer. If he does not catch the greatest Imam, he prays each one at its usual time. When he prays with the Imam, he proceeds to the standing place. All of Arafat is a standing place except the valley of 'Arnah. He performs ghusl after noon at Arafat for the standing. He stands near the Mount of Mercy facing the qibla, saying takbir, tahlil, talbiya, and supplicating, raising his hands like a beggar...
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the actions of Hajj on the day of Arafat, as per the Hanafi school. It begins by describing the combined Zuhr and Asr prayers at Masjid Namirah, stating the two conditions for the combination: being in the state of ihram for Hajj and praying behind the supreme Imam or his deputy. If one misses the Imam, each prayer is prayed in its usual time. After the prayer, the pilgrim proceeds to the standing area (wuquf). All of Arafat is valid for standing except the valley of 'Arnah, which is not part of Arafat. Ghusl after noon is recommended. Standing near the Mount of Mercy is preferred, with facing the qibla, takbir, tahlil, talbiya, and supplication. The passage then quotes the du'a of Ibn Abbas describing the Prophet's posture and includes a lengthy supplication. It also emphasizes earnest supplication, tears, and leaving Arafat after sunset at a calm pace without harming others.

Key Terms
عرفات (Arafat): The specific plain where pilgrims stand on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah; it is a proper noun and is always indefinite (manoona).
جبل الرحمة (Jabal al-Rahmah): The Mount of Mercy, located in the center of Arafat, also called 'Ilal (like Hilal).
بطن عرنة (Batn 'Urnah): The valley adjacent to Arafat; standing there is not valid as part of the wuquf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Combining Zuhr and Asr at Arafat is a sunnah muakkadah that requires ihram for Hajj and the Imam; wuquf is valid in all of Arafat except Batn 'Urnah, and supplication should be earnest with hands raised like a beggar.

The Rites of Muzdalifah
Describes the combined Maghrib and Isha, overnight stay, and Fajr prayer at Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended (sunnah) and obligatory (wajib) rites at Muzdalifah according to the Hanafi school, including the rulings on combining Maghrib and Isha, the overnight stay, and the time for Fajr prayer.

Core Idea
At Muzdalifah, combine Maghrib and Isha, stay overnight (sunnah), and pray Fajr before dawn.

This lesson details the specific rites performed at Muzdalifah after departing from Arafah. Understanding these rulings ensures the pilgrim's Hajj is valid and follows the Sunnah. The passage outlines the sequence: upon arrival, combine Maghrib and Isha with one adhan and one iqama, stay overnight (sunnah), and pray Fajr at ghalas (deep twilight). The entire area of Muzdalifah is a valid standing place.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts at Muzdalifah
List the key acts mentioned: descending near Jabal Qazh, combining Maghrib and Isha, staying overnight, praying Fajr at ghalas, and standing.
These form the sequence of rites.
2
Classify each act as sunnah, wajib, or invalidating
Using the text, determine the hukm for each act. For example, combining prayers upon arrival is a sunnah of travel; staying overnight is sunnah muakkadah; praying Maghrib on the way is invalid and must be repeated.
Hanafi school distinguishes between sunnah and wajib carefully.
3
Note the conditions and exceptions
Identify that if one performs a supererogatory prayer between Maghrib and Isha, the iqama must be repeated. Also, note that Maghrib cannot be prayed before reaching Muzdalifah.
These are specific rulings of this context.
4
Determine the time for Fajr
The text states Fajr is prayed at ghalas, which is the darkness just before dawn. This is the preferred time at Muzdalifah.
This is a sunnah timing specific to this night.
5
Describe the standing (wuquf) at Muzdalifah
All of Muzdalifah is a valid standing place, though it is recommended to stand near Jabal Qazh (al-Mash'ar al-Haram).
This is a sunnah act of the Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

أي فجر يوم النحر
ويلح من ألح السائل في السؤال ألحف أو أقبل عيه مواظبا أقرب الموارد أفاض: أفاض الناس من عرفات: اندفعوا ورجعوا وتفرقوا وأسرعوا منها إلى مكان آخر أقرب الموارد جبل قزح يعني المشعر الحرام، وهو غير منصرف للعدل والعلمية ،كعمر من قزح الشيء ارتفع، يقال: إنه كانون آدم على نبينا وعليه السلام، وهو موقف الإمام كما رواه أبو داود البحر الرائق: ٥٢٢/٢] ولو تطوع ولو سنة مؤكدة على الصحيح. [البحر الرائق: ٥۲۳/۲] ولم تجز إلخ أي لم تحل صلاة المغرب قبل الوصول إلى المزدلفة، وأشار إلى أن العشاء لا تحل بالطريق الأولى وإن كان بعد دخول وقتها؛ لأن صاحبة الوقت - وهي المغرب - إذا كانت لا تحل به فغيرها أولى البحر الرائق بحذف : ٥٢٣/٢] المبيت وهذه ليلة جمعت شرف المكان والزمان فينبغي أن يجتهد في إحيائها بالصلاة والتلاوة والذكر والتضرع. [البحر الرائق: ٥٢٣/٢] فإذا طلع إلخ : أي إذا طلع الفجر يوم النحر يصلي الإمام بالناس الفجر بغلس، والغلس: ظلمة آخر الليل، وفي بعض الشروح ناقلا عن "الديوان" : آخر ظلمة الليل، وهو أوفق لما نحن فيه. [العناية: ٣٧٩/٢]
(He comes to) Muzdalifah, then he descends near Mount Qazh, and stays away from the bottom of the valley to give space to passersby. He prays Maghrib and Isha there with one adhan and one iqama. If he performs a supererogatory prayer between them or engages in something else, he must repeat the iqama. It is not permissible to pray Maghrib on the way to Muzdalifah; if he did, he must repeat it before dawn. It is sunnah to stay overnight at Muzdalifah. When dawn breaks, the Imam leads the people in Fajr prayer in the darkness of the last part of the night, then he stands and the people with him, and all of Muzdalifah is a standing place.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage details the obligations and sunnah acts at Muzdalifah. Upon arrival, the pilgrim prays Maghrib and Isha combined with one adhan and one iqama. Any supererogatory prayer between them requires repeating the iqama. It is impermissible to pray Maghrib before reaching Muzdalifah; if done, it must be repeated before the dawn of the 10th. Staying overnight is sunnah. At the time of ghalas (deep twilight just before dawn), the Imam leads Fajr. The whole of Muzdalifah is valid for standing (wuquf). The commentary explains the terms and provides proofs, including the definition of ghalas and the recommendation to spend the night in worship.

Key Terms
جبل قزح (Jabal Qazh): The mountain at Muzdalifah, also called al-Mash'ar al-Haram; it is the standing place of the Imam.
الغلس (al-Ghalas): The darkness of the last part of the night, i.e., just before dawn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on praying Maghrib on the way to Muzdalifah?
A) Permissible and valid
B) Impermissible and must be repeated before dawn
C) Permissible but disliked
D) Impermissible only if one intentionally delays

Key Takeaway
At Muzdalifah, the pilgrim combines Maghrib and Isha, stays overnight (sunnah), and prays Fajr before dawn; praying Maghrib on the way is invalid and must be repeated.

The Descent from Arafat: Conduct and Prohibitions
Ruling on conduct during the ifadha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the ifadha from Arafat, identify the permitted and prohibited actions during the descent, and apply the condition of avoiding harm.

Core Idea
Speeding and crowding during the descent from Arafat are haram unless a gap exists and no harm is caused.

After the sun sets on the Day of Arafat, the great flow of pilgrims begins. The Hanafi school provides clear guidance: the descent should be calm, with only a measured quickening when space allows, and any action that harms others is strictly prohibited. This lesson unpacks the precise ruling from Nur al-Idah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default manner
The act is the ifadha (departure) from Arafat after sunset. The default manner is for the Imam to move with the people in their usual, calm pace.
The timing (after sunset) is a condition for beginning the ifadha.
2
Recognise the exception for hurrying
The text permits hurrying only if two conditions are met: there is a gap (furjah) in the crowd, and no one is harmed in the process.
This exception is permission (ibahah), not recommendation.
3
List the prohibited actions
The 'actions of the ignorant' are explicitly mentioned: excessive speed (ishtidad fi al-sayr), crowding (izdiham), and causing harm (idha'). These are declared haram.
The prohibition is based on the general Shari'ah principle of avoiding harm (la darar).
4
Determine the ruling's scope
The prohibition applies until reaching Muzdalifah. The entire journey is governed by the same rule.
The ruling is specific to the ifadha; other parts of Hajj have separate regulations.
5
Apply the condition to a scenario
Given a scenario where a pilgrim sees a gap but fears that hurrying might cause someone to stumble, the permission is negated. The hurrying becomes haram if harm is likely.
Harm includes physical or psychological harm; the standard is a reasonable probability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا غربت الشمس أفاض الإمام مع الناس على هيئتهم، وإذا وجد فرجة يسرع من غير أن يؤذي أحدا، ويتحرز أي يتوقى والناس عما يفعله الجهلة من الاشتداد في السير والازدحام والإيذاء؛ فإنه حرام، حتى يأتي مزدلفة
When the sun sets, the Imam moves on with the people in their [usual] manner, and if he finds a gap, he may hurry without harming anyone. He should guard against what the ignorant do: speeding, crowding, and causing harm, for that is prohibited, until he reaches Muzdalifah.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on the departure (ifadha) from Arafat after sunset. The Imam and all pilgrims should move in a calm manner. However, if there is an open space, one may walk faster as long as no one is harmed. The text explicitly prohibits the behaviors of the ignorant: excessive speed, crowding, and harming others, declaring these actions haram. The goal is to reach Muzdalifah.

Key Terms
أفاض (afāḍa): To depart from Arafat after sunset in a flowing manner.
يتحرز (yataḥarraz): To guard oneself; here, to avoid the prohibited actions of the ignorant.
فرجة (furjah): A gap or open space in the crowd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on speeding and crowding during the descent from Arafat?
A) Makruh tanzihan
B) Mubah
C) Haram
D) Wajib

Key Takeaway
Speeding, crowding, and causing harm during the ifadha are haram; only if a gap exists and no harm occurs may one hurry.

Prayer at Muzdalifah: Conditions for Combining Maghrib and Isha
Rulings on combining prayers at Muzdalifah and its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for validly combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah and identify the consequence of praying Maghrib before reaching Muzdalifah.

Core Idea
Maghrib cannot be prayed before Muzdalifah — if done, it must be repeated before dawn.

This lesson covers the specific rulings for the Maghrib and Isha prayers at Muzdalifah during Hajj. The pilgrim must dismount near Mount Quzah, combine the two prayers with a single adhan and iqama, and avoid any supererogatory prayer between them. The key condition is that Maghrib must be performed at Muzdalifah itself.

Guided Path
1
Locate the ritual act
Identify that the pilgrim must dismount near Jabal Quzah and rise above the valley bed to facilitate passage.
This location is also known as al-Mash'ar al-Haram.
2
State the method of combination
Maghrib and Isha are combined with one adhan and one iqama. No supererogatory prayer (nafl) is permitted between them.
If any nafl or distraction occurs, the iqama must be repeated.
3
Consequence of violating combination
If a voluntary prayer is performed between the two prayers or he engages in something else, the iqama must be repeated. The prayer itself remains valid.
The iqama is a wajib element whose omission requires repetition but does not invalidate the prayer.
4
Identify the invalidity rule
Maghrib is not valid if prayed on the way to Muzdalifah. It must be repeated before the dawn of the following day.
This is a specific condition for Muzdalifah; other schools may permit it with an excuse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فينزل بقرب جبل قزح، ويرتفع عن بطن الوادي توسعة للمارين، ويصلي بها المغرب والعشاء بأذان واحد وإقامة واحدة، ولو تطوع بينهما أو تشاغل أعاد الإقامة، ولم تجز المغرب في طريق المزدلفة، وعليه إعادتها ما لم يطلع الفجر
He dismounts near Mount Quzah, and rises above the valley bed to make space for passersby. He prays Maghrib and Isha there with one adhan and one iqama. If he performs a supererogatory prayer between them or engages in something else, he must repeat the iqama. Maghrib is not valid on the way to Muzdalifah, and he must repeat it as long as dawn has not risen.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage explains the rulings for Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah. The pilgrim should stay near Mount Quzah (also known as al-Mash'ar al-Haram) and avoid the valley bed for the convenience of travelers. Maghrib and Isha are combined with a single adhan and a single iqama, with no voluntary prayer between them. If one does pray a nafil or becomes distracted, the iqama must be repeated (though the prayer is valid). Significantly, Maghrib is not valid if prayed before reaching Muzdalifah, and it must be repeated before dawn.

Key Terms
جبل قزح (Jabal Quzaḥ): The mountain known as al-Mash'ar al-Haram, where the Imam stands in Muzdalifah.
تطوع (taṭawwuʿ): Supererogatory prayer performed between Maghrib and Isha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must a pilgrim do if he prays Maghrib on the way to Muzdalifah?
A) He must repeat it even after dawn
B) He must repeat it before dawn
C) His prayer is valid and nothing is needed
D) He must offer a dam (penalty)

Key Takeaway
Maghrib at Muzdalifah must be prayed within Muzdalifah itself; any supererogatory prayer or distraction between the combined prayers requires repeating the iqama, and if Maghrib is prayed on the way, it must be repeated before dawn.

Staying Overnight and Standing at Muzdalifah
Ruling on mabit and wuquf at Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mabit and wuquf at Muzdalifah and identify the exception of Batn Muhassir.

Core Idea
Spending the night at Muzdalifah is sunnah, not wajib, in the Hanafi school.

In this passage from Nur al-Idah, we learn about two recommended acts (sunnah) during Hajj: staying overnight at Muzdalifah and then standing there after Fajr prayer. The Imam leads Fajr early in the remaining darkness. The text emphasizes that the entire area of Muzdalifah is valid for standing except the valley of Muhassir. Understanding the legal status of these acts helps pilgrims prioritize their actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sunnah acts
The text explicitly mentions mabit (spending the night) and wuquf (standing) after Fajr. Both are recommended.
These are separate acts; each has its own ruling.
2
Note the legal level expressed by 'yusannu'
The verb 'yusannu' indicates sunnah. In Hanafi usul, sunnah mu'akkadah is the level here.
Sunnah mu'akkadah is an emphasized sunnah but not obligatory.
3
Understand the timing for Fajr prayer
The phrase 'bi-ghalas' means praying in the last part of the night darkness. This is the recommended time for Fajr on this day.
Praying at this time distinguishes the hajj Fajr from regular Fajr.
4
Determine the valid place for wuquf
'All of Muzdalifah is a standing place except Batn Muhassir.' The exception is a specific valley.
Batn Muhassir is the valley between Muzdalifah and Mina, historically significant.
5
Contrast with other schools
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider mabit wajib. The Hanafi view is sunnah, affecting the consequence of omission.
This ikhtilaf has practical implications for dam (blood) liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسن المبيت بالمزدلفة، فإذا طلع الفجر صلى الإمام بالناس الفجر بغلس، ثم يقف والناس معه، والمزدلفة كلها موقف إلا بطن محسر
It is sunnah to spend the night at Muzdalifah. When dawn appears, the Imam prays Fajr with the people in the darkness (ghalas). Then he stands, and the people with him. All of Muzdalifah is a standing place except Batn Muhassir.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage covers two sunnah acts: spending the night at Muzdalifah (mabit) and standing there after Fajr (wuquf). The Imam leads Fajr early in the remaining darkness (ghalas). After prayer, all pilgrims stand on the ground of Muzdalifah, making supplication. The entire area of Muzdalifah is permissible for standing except the valley of Muhassir, which is excluded. This wuquf is a vital part of hajj.

Key Terms
المبيت (al-mabīt): Spending the night at Muzdalifah.
بطن محسر (Baṭn Muḥassir): A valley between Muzdalifah and Mina, excluded from the standing place.
غلس (ghalas): The darkness of the last part of the night.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, spending the night and standing at Muzdalifah are sunnah mu'akkadah, and all of Muzdalifah is valid for standing except Batn Muhassir.

Supplication at Muzdalifah and Departure to Mina
Ruling on the dua at Muzdalifah and the time of departure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah practices at Muzdalifah after Fajr and identify the correct time for departure to Mina.

Core Idea
Depart Muzdalifah before sunrise when it is very bright, not at sunrise.

After Fajr at Muzdalifah, the pilgrim is encouraged to engage in intense supplication, asking Allah to complete the Hajj as He did for the Prophet. The text then specifies the time for departure: when the morning becomes very bright, just before sunrise. This is a sunnah practice, not an obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts at Muzdalifah after Fajr
The text mentions two actions: standing in supplication and departing. Both are sunnah.
The supplication is made before departure.
2
Understand the nature of the supplication
The pilgrim should exert himself in dua, asking Allah to fulfill his hajj-related desires, following the example of the Prophet (PBUH).
This is a recommended act of worship.
3
Recognize the time marker for departure
The phrase 'asfara jiddan' (very bright) indicates the moment just before sunrise when the sky is fully illuminated.
Hanafi scholars interpret this as the time when only two rak'ahs remain before sunrise.
4
Note the ruling: departure before sunrise is sunnah
The text states that the Imam and people depart before sunrise. This is the sunnah practice, not a fard or wajib.
Deliberately delaying until after sunrise would contradict the sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقف مجتهدا في دعائه، ويدعو الله أن يتم مراده وسؤاله في هذا الموقف كما أتمه لسيدنا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم، فإذا أسفر جدا أفاض الإمام والناس قبل طلوع الشمس
He stands exerting himself in supplication, and prays to Allah to fulfill his desire and request in this standing, just as He fulfilled it for our master Muhammad (peace be upon him). Then, when it becomes very bright, the Imam and the people depart before sunrise.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
After Fajr, the pilgrim stands on the ground of Muzdalifah, making intense supplication. The text recommends asking Allah for the completion of hajj and citing the example of the Prophet (PBUH). Then, when the morning becomes fully bright (i.e., a short while before sunrise), the Imam leads the people towards Mina. The departure occurs before sunrise, not after.

Key Terms
أسفر جدا (asfara jiddan): When the morning has become very bright, just before sunrise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Twelve Matters of Stoning (Ramy) in Hajj
Rulings on the stoning of Jamrat al-Aqaba on the Day of Sacrifice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the twelve key rulings regarding the stoning ritual during Hajj, including the sequencing rule for the Day of Sacrifice.

Core Idea
On the Day of Sacrifice, only Jamrat al-Aqaba is stoned; on the following days, all three jamarat are stoned.

This passage from Nur al-Idah systematically enumerates the twelve essential rulings (masa'il) related to the stoning of the jamarat. It covers every aspect from the timing and location to the number and method of throwing. Mastering these details ensures that the pilgrim fulfills this wajib rite correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Twelve Matters
Scan the passage and list the twelve points the author mentions. They are numbered: time, place of stoning, places stoned, number of pebbles, size, method, distance, description of thrower, location of falling, where stones are taken from, what to throw, and the sequencing rule.
The first seven points are partially explained in the book; the last is the critical sequencing rule.
2
Classify Each Matter
Group the twelve matters into categories: timing (point 1), location (points 2, 3, 9, 10), quantity (point 4), physical characteristics (points 5, 11), technique (points 6, 7), personal state (point 8), and sequencing (point 12).
Categorization aids memorization and application.
3
Focus on the Sequencing Rule
Pay special attention to the twelfth matter: on the first day (10th Dhul Hijjah), only Jamrat al-Aqaba is stoned; on the remaining days (11th-13th), all three jamarat are stoned. This is a key distinction.
This is a common area of confusion among pilgrims.
4
Identify Conditions and Pillars
Based on the twelve matters, extract the conditions (shurut), pillars (arkan), and obligations (wajibat). For example, intention is a condition, hitting with seven pebbles is a pillar, and the sequencing is a wajib.
Distinguish between what makes the act valid (shurut/arkan) and what is required but compensable (wajibat).
5
Apply the Rulings to a Pilgrim's Action
Use the twelve matters as a checklist to evaluate a pilgrim's stoning. For example, if a pilgrim stones only two jamarat on the 11th, that is incorrect because all three must be stoned on subsequent days.
This step bridges theory to practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيأتي إلى منى وينزل بها ثم يأتي جمرة العقبة، فيرميها، اعلم أن الكلام في الرمي في اثني عشر موضعا : أحدها: الوقت وهو يوم النحر وثلاثة أيام بعده، والثاني: في موضع الرمي، وهو بطن الوادي يعني من أسفله إلى أعلاه والثالث في محل الرمي إليه، وهو ثلاثة: جمرة العقبة، ومسجد الخيف، والوسطى، والرابع: في كمية الحصيات، وهي سبعة عند كل جمرة، والخامس: في المقدار، وهو أن يكون مثل الخذف، والسادس في كيفية الرمي وهو ما ذكره في الكتاب، وقيل: يأخذ الحصى بطرف إبهامه وسبابته، والسابع: مقدار الرمي، وقد ذكره في الكتاب، والثامن: في صفة الرامي، وهو أن يكون راكبا أو ماشيا لا فرق بينهما. والتاسع في موضع وقوع الحصيات والعاشر: في الموضع الذي يؤخذ منه الحجر، وهما مذكوران في الكتاب والحادي عشر: في ما يرمى به، وهو ما كان من جنس الأرض، والثاني عشر: أنه يرمي في اليوم الأول جمرة العقبة لا غير، وفي بقية الأيام يرمي الجمار كلها
He goes to Mina and stays there, then comes to Jamrat al-Aqaba and stones it. Know that the discussion on stoning covers twelve matters: first, the time: the Day of Sacrifice and the three days after it; second, the place of stoning: the valley floor, from its bottom to its top; third, the places stoned: three: Jamrat al-Aqaba, Masjid al-Khayf, and the middle; fourth, the number of pebbles: seven at each jamrah; fifth, the size: like a chickpea; sixth, the method: as mentioned in the book, and it is said: take the pebbles with the ends of the thumb and forefinger; seventh, the distance of throwing; eighth, the description of the thrower: whether riding or walking, no difference; ninth, the location where the pebbles fall; tenth, the place from which the stones are taken; both are mentioned in the book; eleventh, what to throw: that which is from the earthly material; twelfth: on the first day, only Jamrat al-Aqaba is stoned, and on the remaining days, all three jamarat are stoned.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage details the rulings on the stoning ritual (ramy) during Hajj. After arriving at Mina, the pilgrim stones Jamrat al-Aqaba (the large pillar) on the Day of Sacrifice (10th of Dhul Hijjah). The twelve points cover all aspects: time (only on specified days), place (the valley floor), the specific jamarat, seven pebbles per jamrah, the size of a chickpea, the method using thumb and forefinger, etc. The key point is that on the first day, only Jamrat al-Aqaba is stoned, and on the following days (11th, 12th, and optionally 13th), all three are stoned.

Key Terms
جمرة العقبة (Jamrat al-ʿAqabah): The large stone pillar near Mina, stoned on the Day of Sacrifice.
رمي (ramy): The act of throwing pebbles at the jamarat.
خذف (khadhf): Small pebbles, about the size of a chickpea.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Three
B) None
C) Only Jamrat al-Aqaba
D) Jamrat al-Ula and al-Aqaba

Key Takeaway
The stoning on the 10th is limited to Jamrat al-Aqaba; on the following days, all three jamarat are stoned.

The Twelve Essential Rulings of Stoning (Rami) in Hajj
Enumeration of twelve legal aspects of stoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the twelve aspects of stoning in Hajj according to the Hanafi school and explain the ruling for each.

Core Idea
Stoning is a wajib act with twelve detailed aspects covering time, place, number, size, and manner.

The passage from Nur al-Idah enumerates twelve rulings that govern the act of stoning during Hajj. These rulings provide a comprehensive legal framework for the pilgrim. In this lesson, we will dissect each of these twelve aspects as outlined by the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the twelve aspects and their categories
Group the aspects into temporal, spatial, quantitative, procedural, and material categories. This helps organize the legal rules.
There are exactly twelve distinct rulings listed.
2
Examine each aspect in detail
Work through each aspect one by one: time, place of stoning, place stoned to, number of pebbles, size, manner, distance, description of stoner, place of falling, source of pebbles, material thrown, and order of throwing.
The author provides specific rulings for each.
3
Note the specific Hanafi rulings for each aspect
For example, time is the Day of Sacrifice and three days after; place is the bottom of the valley; number is seven pebbles per jamrah; size is like a chickpea, etc.
These are the relied-upon positions of the Hanafi school.
4
Understand the implications for the pilgrim's practice
Recognize that any deviation from these rulings may require a dam (sacrifice) or necessitate repetition.
Stoning is valid but may be deficient if aspects are not observed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج
بكسر السين وتشديدها
٢٥٧
كيفية تركيب أفعال الحج
إلا بطن مُحَسِّر، ويقف مجتهدا في دعائه، ويدعو الله أن يتم مراده وسؤاله في هذا الموقف كما أتمه لسيدنا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم ، فإذا أسفر جدا أفاض الإمام والناس قبل طلوع الشمس، فيأتي إلى منى وينزل بها ثم يأتي جمرة العقبة، فيرميها
إلا بطن محسر هو بضم الميم وفتح الحاء المهملة وكسر السين المهملة المشددة وبالراء؛ سمي بذلك لأن فيل أصحاب الفيل حسر فيه، أي عيبي وكلّ ووادي محسّر : موضع فاصل بين منى ومزدلفة ليس من واحدة منهما، قال الأزرقي: إن وادي محسر خمسمائة ذراع وخمس وأربعون ذراعا، وأما مزدلفة فإنها كلها من الحرم، سميت بذلك من التزلف ،والازدلاف، وهو التقرب؛ لأن الحجاج يتقربون منها وحدها ما بين وادي محسر ومأزمي عرفة، ويدخل فيها جميع تلك الشعاب والجبال الداخلة في الحد المذكور [البحر الرائق: ٥٢٥/٢] في دعائه ويقول في دعائه: اللهم أنت خير مطلوب وخير مرغوب، اللهم إن لكل وفد جائزة وقرى، فاجعل قراي في هذا المكان قبول توبتي والتجاوز عن خطيئتي، وأن تجمع على الهدى أمري، اللهم عجت لك الأصوات بالحاجات وأنت تسمعها، ولا يشغلك شأن عن شأن، وحاجتي أن لا تضيع تعبي ونصبي، وأن لا تجعلني من المحرومين، اللهم لا تجعله آخر العهد من هذا الموقف الشريف، وارزقني ذلك أبدا ما أبقيتني، فإني لا أريد إلا رحمتك ولا أبتغي إلا رضاك واحشرني في زمرة ،المخبتين والمتبعين لأمرك والعاملين بفرائضك التي جاء بها كتابك، وحث عليها رسولك ا تبيين الحقائق: ٢٩٩/٢] أسفر: وفسر الإسفار بأن تدفع بحيث لم يبق إلى طلوع الشمس إلا مقدار ما يصلي ركعتين كما في "المحيط". البحر الرائق: ٥٢٦/٢] جمرة العقبة [أي المكان المسمى بذلك البحر الرائق)] الجمار هي الحجارة جمع جمرة، وبها ستموا المواضع التي ترمى جمارا وجمرات؛ لما بينهما من الملابسة، وقيل: لتجمع ما هنالك من الحصى من تحمّر القوم إذا تجمعوا، وجمر شعره إذا جمعه على قفاه البحر الرائق: ٥٢٦/٢] فيرميها إلخ: اعلم أن الكلام في الرمي في اثني عشر موضعا : أحدها: الوقت وهو يوم النحر وثلاثة أيام بعده، والثاني: في موضع الرمي، وهو بطن الوادي يعني من أسفله إلى أعلاه والثالث في محل الرمي إليه، وهو ثلاثة: جمرة العقبة، ومسجد الخيف، والوسطى، والرابع: في كمية الحصيات، وهي سبعة عند كل جمرة، والخامس: في المقدار، وهو أن يكون مثل الخذف، والسادس في كيفية الرمي وهو ما ذكره في الكتاب، وقيل: يأخذ الحصى بطرف إبهامه وسبابته،
حصى
الصغار من
والسابع: مقدار الرمي، وقد ذكره في الكتاب، والثامن: في صفة الرامي، وهو أن يكون راكبا أو ماشيا لا فرق بينهما. والتاسع في موضع وقوع الحصيات والعاشر: في الموضع الذي يؤخذ منه الحجر، وهما مذكوران في الكتاب والحادي عشر: في ما يرمى به، وهو ما كان من جنس الأرض، والثاني عشر: أنه يرمي في اليوم الأول جمرة العقبة لا غير، وفي بقية الأيام يرمي الجمار كلها، وكلامه في الكتاب واضح. [العناية بزيادة: ٣٨٢/٢]

كتاب الحج
٢٥٨
كيفية تركيب أفعال الحج من بطن الوادي بسبع حصيات مثل حصى الخزف، ويستحب أخذ الجمار من المزدلفة
أو من الطريق، ويكره من الذي عند الجمرة، ويكره الرّمي من أعلى العقبة لإيذائه الناس،
تنزيها
وكان مخالفا للسنة
ويلتقطها التقاطا، ولا يكسر حجرا جمارا، ويغسلها ليتيقن طهارتها، فإنها يقام بما قربة ولو رمى بنجسة أجزأه وكره، ويقطع التلبية مع أول حصاة يرميها، وكيفية الرمي: أن
يأخذ الحصاة بطرف إبهامه وسبابته في الأصح؛ لأنه أيسر وأكثر إهانة للشيطان.
والمسنون الرمي باليد اليمنى، ويضع الحصاة على ظهر إبهامه، ويستعين بالمسبحة، ويكون بين الرامي وموضع السقوط خمسة أذرع، ولو وقعت على رجل أو محمل وثبتت أعادها، وإن سقطت على سننها ذلك أجزأه وكبر بكل حصاة، ثم يذبح
على ظهر الرجل
المفرد بالحج إن أحبه، ثم يحلق أو يقصر، والحلق أفضل، ويكفي فيه ربع الرأس، والتقصير أن يأخذ من رؤوس شعره مقدار الأنملة، وقد حلّ له كل شيء إلا النساء، ثم يأتي مكة من يومه ذلك أو من الغد أو بعده،
أن
بالحلق
الخزف: قال في "البحر": وهو بالخاء والذال المعجمتين: أن ترمي بحصاة أو نواة أو نحوها تأخذه بين سبابتيك، وقيل: تضع طرف الإبهام على طرف السبابة، وفعله من باب ضرب، وفي الطحطاوي" نقلا عن "القاموس": هو بالزاء المعجمة كل ما عمل من طين وشوي بالنار حتى يكون فخارا ويكره إلخ وجه الكراهة أنه حصى من لم يقبل حجه، فإنه من قبل حجه رفع حصاه كما ورد في الحديث [البحر الرائق بتصرف: ٥٢٧/٢٢] ولا يكسر : كما يفعله كثير من الناس اليوم. البحر الرائق: ٥٢٧/٢] وأكثر إهانة لأنه لم يلتفت إليه حيث لم يرمه بكل يده بل حقره ولم يعتن به حتى رماه بأطراف أصابعه. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٣٦] خمسة أذرع لأن ما دون ذلك يكون طرحا، ولو طرحها طرحا جاز؛ لأنه رمى إلى قدميه إلا أنه مسيء؛ لمخالفة السنة تبيين الحقائق: ۳۰۳/۲ ولو وقعت إلخ أي لو وقعت الحصاة على ظهر رجل أو على محمل وثبتت عليه كان عليه إعادتها. [البحر الرائق: ٥٢٦/٢] المفرد: هذا الذبح ليس بواجب على المفرد، ويجب على القارن والمتمتع (الزيلعي بتصرف والحلق ويجب إجراء الموسى على الأقرع على المختار. تبيين الحقائق: ۳۰۷/۲]
Book of Hajj. The manner of combining the actions of Hajj. Except the valley of Muhassir, and he stands striving in his supplication, and he asks Allah to complete his purpose and request in this standing as He completed it for our master Muhammad, peace be upon him. When it becomes very bright, the Imam and the people depart before sunrise, then he comes to Mina and alights there, then he comes to Jamrat al-Aqabah and stones it. Except the valley of Muhassir... (commentary) ... He says in his supplication... (dua) ... Isfar: explained as departing such that there remains only enough time to pray two rak'ahs before sunrise. Jamrat al-Aqabah: the place so named. The pebbles are stones, plural of jamrah, and the places where they are thrown are named jimar and jamarat due to association. Then he stones it etc. Know that discussion of stoning covers twelve aspects: first: time, which is the Day of Sacrifice and three days after; second: place of stoning, which is the bottom of the valley from its lowest to highest; third: place stoned to, which are three: Jamrat al-Aqabah, Masjid al-Khayf, and the middle; fourth: quantity of pebbles, which are seven at each jamrah; fifth: size, which is like that of a chickpea; sixth: manner of stoning, which is what the author mentioned; seventh: distance of stoning; eighth: description of the stoner, whether mounted or walking, no difference; ninth: place of falling of pebbles; tenth: place from which the stone is taken; eleventh: what is thrown, which is anything from the earth; twelfth: that on the first day he stones only Jamrat al-Aqabah, and on the remaining days he stones all the jamarat. His words in the book are clear. From the bottom of the valley with seven pebbles like the pebbles of khazaf. It is recommended to take the pebbles from Muzdalifah or from the road, and it is disliked to take from what is near the jamrah, and it is disliked to stone from above the Aqabah because it harms people, and it is against the Sunnah. He picks them up one by one, and does not break a stone into pebbles, and washes them to be certain of their purity, for they are used in an act of worship. If he throws with an impure object, it suffices but is disliked. He cuts off the talbiyah with the first pebble he throws. The manner of stoning: he takes the pebble with the tips of his thumb and index finger in the most correct view, because it is easier and more humiliating to the devil. The sunnah is to throw with the right hand, and he places the pebble on the back of his thumb and uses the index finger. The distance between the stoner and the place of falling should be five cubits. If it falls on a person or a camel litter and sticks, he must repeat it. If it falls in its path, it suffices. He says takbir with each pebble. Then he slaughters; the mufrid (performing tamattu') if he wishes, then he shaves or trims. Shaving is better, and one quarter of the head suffices. Trimming is to take from the ends of his hair the length of a fingertip. Then everything becomes permissible for him except women. Then he comes to Mecca that same day or the next day or after. Khazaf: as mentioned in al-Bahr: it is with khā' and dhāl, that you throw with a pebble or a date pit or similar, taking it between your two index fingers; or you place the tip of the thumb on the tip of the index finger. In al-Tahtawi quoting al-Qamus: it is with zāy, everything made of clay and fired with fire until it becomes pottery. It is disliked because it is the pebbles of one whose Hajj was not accepted, for one whose Hajj is accepted has his pebbles raised. He does not break: as many people do today. And more humiliating because he did not pay attention to it, did not throw with his whole hand, but belittled it. Five cubits because less than that is dropping; if he drops it, it is permissible, but he is doing wrong. If it falls etc., if the pebble falls on a person's back or on a camel litter and sticks, he must repeat it. The mufrid: this slaughter is not obligatory on the mufrid, but it is obligatory on the qarin and mutamatti'. Shaving: it is obligatory to run the razor over the bald man according to the chosen view.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on the matn of Nur al-Idah regarding the actions of Hajj after standing at Arafat and spending the night at Muzdalifah. It provides detailed rulings on stoning (rami) at Jamrat al-Aqabah and the subsequent rites. The author first explains the geographical definitions of Muhassir and Muzdalifah. He then presents a comprehensive supplication (dua) recommended at Muzdalifah. The crucial ruling on the time of departure (isfar) is given: the Imam and people leave when there is only enough time before sunrise to pray two rak'ahs. Upon reaching Mina, the first action is stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah. The commentary then lists twelve aspects of stoning, covering time (Day of Sacrifice and three days of Tashriq), location (bottom of the valley), targets (three jamarat), number of pebbles (seven each), size (like a chickpea), and other details. The matn states that pebbles should be taken from Muzdalifah or the road, not from near the jamrah; stoning from above is disliked. Pebbles must not be broken, and should be washed to ensure purity. Throwing with impure objects is disliked but valid. The talbiyah is cut after the first pebble. The sunnah method of stoning is described: using the right hand, holding the pebble between thumb and index finger, with a distance of five cubits between thrower and target. If the pebble sticks to something, it must be repeated. After stoning, the mufrid may optionally sacrifice, then shave or trim. Shaving is superior, and one quarter of the head suffices. After this, everything becomes halal except marital relations. Finally, the passage notes that the sacrifice is obligatory for qarin and mutamatti', and shaving is obligatory even for a bald man by running the razor over his head. This is a clear exposition of the Hanafi rulings on rami and subsequent rites.

Key Terms
جمرة العقبة (jamrat al-‘aqabah): The largest stone pillar at the far end of Mina, stoned on the Day of Sacrifice.
حصى الخزف (hasa al-khazaf): Pebbles of baked clay, about chickpea size, used for stoning.
الإسفار (al-isfar): Departure from Muzdalifah before sunrise, with only time for two rak'ah left.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many pebbles must be thrown at each jamrah?
A) Five
B) Seven
C) Nine
D) Eleven

Key Takeaway
Stoning is a wajib act governed by twelve specific rulings that pilgrims must observe for a complete and valid Hajj.

Module 8 · Lesson 46

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
10 min
Method of Stoning and Post-Stoning Obligations
Detailed method of stoning and post-stoning obligations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the correct method of stoning, including the preparation of pebbles, the manner of throwing, and the subsequent rites of shaving/trimming and sacrifice.

Core Idea
After stoning, the pilgrim must cut talbiyah, then shave or trim, and sacrifice if required, before proceeding to Mecca.

Having outlined the twelve general rulings, the passage now provides the detailed procedure for stoning and the actions that follow. This lesson will walk you through the practical steps: taking pebbles from Muzdalifah, washing them, the sunnah method of throwing with the right hand, the proper distance, and the obligations after stoning including shaving, trimming, and sacrifice.

Guided Path
1
Prepare the pebbles
Take seven pebbles from Muzdalifah or the road. Wash them to ensure purity. Do not break stones; use them whole. The pebbles should be like khazaf (baked clay, chickpea size). It is disliked to take pebbles from near the jamrah.
The pebbles are used in an act of worship, so purity is recommended.
2
Perform the stoning
Cut the talbiyah with the first pebble. Stand at a distance of five cubits from the jamrah. Use the right hand; place the pebble on the back of the thumb and push with the index finger. Say 'Allahu Akbar' with each throw. If the pebble falls on someone and sticks, repeat it. If it falls normally, it suffices.
Stoning from above the Aqabah is disliked as it harms others.
3
After stoning: shave or trim
After stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Sacrifice, the mufrid may sacrifice if he wishes. Then shave or trim. Shaving is better; one quarter of the head suffices. Trimming means cutting the ends of hair by a fingertip length. After shaving/trimming, everything becomes permissible except marital relations.
Shaving is obligatory even for a bald man: the razor must be run over the head.
4
Understand sacrifice obligations
The sacrifice is not wajib on the mufrid (one performing Hajj only). It is wajib on the qarin (performing Hajj and Umrah together) and the mutamatti' (performing Umrah then Hajj).
The passage specifies this difference.

إلا بطن محسر هو بضم الميم وفتح الحاء المهملة وكسر السين المهملة المشددة وبالراء؛ سمي بذلك لأن فيل أصحاب الفيل حسر فيه، أي عيبي وكلّ ووادي محسّر : موضع فاصل بين منى ومزدلفة ليس من واحدة منهما، قال الأزرقي: إن وادي محسر خمسمائة ذراع وخمس وأربعون ذراعا، وأما مزدلفة فإنها كلها من الحرم، سميت بذلك من التزلف ،والازدلاف، وهو التقرب؛ لأن الحجاج يتقربون منها وحدها ما بين وادي محسر ومأزمي عرفة، ويدخل فيها جميع تلك الشعاب والجبال الداخلة في الحد المذكور [البحر الرائق: ٥٢٥/٢] في دعائه ويقول في دعائه: اللهم أنت خير مطلوب وخير مرغوب، اللهم إن لكل وفد جائزة وقرى، فاجعل قراي في هذا المكان قبول توبتي والتجاوز عن خطيئتي، وأن تجمع على الهدى أمري، اللهم عجت لك الأصوات بالحاجات وأنت تسمعها، ولا يشغلك شأن عن شأن، وحاجتي أن لا تضيع تعبي ونصبي، وأن لا تجعلني من المحرومين، اللهم لا تجعله آخر العهد من هذا الموقف الشريف، وارزقني ذلك أبدا ما أبقيتني، فإني لا أريد إلا رحمتك ولا أبتغي إلا رضاك واحشرني في زمرة ،المخبتين والمتبعين لأمرك والعاملين بفرائضك التي جاء بها كتابك، وحث عليها رسولك ا تبيين الحقائق: ٢٩٩/٢] أسفر: وفسر الإسفار بأن تدفع بحيث لم يبق إلى طلوع الشمس إلا مقدار ما يصلي ركعتين كما في "المحيط". البحر الرائق: ٥٢٦/٢] جمرة العقبة [أي المكان المسمى بذلك البحر الرائق)] الجمار هي الحجارة جمع جمرة، وبها ستموا المواضع التي ترمى جمارا وجمرات؛ لما بينهما من الملابسة، وقيل: لتجمع ما هنالك من الحصى من تحمّر القوم إذا تجمعوا، وجمر شعره إذا جمعه على قفاه البحر الرائق: ٥٢٦/٢] فيرميها إلخ: اعلم أن الكلام في الرمي في اثني عشر موضعا : أحدها: الوقت وهو يوم النحر وثلاثة أيام بعده، والثاني: في موضع الرمي، وهو بطن الوادي يعني من أسفله إلى أعلاه والثالث في محل الرمي إليه، وهو ثلاثة: جمرة العقبة، ومسجد الخيف، والوسطى، والرابع: في كمية الحصيات، وهي سبعة عند كل جمرة، والخامس: في المقدار، وهو أن يكون مثل الخذف، والسادس في كيفية الرمي وهو ما ذكره في الكتاب، وقيل: يأخذ الحصى بطرف إبهامه وسبابته،

الخزف: قال في "البحر": وهو بالخاء والذال المعجمتين: أن ترمي بحصاة أو نواة أو نحوها تأخذه بين سبابتيك، وقيل: تضع طرف الإبهام على طرف السبابة، وفعله من باب ضرب، وفي الطحطاوي" نقلا عن "القاموس": هو بالزاء المعجمة كل ما عمل من طين وشوي بالنار حتى يكون فخارا ويكره إلخ وجه الكراهة أنه حصى من لم يقبل حجه، فإنه من قبل حجه رفع حصاه كما ورد في الحديث [البحر الرائق بتصرف: ٥٢٧/٢٢] ولا يكسر : كما يفعله كثير من الناس اليوم. البحر الرائق: ٥٢٧/٢] وأكثر إهانة لأنه لم يلتفت إليه حيث لم يرمه بكل يده بل حقره ولم يعتن به حتى رماه بأطراف أصابعه. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٣٦] خمسة أذرع لأن ما دون ذلك يكون طرحا، ولو طرحها طرحا جاز؛ لأنه رمى إلى قدميه إلا أنه مسيء؛ لمخالفة السنة تبيين الحقائق: ۳۰۳/۲ ولو وقعت إلخ أي لو وقعت الحصاة على ظهر رجل أو على محمل وثبتت عليه كان عليه إعادتها. [البحر الرائق: ٥٢٦/٢] المفرد: هذا الذبح ليس بواجب على المفرد، ويجب على القارن والمتمتع (الزيلعي بتصرف والحلق ويجب إجراء الموسى على الأقرع على المختار. تبيين الحقائق: ۳۰۷/۲]
Book of Hajj. The manner of combining the actions of Hajj. Except the valley of Muhassir, and he stands striving in his supplication, and he asks Allah to complete his purpose and request in this standing as He completed it for our master Muhammad, peace be upon him. When it becomes very bright, the Imam and the people depart before sunrise, then he comes to Mina and alights there, then he comes to Jamrat al-Aqabah and stones it. Except the valley of Muhassir... (commentary) ... He says in his supplication... (dua) ... Isfar: explained as departing such that there remains only enough time to pray two rak'ahs before sunrise. Jamrat al-Aqabah: the place so named. The pebbles are stones, plural of jamrah, and the places where they are thrown are named jimar and jamarat due to association. Then he stones it etc. Know that discussion of stoning covers twelve aspects: first: time, which is the Day of Sacrifice and three days after; second: place of stoning, which is the bottom of the valley from its lowest to highest; third: place stoned to, which are three: Jamrat al-Aqabah, Masjid al-Khayf, and the middle; fourth: quantity of pebbles, which are seven at each jamrah; fifth: size, which is like that of a chickpea; sixth: manner of stoning, which is what the author mentioned; seventh: distance of stoning; eighth: description of the stoner, whether mounted or walking, no difference; ninth: place of falling of pebbles; tenth: place from which the stone is taken; eleventh: what is thrown, which is anything from the earth; twelfth: that on the first day he stones only Jamrat al-Aqabah, and on the remaining days he stones all the jamarat. His words in the book are clear. From the bottom of the valley with seven pebbles like the pebbles of khazaf. It is recommended to take the pebbles from Muzdalifah or from the road, and it is disliked to take from what is near the jamrah, and it is disliked to stone from above the Aqabah because it harms people, and it is against the Sunnah. He picks them up one by one, and does not break a stone into pebbles, and washes them to be certain of their purity, for they are used in an act of worship. If he throws with an impure object, it suffices but is disliked. He cuts off the talbiyah with the first pebble he throws. The manner of stoning: he takes the pebble with the tips of his thumb and index finger in the most correct view, because it is easier and more humiliating to the devil. The sunnah is to throw with the right hand, and he places the pebble on the back of his thumb and uses the index finger. The distance between the stoner and the place of falling should be five cubits. If it falls on a person or a camel litter and sticks, he must repeat it. If it falls in its path, it suffices. He says takbir with each pebble. Then he slaughters; the mufrid (performing tamattu') if he wishes, then he shaves or trims. Shaving is better, and one quarter of the head suffices. Trimming is to take from the ends of his hair the length of a fingertip. Then everything becomes permissible for him except women. Then he comes to Mecca that same day or the next day or after. Khazaf: as mentioned in al-Bahr: it is with khā' and dhāl, that you throw with a pebble or a date pit or similar, taking it between your two index fingers; or you place the tip of the thumb on the tip of the index finger. In al-Tahtawi quoting al-Qamus: it is with zāy, everything made of clay and fired with fire until it becomes pottery. It is disliked because it is the pebbles of one whose Hajj was not accepted, for one whose Hajj is accepted has his pebbles raised. He does not break: as many people do today. And more humiliating because he did not pay attention to it, did not throw with his whole hand, but belittled it. Five cubits because less than that is dropping; if he drops it, it is permissible, but he is doing wrong. If it falls etc., if the pebble falls on a person's back or on a camel litter and sticks, he must repeat it. The mufrid: this slaughter is not obligatory on the mufrid, but it is obligatory on the qarin and mutamatti'. Shaving: it is obligatory to run the razor over the bald man according to the chosen view.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on the matn of Nur al-Idah regarding the actions of Hajj after standing at Arafat and spending the night at Muzdalifah. It provides detailed rulings on stoning (rami) at Jamrat al-Aqabah and the subsequent rites. The author first explains the geographical definitions of Muhassir and Muzdalifah. He then presents a comprehensive supplication (dua) recommended at Muzdalifah. The crucial ruling on the time of departure (isfar) is given: the Imam and people leave when there is only enough time before sunrise to pray two rak'ahs. Upon reaching Mina, the first action is stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah. The commentary then lists twelve aspects of stoning, covering time (Day of Sacrifice and three days of Tashriq), location (bottom of the valley), targets (three jamarat), number of pebbles (seven each), size (like a chickpea), and other details. The matn states that pebbles should be taken from Muzdalifah or the road, not from near the jamrah; stoning from above is disliked. Pebbles must not be broken, and should be washed to ensure purity. Throwing with impure objects is disliked but valid. The talbiyah is cut after the first pebble. The sunnah method of stoning is described: using the right hand, holding the pebble between thumb and index finger, with a distance of five cubits between thrower and target. If the pebble sticks to something, it must be repeated. After stoning, the mufrid may optionally sacrifice, then shave or trim. Shaving is superior, and one quarter of the head suffices. After this, everything becomes halal except marital relations. Finally, the passage notes that the sacrifice is obligatory for qarin and mutamatti', and shaving is obligatory even for a bald man by running the razor over his head. This is a clear exposition of the Hanafi rulings on rami and subsequent rites.

Key Terms
جمرة العقبة (jamrat al-‘aqabah): The largest stone pillar at the far end of Mina, stoned on the Day of Sacrifice.
حصى الخزف (hasa al-khazaf): Pebbles of baked clay, about chickpea size, used for stoning.
الإسفار (al-isfar): Departure from Muzdalifah before sunrise, with only time for two rak'ah left.

Key Takeaway
The correct method of stoning and the subsequent rites of shaving/trimming and sacrifice ensure the validity and completeness of Hajj.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
8 min
The Day of Sacrifice Rituals: From Stoning to Tawaf al-Ziyarah
Procedural description of Day of Sacrifice rituals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sequence of actions on the Day of Sacrifice and identify the rulings (wajib, sunnah, makruh) for each step.

Core Idea
The Day of Sacrifice requires stoning, sacrifice, shaving, and tawaf, each with precise sunnah methods and conditions.

This passage details the actions a pilgrim performs on the Day of Sacrifice after returning from Muzdalifah: stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah, offering sacrifice, shaving or trimming, and performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah. Each step has recommended methods and conditions, and understanding them ensures the pilgrimage is valid and complete.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actions after returning from Muzdalifah
List the four main actions: stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah, sacrifice (for mufrid optionally), shaving/trimming, and Tawaf al-Ziyarah. Note the order and the effect of each on ihram.
First tahallul occurs after stoning and shaving, permitting everything except women.
2
Explain the recommended method for stoning
Describe the sunnah method: use seven pebbles like pottery, taken from Muzdalifah or the road, washed, thrown with right hand, distance of five cubits, saying takbir with each. Avoid throwing from above the jamrah, and stop talbiyah with first stone.
Disliked (makruh tanzih) actions: taking pebbles from near the jamrah, throwing from above, using impure pebbles.
3
Differentiate the sacrifice ruling for mufrid vs others
State that for the mufrid (ifrad), sacrifice is mustahabb (optional), indicated by 'in ahabba' (if he wishes). For qarin and mutamatti', sacrifice is wajib.
This textual detail is critical for fatwa.
4
Describe shaving/trimming and its sufficiency
Shaving is better; sufficient to shave a quarter of the head. Trimming is cutting hair to the length of a fingertip. This completes the first tahallul.
Bald man passes razor over head; no minimum hair required.
5
State the ruling of Tawaf al-Ziyarah
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a rukn (obligatory) of Hajj, performed after returning to Mecca on the same day or next days. Delaying beyond the Days of Sacrifice requires a dam (sheep). Best performed first day. After completion, women become permissible (second tahallul).
This tawaf is also called Tawaf al-Ifadah.
