كتاب الحج
كيفية تركيب أفعال الحج من بطن الوادي بسبع حصيات مثل حصى الخزف، ويستحب أخذ الجمار من المزدلفة أو من الطريق، ويكره من الذي عند الجمرة، ويكره الرّمي من أعلى العقبة لإيذائه الناس، تنزيها وكان مخالفا للسنة ويلتقطها التقاطا، ولا يكسر حجرا جمارا، ويغسلها ليتيقن طهارتها، فإنها يقام بما قربة ولو رمى بنجسة أجزأه وكره، ويقطع التلبية مع أول حصاة يرميها، وكيفية الرمي: أن يأخذ الحصاة بطرف إبهامه وسبابته في الأصح؛ لأنه أيسر وأكثر إهانة للشيطان. والمسنون الرمي باليد اليمنى، ويضع الحصاة على ظهر إبهامه، ويستعين بالمسبحة، ويكون بين الرامي وموضع السقوط خمسة أذرع، ولو وقعت على رجل أو محمل وثبتت أعادها، وإن سقطت على سننها ذلك أجزأه وكبر بكل حصاة، ثم يذبح على ظهر الرجل المفرد بالحج إن أحبه، ثم يحلق أو يقصر، والحلق أفضل، ويكفي فيه ربع الرأس، والتقصير أن يأخذ من رؤوس شعره مقدار الأنملة، وقد حلّ له كل شيء إلا النساء، ثم يأتي مكة من يومه ذلك أو من الغد أو بعده، فيطوف بالبيت طواف الزيارة سبعة أشواط، وحلت له النساء، وأفضل هذه الأيام أولها، وإن أخره عنها لزمه شاة؛ لتأخير الواجب، ثم يعود إلى منى، فيقيم بها، فإذا زالت الشمس من اليوم الثاني من أيام النحر رمى الجمار الثلاث، يبدأ بالجمرة التي تلي مسجد الخيف، فيرميها بسبع حصيات ماشيا، يكبر بكل حصاة، ثم يقف عندها داعيا بما أحب حامدا لله تعالى، مصليا على النبي ويرفع يديه في الدعاء، ويستغفر لوالديه وإخوانه المؤمنين ثم يرمي الثانية التي تليها مثل ذلك، ويقف عندها داعيا، ثم يرمي جمرة العقبة راكبا، ولا يقف عندها. فإذا كان اليوم الثالث من أيام النحر رمي الجمار الثلاث بعد الزوال كذلك، وإذا أراد أن يتعجل نفر إلى مكة قبل غروب الشمس، وإن أقام إلى الغروب كره، وليس عليه شيء، وإن طلع الفجر - وهو بمنى - في الرابع لزمه الرمي، وجاز قبل الزوال، والأفضل بعده، وكره قبل طلوع الشمس، وكل رمي بعده رمي، ترميه ماشيا؛ سبعة أشواط أي لا ترمل فيه ولا تسعى بعده بين الصفا والمروة، إن كنت رملت في طواف القدوم، وسعيت بين الصفا والمروة بعده، وإلا فارمل في هذا الطواف واسع بعده. تبيين الحقائق: ۳۱۰/۲] فإذا كان الخ: يعني: إذا زالت الشمس من اليوم الثالث من أيام النحر، رمي الجمار الثلاث مثل ما رمى في اليوم الثاني. [العناية: ٣٩٢/٢] ترمیه ماشيا هذا لبيان الأفضلية، وأما الجواز فثابت كيفما كان الحصول المقصود وهو الرمي، والأول مروي عن أبي يوسف، فإنه قد ذكر ابن الجراح - وهو من أكبر تلامذة عطاء بن أبي رباح تلميذ ابن عباس وكان عالما بالمناسك - أنه قال: دخلت على أبي يوسف وقد أغمي عليه فأفاق فلما رآني قال: يا إبراهيم ما تقول في رمي الجمار يرميها الحاج راكبا أو ماشيا؟ فقلت يرميها ماشيا فقال: أخطأت، فقلت: يرميها راكبا، فقال: أخطأت قلت فماذا يقول الإمام، قال: كل رمي بعده رمي، يرميها ماشيا، وكل رمي ليس بعده رمي، يرميها راكبا فخرجت من عنده فسمعت بكاء الناس في داره فقيل لي قضي أبو يوسف له، فتعجبت من حرصه على العلم في مثل هذه الحادثة تبيين الحقائق بزيادة: ٣١٥/٢] اللهم اجعل عبدك إعزاز علي ممن جعله قدوة في جميع مسالكه عامة وفي هذا المسلك خاصة. آمين.
The Book of Hajj. The method of arranging the actions of Hajj: from the middle of the valley with seven pebbles like pottery pebbles. It is recommended to take the pebbles from Muzdalifah or from the road, and it is disliked to take from near the jamrah. It is disliked to throw from the top of al-Aqabah due to harming people, as a tanzihan, and it is contrary to the Sunnah. He should pick them up one by one, and not break a stone (to use as a pebble). He should wash them to be certain of their purity, for they are used for an act of worship. If he throws with something impure, it suffices and is disliked. He stops the talbiyah with the first pebble he throws. The manner of throwing: he takes the pebble with the tip of his thumb and index finger according to the most correct view, because it is easier and a greater humiliation for the devil. The sunnah is to throw with the right hand, placing the pebble on the back of his thumb, using the index finger. The distance between the thrower and the landing spot should be five cubits. If (the pebble) hits a man or a howdah and sticks, he repeats it. If it falls on its own course, it suffices. He says takbir with each pebble. Then the mufrid (performer of ifrad) sacrifices (if he wishes) on the side of the road. Then he shaves or trims; shaving is better. It is sufficient to shave a quarter of the head. Trimming is to take from the ends of his hair the length of a fingertip. Now everything becomes permissible for him except women. Then he comes to Mecca on that day or the next or after it, and performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah of the House, seven circuits, and women become permissible for him. The best of these days is the first. If he delays it beyond these (days), a sheep is due upon him for delaying the obligatory. Then he returns to Mina and stays there. When the sun passes the zenith on the second day of the days of sacrifice, he stones the three jamarat. He begins with the jamrah nearest to Masjid al-Khayf, throwing seven pebbles while walking, saying takbir with each pebble. Then he stands there supplicating as he wishes, praising Allah, sending blessings on the Prophet, raising his hands in supplication, seeking forgiveness for his parents and believing brothers. Then he stones the second (jamrah) similarly and stands supplicating. Then he stones Jamrat al-Aqabah while riding and does not stand there. On the third day of the days of sacrifice, he stones the three jamarat after zenith similarly. If he wishes to hasten, he departs to Mecca before sunset. If he stays until sunset, it is disliked but nothing is upon him. If dawn breaks while he is in Mina on the fourth day, stoning is required of him, and it is permissible before noon, but after noon is better, and it is disliked before sunrise. Every stoning after which there is (another) stoning, he stones walking. Seven circuits: i.e., he does not do ramal in it nor does he perform sa'y between Safa and Marwah after it, if he did ramal in Tawaf al-Qudum and sa'y between Safa and Marwah after it; otherwise he does ramal in this tawaf and sa'y after it. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 310/2] Then if: meaning: when the sun passes the zenith on the third day of the days of sacrifice, he stones the three jamarat just as he stoned on the second day. [al-'Inayah 392/2] He stones walking: this is to show preference; as for permissibility, it is established in any way the intended purpose (throwing) is achieved. The first is narrated from Abu Yusuf. Ibn al-Jarrah, who was one of the senior students of 'Ata' ibn Abi Rabah, a student of Ibn 'Abbas, and a scholar of the rituals, said: I visited Abu Yusuf while he was unconscious. He regained consciousness and when he saw me said: O Ibrahim, what do you say about stoning the jamarat, should the pilgrim stone riding or walking? I said: walking. He said: You are mistaken. I said: riding. He said: You are mistaken. I said: So what does the Imam say? He said: Every stoning after which there is (another) stoning, he stones walking; and every stoning after which there is no (other) stoning, he stones riding. I left him and heard people crying in his house. I was told: Abu Yusuf has passed away. So I marvelled at his eagerness for knowledge even in such a moment. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq with addition 315/2] O Allah, make Your servant 'Izzaz 'Ali among those whom You have made a guide in all his paths generally and in this path specifically. Amen.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage is a procedural description of the actions of Hajj after the stay at Arafat and Muzdalifah, covering the rituals from the stoning of Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Sacrifice up to the days of Tashriq in Mina. It begins by detailing the recommended method for stoning: taking seven pebbles similar to pottery pebbles, preferably from Muzdalifah or the road, not from near the jamrah. It is disliked to throw from above the jamrah to avoid harming others. The pebbles should be picked up individually, not broken from stones, and washed to ensure purity. Throwing with impure material suffices but is disliked. The talbiyah ceases with the first stone. The sunnah method is to hold the pebble between thumb and index finger, throw with the right hand, and maintain a distance of five cubits. If the pebble hits a person or litter and sticks, it must be repeated; if it falls naturally, it suffices. Takbir is said with each stone. After stoning, the mufrid (one performing ifrad) may offer a sacrifice, though it is not obligatory. Then he shaves or trims, shaving being better; a quarter of the head is sufficient, and trimming is to cut the hair length of a fingertip. At this point, everything becomes permissible except sexual relations with women. Next, he proceeds to Mecca for Tawaf al-Ziyarah, seven circuits, after which intercourse becomes permissible. Delaying this tawaf beyond its days requires a compensatory sheep. The passage then describes the stoning of the three jamarat on the 11th and 12th of Dhul-Hijjah: starting with the jamrah nearest Masjid al-Khayf while walking, then the second, and finally Jamrat al-Aqabah while riding, with supplications at the first two but not the third. On the 12th, the same procedure applies. If the pilgrim wishes to hasten, he may leave Mina before sunset on the 12th; if he stays until sunset, it is disliked but no penalty. If dawn of the 13th finds him in Mina, stoning becomes obligatory. The commentary clarifies that walking for stoning is preferred when a subsequent stoning follows, and riding when none follows, as narrated from Abu Yusuf. This passage also includes a moving anecdote about Abu Yusuf's dedication to knowledge even at the point of death.

Key Terms
الجمرة (al-jamrah): A pillar (now a wall) at which pebbles are thrown during Hajj; three in Mina: al-Ula, al-Wusta, and al-Aqabah.
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The obligatory circumambulation of the Kaaba performed after stoning and shaving on the Day of Sacrifice or the following days.
المفرد (al-mufrid): One performing Hajj ifrad, i.e., Hajj alone without Umrah.
الحلق (al-halq): Shaving the head, which is recommended (afdal) over trimming for men performing Hajj.
التحلل (al-tahallul): The state of becoming permissible (halal) after completing specific Hajj actions; the first tahallul after stoning and shaving/trimming, the second after Tawaf al-Ziyarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling of the sacrifice (hady) for a mufrid (one performing Hajj ifrad)?
A) Wajib
B) Mustahabb
C) Haram
D) Fard

Key Takeaway
On the Day of Sacrifice, the mufrid pilgrim stones, optionally sacrifices, shaves, and performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah, with women becoming permissible only after the tawaf.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate

Stoning the Jamarat on the Days of Tashriq: Walking vs. Riding
Hanafi ruling on walking vs riding during stoning on days of Tashriq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that determines whether to stone each jamrah walking or riding based on whether a subsequent stoning follows.

Core Idea
Every stoning after which another stoning follows is done walking; the final stoning of the day is done riding.

The passage describes the stoning of the three jamarat on the 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul-Hijjah. A key principle derived from Abu Yusuf distinguishes between stonings that have a subsequent stoning (walking) and those that do not (riding). This lesson unpacks that principle and its application.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the three jamarat and their order
On each day, the pilgrim stones al-Jamrah al-Ula (nearest Masjid al-Khayf), then al-Wusta, then al-Aqabah. Each is stoned with seven pebbles.
The first two are collectively called 'the first two jamarat'.
2
Understand the principle from Abu Yusuf
Analyze the statement: 'Every stoning after which there is a stoning, stone walking; every stoning after which there is no stoning, stone riding.' This applies to each day's sequence.
The final jamrah of each day (al-Aqabah) has no subsequent stoning, so it is done riding.
3
Apply the rule to each day
On the 11th and 12th: stone first two walking, third riding. On the 13th (if staying): same pattern. For the 12th, if hastening (depart before sunset), only the first two are stoned (both done walking? Actually, the third is also stoned but no subsequent, so riding). Wait: hastening means leaving before sunset on 12th, so stoning is done for all three? Actually, text: 'If he wishes to hasten, he departs to Mecca before sunset' meaning he stones the three on 12th then leaves. So same rule: first two walking, third riding.
If dawn of 13th finds him in Mina, stoning all three is required following the same pattern.
4
Note the permissibility of alternative methods
The text states that walking is for preference (afdaliyyah); permissibility is broad as long as stoning is achieved. So riding for all is permissible but less preferred.
The first narration from Abu Yusuf is considered the preferred method.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج
كيفية تركيب أفعال الحج من بطن الوادي بسبع حصيات مثل حصى الخزف، ويستحب أخذ الجمار من المزدلفة أو من الطريق، ويكره من الذي عند الجمرة، ويكره الرّمي من أعلى العقبة لإيذائه الناس، تنزيها وكان مخالفا للسنة ويلتقطها التقاطا، ولا يكسر حجرا جمارا، ويغسلها ليتيقن طهارتها، فإنها يقام بما قربة ولو رمى بنجسة أجزأه وكره، ويقطع التلبية مع أول حصاة يرميها، وكيفية الرمي: أن يأخذ الحصاة بطرف إبهامه وسبابته في الأصح؛ لأنه أيسر وأكثر إهانة للشيطان. والمسنون الرمي باليد اليمنى، ويضع الحصاة على ظهر إبهامه، ويستعين بالمسبحة، ويكون بين الرامي وموضع السقوط خمسة أذرع، ولو وقعت على رجل أو محمل وثبتت أعادها، وإن سقطت على سننها ذلك أجزأه وكبر بكل حصاة، ثم يذبح على ظهر الرجل المفرد بالحج إن أحبه، ثم يحلق أو يقصر، والحلق أفضل، ويكفي فيه ربع الرأس، والتقصير أن يأخذ من رؤوس شعره مقدار الأنملة، وقد حلّ له كل شيء إلا النساء، ثم يأتي مكة من يومه ذلك أو من الغد أو بعده، فيطوف بالبيت طواف الزيارة سبعة أشواط، وحلت له النساء، وأفضل هذه الأيام أولها، وإن أخره عنها لزمه شاة؛ لتأخير الواجب، ثم يعود إلى منى، فيقيم بها، فإذا زالت الشمس من اليوم الثاني من أيام النحر رمى الجمار الثلاث، يبدأ بالجمرة التي تلي مسجد الخيف، فيرميها بسبع حصيات ماشيا، يكبر بكل حصاة، ثم يقف عندها داعيا بما أحب حامدا لله تعالى، مصليا على النبي ويرفع يديه في الدعاء، ويستغفر لوالديه وإخوانه المؤمنين ثم يرمي الثانية التي تليها مثل ذلك، ويقف عندها داعيا، ثم يرمي جمرة العقبة راكبا، ولا يقف عندها. فإذا كان اليوم الثالث من أيام النحر رمي الجمار الثلاث بعد الزوال كذلك، وإذا أراد أن يتعجل نفر إلى مكة قبل غروب الشمس، وإن أقام إلى الغروب كره، وليس عليه شيء، وإن طلع الفجر - وهو بمنى - في الرابع لزمه الرمي، وجاز قبل الزوال، والأفضل بعده، وكره قبل طلوع الشمس، وكل رمي بعده رمي، ترميه ماشيا؛ سبعة أشواط أي لا ترمل فيه ولا تسعى بعده بين الصفا والمروة، إن كنت رملت في طواف القدوم، وسعيت بين الصفا والمروة بعده، وإلا فارمل في هذا الطواف واسع بعده. تبيين الحقائق: ۳۱۰/۲] فإذا كان الخ: يعني: إذا زالت الشمس من اليوم الثالث من أيام النحر، رمي الجمار الثلاث مثل ما رمى في اليوم الثاني. [العناية: ٣٩٢/٢] ترمیه ماشيا هذا لبيان الأفضلية، وأما الجواز فثابت كيفما كان الحصول المقصود وهو الرمي، والأول مروي عن أبي يوسف، فإنه قد ذكر ابن الجراح - وهو من أكبر تلامذة عطاء بن أبي رباح تلميذ ابن عباس وكان عالما بالمناسك - أنه قال: دخلت على أبي يوسف وقد أغمي عليه فأفاق فلما رآني قال: يا إبراهيم ما تقول في رمي الجمار يرميها الحاج راكبا أو ماشيا؟ فقلت يرميها ماشيا فقال: أخطأت، فقلت: يرميها راكبا، فقال: أخطأت قلت فماذا يقول الإمام، قال: كل رمي بعده رمي، يرميها ماشيا، وكل رمي ليس بعده رمي، يرميها راكبا فخرجت من عنده فسمعت بكاء الناس في داره فقيل لي قضي أبو يوسف له، فتعجبت من حرصه على العلم في مثل هذه الحادثة تبيين الحقائق بزيادة: ٣١٥/٢] اللهم اجعل عبدك إعزاز علي ممن جعله قدوة في جميع مسالكه عامة وفي هذا المسلك خاصة. آمين.
The Book of Hajj. The method of arranging the actions of Hajj: from the middle of the valley with seven pebbles like pottery pebbles. It is recommended to take the pebbles from Muzdalifah or from the road, and it is disliked to take from near the jamrah. It is disliked to throw from the top of al-Aqabah due to harming people, as a tanzihan, and it is contrary to the Sunnah. He should pick them up one by one, and not break a stone (to use as a pebble). He should wash them to be certain of their purity, for they are used for an act of worship. If he throws with something impure, it suffices and is disliked. He stops the talbiyah with the first pebble he throws. The manner of throwing: he takes the pebble with the tip of his thumb and index finger according to the most correct view, because it is easier and a greater humiliation for the devil. The sunnah is to throw with the right hand, placing the pebble on the back of his thumb, using the index finger. The distance between the thrower and the landing spot should be five cubits. If (the pebble) hits a man or a howdah and sticks, he repeats it. If it falls on its own course, it suffices. He says takbir with each pebble. Then the mufrid (performer of ifrad) sacrifices (if he wishes) on the side of the road. Then he shaves or trims; shaving is better. It is sufficient to shave a quarter of the head. Trimming is to take from the ends of his hair the length of a fingertip. Now everything becomes permissible for him except women. Then he comes to Mecca on that day or the next or after it, and performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah of the House, seven circuits, and women become permissible for him. The best of these days is the first. If he delays it beyond these (days), a sheep is due upon him for delaying the obligatory. Then he returns to Mina and stays there. When the sun passes the zenith on the second day of the days of sacrifice, he stones the three jamarat. He begins with the jamrah nearest to Masjid al-Khayf, throwing seven pebbles while walking, saying takbir with each pebble. Then he stands there supplicating as he wishes, praising Allah, sending blessings on the Prophet, raising his hands in supplication, seeking forgiveness for his parents and believing brothers. Then he stones the second (jamrah) similarly and stands supplicating. Then he stones Jamrat al-Aqabah while riding and does not stand there. On the third day of the days of sacrifice, he stones the three jamarat after zenith similarly. If he wishes to hasten, he departs to Mecca before sunset. If he stays until sunset, it is disliked but nothing is upon him. If dawn breaks while he is in Mina on the fourth day, stoning is required of him, and it is permissible before noon, but after noon is better, and it is disliked before sunrise. Every stoning after which there is (another) stoning, he stones walking. Seven circuits: i.e., he does not do ramal in it nor does he perform sa'y between Safa and Marwah after it, if he did ramal in Tawaf al-Qudum and sa'y between Safa and Marwah after it; otherwise he does ramal in this tawaf and sa'y after it. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 310/2] Then if: meaning: when the sun passes the zenith on the third day of the days of sacrifice, he stones the three jamarat just as he stoned on the second day. [al-'Inayah 392/2] He stones walking: this is to show preference; as for permissibility, it is established in any way the intended purpose (throwing) is achieved. The first is narrated from Abu Yusuf. Ibn al-Jarrah, who was one of the senior students of 'Ata' ibn Abi Rabah, a student of Ibn 'Abbas, and a scholar of the rituals, said: I visited Abu Yusuf while he was unconscious. He regained consciousness and when he saw me said: O Ibrahim, what do you say about stoning the jamarat, should the pilgrim stone riding or walking? I said: walking. He said: You are mistaken. I said: riding. He said: You are mistaken. I said: So what does the Imam say? He said: Every stoning after which there is (another) stoning, he stones walking; and every stoning after which there is no (other) stoning, he stones riding. I left him and heard people crying in his house. I was told: Abu Yusuf has passed away. So I marvelled at his eagerness for knowledge even in such a moment. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq with addition 315/2] O Allah, make Your servant 'Izzaz 'Ali among those whom You have made a guide in all his paths generally and in this path specifically. Amen.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage is a procedural description of the actions of Hajj after the stay at Arafat and Muzdalifah, covering the rituals from the stoning of Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Sacrifice up to the days of Tashriq in Mina. It begins by detailing the recommended method for stoning: taking seven pebbles similar to pottery pebbles, preferably from Muzdalifah or the road, not from near the jamrah. It is disliked to throw from above the jamrah to avoid harming others. The pebbles should be picked up individually, not broken from stones, and washed to ensure purity. Throwing with impure material suffices but is disliked. The talbiyah ceases with the first stone. The sunnah method is to hold the pebble between thumb and index finger, throw with the right hand, and maintain a distance of five cubits. If the pebble hits a person or litter and sticks, it must be repeated; if it falls naturally, it suffices. Takbir is said with each stone. After stoning, the mufrid (one performing ifrad) may offer a sacrifice, though it is not obligatory. Then he shaves or trims, shaving being better; a quarter of the head is sufficient, and trimming is to cut the hair length of a fingertip. At this point, everything becomes permissible except sexual relations with women. Next, he proceeds to Mecca for Tawaf al-Ziyarah, seven circuits, after which intercourse becomes permissible. Delaying this tawaf beyond its days requires a compensatory sheep. The passage then describes the stoning of the three jamarat on the 11th and 12th of Dhul-Hijjah: starting with the jamrah nearest Masjid al-Khayf while walking, then the second, and finally Jamrat al-Aqabah while riding, with supplications at the first two but not the third. On the 12th, the same procedure applies. If the pilgrim wishes to hasten, he may leave Mina before sunset on the 12th; if he stays until sunset, it is disliked but no penalty. If dawn of the 13th finds him in Mina, stoning becomes obligatory. The commentary clarifies that walking for stoning is preferred when a subsequent stoning follows, and riding when none follows, as narrated from Abu Yusuf. This passage also includes a moving anecdote about Abu Yusuf's dedication to knowledge even at the point of death.

Key Terms
الجمرة (al-jamrah): A pillar (now a wall) at which pebbles are thrown during Hajj; three in Mina: al-Ula, al-Wusta, and al-Aqabah.
أيام التشريق (ayyam al-tashriq): The three days following the Day of Sacrifice: 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul-Hijjah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the principle from Abu Yusuf, how should a pilgrim stone Jamrat al-Aqabah on the 11th of Dhul-Hijjah?
A) Walking
B) Riding
C) Either walking or riding
D) It is not stoned on the 11th

Key Takeaway
The method of stoning (walking/riding) is determined by whether another stoning follows: walk when yes, ride when no.

Ruling on Tawaf al-Ziyarah and Ramy on the 2nd Day
Describes the sequence of Hajj actions from tawaf al-ziyarah to ramy on 2nd day.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sequence of actions after the day of sacrifice in Hajj, identify the ruling of Tawaf al-Ziyarah and ramy, and explain the consequences of delaying them.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Ziyarah and ramy are wajib acts; delaying the tawaf requires a sacrifice.

This passage from Nur al-Idah describes the essential actions a pilgrim performs after the day of sacrifice: Tawaf al-Ziyarah and the ramy on the second day of Tashreeq. Understanding the order and rulings ensures the pilgrim fulfills these wajibat correctly and knows the consequences of delay.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first wajib action
The passage begins with Tawaf al-Ziyarah (also called Tawaf al-Ifadah). Note that it consists of seven circuits and after it, marital relations become permissible.
This tawaf is a wajib act; some schools consider it a pillar.
2
Note the ruling on timing
The best day is the first day of sacrifice (10th Dhul Hijjah). If delayed beyond the days of sacrifice, a sheep (dam) becomes incumbent because a wajib was delayed.
3
Identify the second action: return to Mina
After tawaf, the pilgrim returns to Mina and stays there until the ramy.
Staying in Mina is also wajib during the days of Tashreeq.
4
Describe the ramy procedure for the second day
After zawal (noon) on the second day (11th Dhul Hijjah), the pilgrim pelts the three jamarat. Begin with the jamrah nearest to Masjid al-Khayf: pelt with seven pebbles while walking, say takbir with each pebble, then stand and supplicate. Repeat for the middle jamrah.
Walking for the first two jamarat is mustahab, as is supplicating after them.
5
Note the difference for the third jamrah
For Jamrat al-Aqabah, the pilgrim pelts while riding (mustahab) and does not stand to supplicate afterwards.
This is the final jamrah of the day.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج كيفية تركيب أفعال الحج فيطوف بالبيت طواف الزيارة سبعة أشواط، وحلت له النساء، وأفضل هذه الأيام أولها، وإن أخره عنها لزمه شاة؛ لتأخير الواجب، ثم يعود إلى منى، فيقيم بها، فإذا زالت الشمس من اليوم الثاني من أيام النحر رمى الجمار الثلاث، يبدأ بالجمرة التي تلي مسجد الخيف، فيرميها بسبع حصيات ماشيا، يكبر بكل حصاة، ثم يقف عندها داعيا بما أحب حامدا لله تعالى، مصليا على النبي ويرفع يديه في الدعاء، ويستغفر لوالديه وإخوانه المؤمنين ثم يرمي الثانية التي تليها مثل ذلك، ويقف عندها داعيا، ثم يرمي جمرة العقبة راكبا، ولا يقف عندها.
The Book of Hajj: How to arrange the actions of Hajj: He performs tawaf of the House, the tawaf of visitation, seven circuits, and women become permissible for him. The best of these days is the first of them. If he delays it beyond them, a sheep becomes incumbent on him due to delaying a wajib. Then he returns to Mina and stays there. When the sun has passed its zenith on the second day of the days of sacrifice, he pelts the three jamarat. He begins with the jamrah that is closest to the Mosque of al-Khayf, pelting it with seven pebbles while walking, saying takbir with each pebble. Then he stands near it supplicating as he wishes, praising Allah Almighty, sending blessings on the Prophet, raising his hands in supplication, asking forgiveness for his parents and believing brothers. Then he pelts the second jamrah that follows it similarly, and stands near it supplicating. Then he pelts Jamrat al-Aqabah while riding, and does not stand near it.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This is a ruling statement describing the order of actions in Hajj after the sacrifice days begin. The pilgrim first performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah, also known as Tawaf al-Ifadah, which is a wajib act. After this tawaf, marital relations become permissible. The best time for this tawaf is the first day of sacrifice (10th Dhul Hijjah). If delayed beyond the days of sacrifice, a sheep (damm) becomes wajib as compensation. Then the pilgrim returns to Mina to stay there. On the second day of Tashreeq (11th Dhul Hijjah), after zawal (sun past zenith), he pelts the three jamarat in order: first the small jamrah near Masjid al-Khayf, then the middle jamrah, both while walking and supplicating. The third is Jamrat al-Aqabah, pelted while riding with no supplication afterwards.

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The tawaf performed after returning from Mina on the day of sacrifice; also called tawaf al-ifadah.
الجمرات (al-jamarat): The three stone pillars at Mina representing the devil; they are pelted with pebbles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consequence if Tawaf al-Ziyarah is delayed beyond the days of sacrifice?
A) The tawaf becomes invalid and must be repeated
B) A sheep (dam) becomes incumbent
C) No consequence; it is still valid without penalty
D) The pilgrim must perform a second tawaf

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is wajib with a specific time window, and ramy on the second day follows a prescribed order: walking and supplicating for the first two jamarat, riding without supplication for the third.

Ramy on the 3rd Day and Hastening (Ta'jil)
Explains ramy on 3rd day and hastening options.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for the third day of Tashreeq and identify when hastening is permissible and its consequences.

Core Idea
Hastening from Mina on the 3rd day is permissible before sunset; staying until sunset is makruh but no penalty.

This passage from Nur al-Idah outlines the obligations and options on the third day of Tashreeq (12th Dhul Hijjah). It details the wajib pelting of all three jamarat after zawal, the option to hasten departure before sunset, and the varying rulings if one delays beyond certain thresholds.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary obligation
On the third day, the pilgrim must pelt all three jamarat after zawal. This is wajib.
2
Understand the hastening option
If the pilgrim wishes to hasten (ta'jil) and leave Mina on the same day, he must depart before sunset.
3
Know the ruling if staying until sunset
If he stays until sunset, it is makruh tanzihi, and no penalty (dam) is due.
4
Recognize the trigger for an additional day
If dawn of the fourth day (13th) breaks while he is still in Mina, pelting becomes wajib for that day as well.
5
Note the timing for the additional day's pelting
Pelting on the fourth day is permissible before zawal but better after zawal, and makruh before sunrise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا كان اليوم الثالث من أيام النحر رمي الجمار الثلاث بعد الزوال كذلك، وإذا أراد أن يتعجل نفر إلى مكة قبل غروب الشمس، وإن أقام إلى الغروب كره، وليس عليه شيء، وإن طلع الفجر - وهو بمنى - في الرابع لزمه الرمي، وجاز قبل الزوال، والأفضل بعده، وكره قبل طلوع الشمس، وكل رمي بعده رمي، ترميه ماشيا؛
Then when it is the third day of the days of sacrifice, he pelts the three jamarat after zawal similarly. And if he wishes to hasten, he departs to Mecca before sunset. If he stays until sunset, it is makruh, and nothing is due on him. If dawn breaks while he is at Mina on the fourth day, pelting becomes incumbent on him, and it is permissible before zawal, but better after it, and makruh before sunrise. Every pelting after which there is no pelting, he pelts it walking.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling for the third day of Tashreeq (12th Dhul Hijjah). The pilgrim must pelt all three jamarat after zawal. If he wants to hasten (ta'jil) and leave Mina on the same day, he must depart before sunset. Staying until sunset is makruh tanzihi but no penalty. If he stays until the dawn of the fourth day (13th Dhul Hijjah), then pelting becomes wajib on him (the additional third day ramy). That ramy can be performed before zawal (though after zawal is better). Pelting before sunrise is makruh. The phrase 'كل رمي بعده رمي' means that for any pelting after which there is another pelting (i.e., the first two jamarat on days when there is a subsequent jamarah), one should walk. For the last pelt (Jamrat al-Aqabah on the 10th or the final pelt on the third day), where no pelt follows, one may ride.

Key Terms
التعجيل (al-ta'jil): Hastening departure from Mina on the 3rd day of Tashreeq before sunset.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a pilgrim stays at Mina until sunset on the 3rd day of Tashreeq?
A) He must sacrifice a sheep
B) It is makruh but no penalty
C) It is impermissible
D) He must still pelt that day

Key Takeaway
On the third day, pelting is wajib; hastening is valid only before sunset; staying until sunset is makruh but no penalty; staying until dawn of the fourth day makes pelting wajib again.
